This world is sinking.
It is being swallowed up by the rising seas.
Humanity has less and to live on, and the technological advances they have made are being lost.
I remember a time when they seemed content to peacefully accept their extinction.
It was then that I met him.
He said that if he couldn’t save the world, he wouldn’t be saved.
I asked him a question.
Does the world include me?
I will look over this planet.
I will watch it sink.
And I will watch them, as they fight back against their fate.
Here, in this infinite loneliness.
Time is a cruel thief to rob us of our former selves. We lose as much to life as we do to death…
I am surrounded by endless darkness.
Not a single ray of light illuminates my path as I craw I through the gloom, praying for an exit that may not even exist.
But as hard as I try, I cannot move.
My leg is crushed beneath a dreadful weight, completely trapped.
Searing agony radiates through my body.
Please, Mom, someone…Help!
My hands scrabble around in the dirt, reaching out for anyone, anything. But they find nothing.
It hurts…It hurts…!
Natsuki: Somebody, save me!
I awaken suddenly to the sight of my hand, stretched out toward the low ceiling of my room.
Grasping at nothing, I let my arm drop down by my side.
And then I feel it.
Natsuki: Nnngh!?
My body twists and contorts as an intense pain throbs in my right leg.
Natsuki: Hngh…Hahh,hahh…Ugh…
After a few torturous seconds, it disappears as if it was never there in the first place.
I lay limply back on the bed, trying to slow my breathing.
My body is coated in a clammy layer of sweat.
Natsuki: …I must have fallen asleep.
I raise my head, and look down at my leg.
Or at least, where it should be.
The very same right leg that just a moment ago was pulsing with agony is as non-existent as it has been for the past eight years.
And yet, it still hurts. The empty space where my flesh should be still torments me.
There are no nerves there to send signals to my brain, but my mind still will not accept the truth.
They call it “phantom pain.”
It’s started to flare up again lately.
Phantom pain isn’t affected by regular pain killers.
I mean, of course it isn’t. It’s all an illusion, pain emanating from nerves that don’t even exist.
A doctor would prescribe antidepressants, but their side-effects could be even worse than the pain. Not that a doctor would be able to get their hands on those these days.
I simply have to live in constant dread of the next attack.
The gentles sunlight leaking through the portholes stabs at my eyes. It must be morning.
Natsuki: …No point lying around here, I suppose.
I hear a sudden, satisfying crunch from somewhere across the room.
Woman’s Voice: You awake? Didn’t look like you were having a nice time in dreamland there.
I look over to find a young woman, chopping pieces off of an apple with a penknife.
Catherine: Damn, you’ve got a resting bitch face at the best of times, but it sure is bad when you’ve just woken up. You could make a kid cry if you looked at them like that.
Natsuki: …Really nice to hear that from a woman who sneaks into someone else’s room and steals their breakfast.
Lifting myself up from the sweat-streaked sheets, I sit on the edge of my bed and reach for my prosthetic leg.
Naturally, a prosthetic leg is supposed to be built to fit an individual’s body.
But this one wasn’t made specifically for me. It’s an old, second-hand model, not just ill-fitting, but on the verge of breaking too.
It’s better than nothing, though.
These days, it’s possible to get cybernetic legs that can be controlled by nerve signals, or even full cybernetic implants.
Unfortunately, those are far, far out of my price range right now.
I place my stump into the socket, and tighten the straps around it.
When I try moving the joint, it lets out an ominous creak.
I fiddle with its screws, and give it a little oil.
Newsreader: The weather out there this morning is looking bright and clear, with a mild south-westerly breeze…
The radio I’d switched on before I laid down is still blaring.
I got through the motions of keeping my decrepit old leg working while half-listening to the drone of the announcer’s voice.
Newsreader: …The rocket has been hailed by some as representing a bold new hope for humanity, but citizens have been raising concerns that…
Catherine: I hope they actually launch this one.
Natsuki: They will.
Catherine: Well, here’s hoping. If they’ve got the time to mess about launching fireworks, maybe they could actually help the people with their problems too, huh?
Natsuki: They’ve got the bigger picture in mind. If they don’t work to assure we’ve got a future, what’s the point in fixing whatever bullshit the common person’s got going on?
Natsuki: …Ugh, there’s no point trying to get philosophical with you, I know.
I push my foot down, getting a feel for the leg.
The joint’s moving a little more smoothly now.
Catherine: Nice weather we’ve got today. Perfect for diving. What to get started?
Natsuki: At least let me have breakfast first.
It’s only when I’ve finished my sentence that I remember that my apple’s already long gone.
Someone’s Voice: H-Hello?
Another female voice calls out, this time from off my ship.
Minamo: Natsu-kuuun?
Minamo: Hmm, maybe
Minamo: Hmm, maybe he’s asleep. I wish he’d put a doorbell on this thing.
Catherine: Hey.
Minamo: Oh,Natsu-ku-
Minamo: Wait, who are you!?
Catherine: That’s my line.
Minamo: Err, well… I’m Kamishiro Minamo, I’m a friend of Natsu-kun’s.
Catherine: Huh, that kid’s got friends?
Minamo: Ahem, so could I ask who you are?
Catherine: Me? Well, y’know. I guess I’m like his wife.
Minamo: Wife? His W-I-F-E wife!?
Natsuki: Don’t listen to her. She’s just your average apple-pinching intruder.
Minamo: Err… So who actually are you?
Catherine: I’m his business partner.
Natsuki: Why are you here, Minamo?
Minamo: I’ve come to take you to school, Natsu-kun.
Minamo: You haven’t turned up at all ever since you transferred here…
Before I can say anything, Catherine has already opened her big mouth.
Catherine: Unfortunately, my little partner here’s got a job to do, a job that’s going to make us both very, very rich. So you just run a long to school now, sweetie.
Minamo: Eep!
Minamo flinches and almost tears up as a slght glare is flashed her way.
Natsuki: If you’re not doing anything else, you could help us out. An extra pair of hands would be useful.
Minamo: I just said that I’m going to school, though?
Natsuki: What’s the point in that? School makes you dumb.
Minamo: Err… I thought it was supposed to make you smarter?
Minamo: Hey, wait! Natsu-kuuun!
The ship rumbles its way away from the pier, and stops a little distance from the shore.
Natsuki: This seems like the place.
Deep in the translucent waters, I can see the shadow of something man-made.
Minamo: Aww, man, I ended up coming along anyway. I should be at school…
Minamo grumbles to herself as she stares out at the endless expanse of blue.
I climb down from the deck, toward the other vessel the ship is towing.
I open the hatch on the large, egg-like craft bobbing up and down in the waves.
Natsuki: Minamo, when I close the hatch, disengage the clamps. You know how to do that, right?
Minamo: O-Of course I don’t!
Catherine: I’ll teach you. Come over here.
Minamo: Eep!
Natsuki: I’ll need you to operate the crane too. If you’ve got any questions, ask Catherine.
Minamo: I-Is this thing even seaworthy? It’s got rust all over it.
Natsuki: I’m not going to be diving too deep. A little bit of leakage isn’t anything to worry about.
Minamo: Seriously? Won’t it sink?
Natsuki: Right, here goes.
I duck down inside the sub, and close the hatch behind me.
I take my seat at the controls and pump the choke lever until hear the engine splutter into life.
I tap all of the gauges to check they’re working, and signal to Minamo out of the small window in the top the sub.
Natsuki: Okay, disengage the clamps.
Minamo: …
Minamo flaps her arms back at me with a troubled espression.
Natsuki: Sorry, I can’t hear a word you’re saying.
I can’t hear her though the glass, and her arm movements don’t communicate anything except possibly “frightened goose.”
Better signal to Catherine instead.
Grinning like a demon plunging a sinner into the depths of hell, she disengages the lock.
I feel the sub sway as it floats freely in the water.
I call out through the radio.
Natsuki: Okay, lower the crane.
Catherine: Roger.
I tug on the control stick and the sub’s manipulator arms grasp the crane’s hook. I attach it to the eyelet on top of the egg.
Natsuki: Venting the ballast tanks.
The sea around the sub ripples with bubbles as the tanks empty out their air and replace it with water.
The rotund little ship starts to gradually submerge as it grows heavy with ballast.
The color outside the window darkness from the baby blue of the sky to the deep aqua of the sea.
The submarine. Serpens Albus slowly sinks into the water, glistening in the morning sun.
The little ship slowly and silently drifts through the sea.
It sinks deeper and deeper.
Before long, the rusty joints of its hull start to creak under the pressure.
Natsuki: You’re already hurting at this depth? Hmm, this might be a problem after all.
Minamo’s doubts seem to be contagious.
The Serpens Albus is s pretty old ship. It’s supposed to be capable of going a few hundred meters down, but I can’t help but feel that if I tried going that deep now I’d end up the size of a basketball.
Thankfully, I’m not heading down anywhere that deep. It’ll be a couple of dozen meters at most.
The light outside grows dimmer, and soon all that I can see beyond the window is a dark navy.
I cruise through the lonely waters, toward the treasure I seek.
I came to this town because I had nothing left. I’d lost everything.
I lived here once as a child, left in the care of my grandmother.
But when I returned after eight years, the scenery was unrecognizable.
The beautiful coastal town I remembered was gone.
Natsuki: There is…
Sunken beneath the waves.
Buried here at the bottom of the ocean is a town that just a few years ago was teeming with people.
The sight of the buildings shimmering in the sunlight piercing the water is uncanny. It’s like time has stopped.
This town was not the only one to be enveloped by the sea.
When the waters around the world suddenly began to rise, entire cities were plunged into this limbo.
No one knows why. Scientists posited that it might be climate change, or some kind of movement in the earth’s crust, but no one can say for sure.
All we really know is that sea levels suddenly began to rise inexorably, swallowing up more and more land.
The mysterious phenomenon brought humanity to its knees, almost entirely destroying our civilization. They say we’ve entered the twilight of our species, and it’s hard to disagree.
The population had already started to drop before I was born, and by the time I became aware of the world, it was already doomed.
Even though I lived through the terror of the great sea rise, I don’t really have any conception of the supposed “time of the party” that adults talk about.
Natsuki: They’re always droning on about the past and other bullshit. But this is the only world I’ve ever known.
Something inside me makes me want to blame the state of this planet on them.
As I sit there lost in my thoughts, a transmission comes through my radio.
Catherine: How’s it going, kid?
Natsuki: Great. I’ll be arriving at the target soon.
…
After a moment’s lag, the reply comes.
Catherine: Nice. Let’s get what we need, and then I can get the hell out of this hole.
The lag’s a necessary annoyance, given that radio waves don’t pass through water too easily. All of our communications are converted into high-frequency sound waves, which travel slower.
Natsuki: If you want to get out of here so much, why not find some other job? You don’t want to die a debt collector, do you?
Catherine: When I’m done with this case, I’ll consider it.
Just as I’m about to get back to work, another voice comes over the radio.
Minamo: Natsu-kun!
Natsuki: What’s wrong? You sound like you’re about to burst into tears.
Minamo: Are you okay? Is this ship still all right? You’re not sinking are you?
Natsuki: It’s fine. Little bit creaky, but nothing worth worrying about.
Natsuki: It looks pretty nice down here. I should show you sometime.
This kind of scenery could takes someone’s breath away, that’s for sure.
Minamo: Come back as quick as you can, okay?
Natsuki: I’m telling you, it’s fine. This thing might be old, but that means it’s tough and simple too.
Minamo: That’s not what I mean. We’ll be late for school!
Oh, yeah, that.
Minamo: If my mom finds out I’m skipping school, she’d be furious.
I sigh.
Natsuki: You really are a good girl, aren’t you?
Minamo: H-Huh!? D-Don’t start complimenting me all of a sudden…
Giggling with a strangely elated tone, she ends the transmission.
Natsuki: What the hell was that…?
Gah, that completely broke my concentration.
My grandmother was an ocean geologist. She left me a lot in her will.
Although her home was flooded, her boat and this submarine, that she used for field work, weren’t taken by the waters.
She was obsessed with her research, and despised children.
Before she died, she poured a significant a mount of her saving into something that she locked up in her storehouse.
And that’s what I’m here to salvage.
Natsuki: There it is-her house.
For a short time, I suppose it was mine too.
I grasp the controls, and steer the sub into the back garden.
There, just as I remember, is the storehouse. It’s quite big, almost out of keeping with the size of the actual house.
My grandmother never let me get close to it. Perhaps she was keeping materials related to her research in there.
Now, however, it’s the only place I’m interested in. Getting in might be difficult, though-the storehouse’s heavy iron doors look to be locked tight.
Natsuki: We’re going to have to break the doors down. When I give you the signal, wind in the winch.
Catherine: Roger.
I reach the manipulator arm up to undo the crane’s hook, and attach it to the bar holding the two doors solidly closed.
Natsuki: Okey, pull!
The cable winds back swiftly and snaps taut, but the doors don’t move an rich.
Natsuki: Huh. No dice.
Just as I’m about to give the signa l to stop, a clang and the sound of creaking metal echo through the water. The door collapses, sending up a billowing cloud of sediment.
The resulting opening is large enough for the Serpens Albus to fit straight through.
Natsuki: Well, looks like that’ll do.
If I hadn’t been able to get these doors open, I would have had to break through the roof, and that could have damaged whatever’s inside.
Natsuki: It’s been ten years… Finally time to see what’s in here.
I orient the sub towards the door, and slowly start to push forward.
The inside of the storehouse is in far better condition than the outside.
The walls are lined with bookshelves full of research materials, and measurement buoys and data collection equipment are scattered all over the floor.
As a kid, this place would have made the perfect playground. I can picture my grandmother thinking about all the fun children could get up to in here, and scowling as she locked the doors.
Natsuki: Probably a wise decision, to be fair.
I shine the subs lights across the room, searching out my target.
The fact that I don’t actually know what I’m looking for makes that easier said than done, however. It’s supposed to be something valuable, but to my untrained eyes, all of the devices in here look like they cost a pretty penny.
Crabs and fish skitter around the assorted detritus, fleeing from the torch beams.
Natsuki: …Hmm?
I notice an odd object as I sweep the lights around.
Natsuki: What’s that?
It’s a large, oblong box. Down here in the murky gloom, it almost looks a sunken sarcophagus.
Slowing down my engine so that my screw drives don’t kick up too much sediment, I cautiously approach.
…
It really does seem to be some kind of casket.
It’s the perfect size for a single person.
Part of the surface seems to be glass. I peer through the gloom…
Natsuki: A mannequin? No… A girl?
Inside the capsule is a young girl, as delicate and fragile-looking as an antique doll.
Strangely, I don’t feel even an inkling of fear or discomfort.
Maybe it’s because this seems so unreal. Or perhaps it’s just how adorable she looks.
Whatever the case, I have no idea what she really is.
There’s only one thing I’m sure about-this has to be what I’m here for.
Natsuki: What even is this? It looks like it has electricity, but that’s all can really tell from looking at it…
I’m going to have to raise the whole thing.
I’m not going to be able to manage that with just the manipulator arm. I’ll have to rely on the crane.
I steer the sub back out of the building, and pull the wire out from the remains of the door.
Dragging it along behind me, I make my way back to the casket.
As I approach it, my hand slips from the control stick, and the sub nudges the case.
It’s not a hard hit, but for a moment a chill runs down my spine.
Natsuki: …I haven’t broken it, have I?
It doesn’t seem like the glass is cracked…
But the eyes of the girl in the casket have opened.
Our gaze meets through the glass.
Girl: …
Natsuki: She’s alive…
I know my voice can’t be reaching her, but she tilts her head slightly as if in response.
Suddenly, like a bolt of lightning, a name pops into my mind.
I’d heard it once in the hospital, at my grandmother’s bedside…
Natsuki: ATRI…?
The girl watches the movement of my lips carefully.
Girl: …
And she smiles.
She really is alive…
Natsuki: (But… What is she?)
As I sit wondering what to do next, the girl starts to move. She begins to tap away at some panels inside her capsule.
The glass of the case opens.
A great cloud of bubbles billows out as the casket is inundated with water.
Natsuki: What are you doing!?
Girl: …
It seems like she didn’t realize that she was underwater.
As much as she panics and tries to hammer the controls, there’s no closing the glass now.
I’ve got to save her-
At that moment, a shadow looms over me.
The sudden rush of air from the casket buffets the ceiling of the building, the already water-damaged framework seemingly rattled by my destruction of the doors.
The walls start to cave in, and the concrete ceiling cracks.
Natsuki: No!
I instinctively push the control stick forward.
The Serpens Albus moans in agony as steel beams collapse on top of it.
Thankfully, I’ve managed to cover the girl from harm.
But we’re not out of the woods yet.
Natsuki: Hngh, this is bad… Am I trapped!?
I try to put my engine into reverse, but the sub is pinned down under the ceiling.
My mind is instantly filled with intense, gruesome memories…
Natsuki: (I’m buried alive, just like before…)
My body is quickly coated in an ice-cold sweat, and pain throbs through the spot where my leg should be.
Natsuki: Nnngh… Hahh, hahh… Hahh…
As the weight above me seems to bear down on my very soul, my eyes meet the girl’s.
Girl: …
She stares at me with a strange look, as if she doesn’t realize the danger that she’s in.
Natsuki: I’ve got… I’ve got to save her…
Grasping the controls, I try to find the hook of the crane to affix it to the sub, but it’s now here to be found.
Natsuki: …Did it come off in the impact?
I try to peer around the floor, but my manipulator arms couldn’t reach down there even if I did see it, and the sub can’t move an inch.
Natsuki: What do I do? Nnngh!
Pain and panic surges through my brain, and I feel my consciousness grow distant.
Just as I’m about to black out, I see the girl jump from the casket. She reaches down, and lifts up a glimmering silver object-the hook.
Girl: …?
Natsuki: Please… Give that to me…
She tilts her head to the side and stares. She places the hook in the fingers of my manipulator.
I quickly attach it to the sub’s frame.
Natsuki: Hey… Can you hear me up there!?
Catherine: Wassup?
Natsuki: Hahh, hahh… Wind in the winch! Quick!
Catherine: What was that? Speak up, Kid.
Minamo: What’s going on? Is something wrong, Natsu-kun?
Natsuki: Wind in the winch! Now!
Catherine: Wait a second, if we do that-
If they don’t do it this instant, I’m going to end up completely crushed.
Minamo: O-Okay! Oof!
Catherine: What are you doing, you stupid girl!?
I grab the girl from the casket in the manipulator arm.
Girl: …
She stare impassively at me through the window, unfazed by the metal gripper around her waist.
Natsuki: (Isn’t she scared?)
If anything, she looks particular relaxed.
Why isn’t she struggling for breath by now?
I’m thrown from my seat from the sudden acceleration as the winch pulls taut, the sub creaking painfully as the ceiling pinning it down scrapes against it.
Catherine: Phew… I thought we were going to capsize. Jeez, this girl…
Minamo: Ah, there he is!
Catherine: Huh. Sure looks like he’s in a hurry.
Catherine: That must mean we’ve hit the jackpot!
When the hull breaks the water, I fling open the hatch.
Crawling out, I heard toward the ship’s fore.
Minamo: What are you doing, Natsu-kun! That’s dangerous!
Catherine: Hey, you’re gonna fall in! You can’t swim with that leg, can you?
Natsuki: If I don’t hurry, the girl’s going to die!
Minamo: What girl?
Minamo: suddenly notices the body held between the manipulator’s claws.
Minamo: Who is that!?
The girl is floating face-down, unmoving, her body limp.
I craw I towards her, and thrust out my hand.
Natsuki: Grab hold! Quickly!
She doesn’t move. Maybe she’s unconscious…
I push myself off of the sub’s hull, trying to make my way over to her.
But as my foot drives against the rusty metal, I feel it shudder beneath me.
Natsuki: What!?
My leg catches against the framework-my prosthetic leg, which tears away from my body.
I fall into the water, and sink beneath the surface. Stunned, I gaze up at the soft morning light glimmering through the azure.
Natsuki: (It’s beautiful…)
Perhaps it’s because I instantly realize the hopelessness of my plight, but I’m surprising calm.
My clothes are heavy with water. My one leg doesn’t even attempt to keep me afloat.
Opening myself to the soft embrace of the cool, radiant light, I let myself be taken by the depths.
Natsuki: (So this is how I die… At least I’m going to die somewhere beautiful.)
I’d rather my last breath fill my lungs with water than darkness.
As I gaze in wonder at the shimmering light, like a million jewels enveloping my body, a shadow starts to form within them.
It grows and grows, blocking all that beauty from my view.
Natsuki: (Stop it… Don’t take the light away… The darkness scares me…!)
Natsuki: (Mmmph!?)
The shadow bears down on me, and I feel a strange sensation against my lips.
I see clearly now. The shadow is the girl.
Natsuki: (What is she doing…?)
She’s sinking with me, pushing air into my mouth from her own.
Girl: (…)
As I feel her gift of oxygen fill my lungs, a terrible thought begins to float through my mind.
Natsuki: (I don’t want to die…)
I came to this town because I had lost everything.
I thought I had no reason to live any more.
And yet, I do not want to die.
What a selfish, greedy creature a human can be, to want to live on without reason.
But now, there’s no way back.
Natsuki: (I’m sorry. I dragged you into this…)
If she hadn’t tried to save me, she could have lived on.
But even with her breath sustaining me, my one remaining leg can do nothing to keep us from falling the darkness.
Girl: (…)
A plume of bubbles erupts from her mouth as she tried to say something.
Girl: (…!)
Not wishing to waste more air, she quickly presses her mouth back to mine, and points upward.
Natsuki: (Huh…?)
Through the shining water comes a shape.
A thin, long line, connecting us to the light.
A rope.
I grasp hold of it, and wrap my other arm around the girl.
Natsuki: Hahh, hahh…
I collapse on the ship’s deck, basking in the sheer joy of breathing freely once more.
Minamo: Ahh, that was so scary! I thought you were going to die, Natsu-kun!
Natsuki: Hahh, hahh… Thanks for the help, Minamo.
Minamo: No…*sniffle*, that wasn’t me.
Catherine: Couldn’t let my meal ticket get away, now could I?
She holds up the rope with a grin.
I don’t have the energy to snap at her like I normally would. For once, I’m grateful for her debt collector instincts.
Catherine: So, I suppose I should ask… Who’s the girl?
She’s sitting next to me, soaking wet, seeming unfazed.
She’s still holding the sleeve of my shirt in her hand.
Her grip is firm, as if she’s trying to stop me jumping into the sea again.
Girl: …
Natsuki: …Thanking you.
Girl: There is no need to thank me. I was merely carrying out my innate duty.
Natsuki: (What a strange phrasing…)
Minamo: Where did she come from? She wasn’t with you when you dived, was she?
Natsuki: I found her down there. She was sleeping in my grandmother’s storehouse.
Minamo: What? Sleeping?
Natsuki: I think she might be a robot.
Girl: That is s common colloquial term for the category of equipment I belong to. However, it is imprecise.
She’s not human…
She’s just a robot in the shape of a human.
Catherine: She must be a Humanoid! Your grandmother was keeping a thing like this down there all this time?
Humanoids: robots intended to resemble humans as much as possible.
Also marketed as ”Androids” or ”Gynoids” depending on the manufacturer.
Humanoids were produced en masse when humanity’s technological progress was at its peak, and their construction was so advanced that they were indistinguishable from humans.
They don’t need to breathe, but their vocal systems are intended to replicate the human voicebox. Naturally, that means they need a pair of lungs, or at least something resembling them, to hold air.
I own my life to that particular design quirk.
Minamo: She’s a robot? Wow, I couldn’t tell at all!
Robot Girl: Of course not. I am an extremely high-performance model.
Catherine: Phew, we really have struck the jackpot! This thing will sell for a pretty penny.♪
Minamo: What!? You’re going to sell her?
Catherine: Of course. Selling it’s the reason we salvaged it.
Catherine: Humanoids are pretty thin on the ground these days. If we sell it, he’ll be able to pay off Professor Yachigusa’s debts, and then some.
Minamo: But, um, isn’t that kind of cruel? It’s like, umm…
Minamo looks back and forth between Catherine and the robot girl.
Somehow I don’t think she’d have the same kind of reaction if she was looking at any other piece of industrial machinery.
But to the untrained eye, this girl looks just like a human being.
Robot Girl: Yes. That is not possible.
Minamo: See, she thinks so tool!
Robot Girl: I am the private property of my master. It is against the law to sell me without permission.
Catherine: Your master? Ah, Professor Yachigusa…
Natsuki: Your master died a month ago.
Robot Girl: Oh.
Natsuki: This town sunk into the rising seas three years ago. You’ve been asleep down there for all that time.
The robot counts to there on her fingers.
A look of realization dawns on her face.
Robot Girl: Ohhh. So my master is dead. I see. R.I.P.
Minamo: She, err, doesn’t seem very upset.
Catherine: Well, it’s a robot. Saying that, even this level of emotion marks it out as a pretty expressive model.
Catherine: Don’t you worry, though, your new master’s right here! This kid here got all of the professor’s stuff her will.
Robot Girl: …
The robot girl turns to me, and peers closely at my face.
Robot Girl: I see. So you’re…
Natsuki: Err, yeah, I suppose I’m your master now.
Robot Girl: For some reason, I felt like that was the case from the very first time I saw you, under the water. I should have known.
She speaks with a strange air of conviction.
She tugs on my sleeve again.
Natsuki: (She looks like a kid who’s just found her dad…)
I wonder if a sufficiently advance robot without a master experience the same fears a lost child would…
Robot Girl: What should I call you? I will adjust my speech protocols accordingly.
Robot Girl: Popular options include ‘master’, ‘sir’, ‘big bro’, ‘daddy’-
Natsuki: Just call me Natsuki.
I abruptly cut her off, before she says something I really don’t want to have in my head.
Natsuki: Ikaruga Natsuki. That’s my name.
Robot Girl: Natsuki.
Natsuki: And what do I call you?
Robot: Girl: Would you like to confirm my serial number?
She reaches behind her head to lift up her hair. Her serial number must be on the back of her neck.
Natsuki: No, I’m asking if you have a name.
I wouldn’t be surprised if that old bag never gave her one.
Robot Girl: My name is ‘ATRI’.
ATRI: My master gave me it.
Natsuki: ATRI… That’s a nice name.
The words slip out of my mouth without thinking.
ATRI: I know, right? Being given a human name is proof of being recognized as a living being.
ATRI: It’s a marker of status.♪
Robot think of names in that way? I’d never considered that before.
ATRI: Ah, Natsuki is a pretty nice name too, I suppose.
Natsuki: …Are you patronizing me?
ATRI: Error. I do not understand the word ‘patronizing’.
She looks up at me with a blank expression.
It’s probably my imagination, but there seems to be a glint of mischief in her young, delicate eyes. Then again, maybe it’s just a reflection of the midday sun…
I think back to the lights that I saw underwater.
After staring at me for a while, ATRI suddenly smiles.
It’s a smiles so soft and gentle that I have the sudden wish to capture this moment in amber for eternity.
ATRI: Take good care of me, Natsuki-san.
I remember the first thing my grandmother said to me when I walked into her hospital room, propped up by a walking stick, dragging my ill-fitting prosthetic leg.
Nonko: You look a mess…
That’s all.
Natsuki: If I hadn’t sold my cybernetic leg, I wouldn’t have been able to pay my tuition fees.
Nonko: And yet, you’ve ended up crawling back here anyway. Who does that remind me of? Well, I guess it’s my fault, in the end…
I didn’t expect those words to hit me hard, but they did.
To hear this selfish woman say that something was her fault came straight out of the blue.
Nonko: I’m glad you’ve returned, though. I want you to carry on my research, Natsuki.
Nonko: I lost a lot when the seas rose, but my work isn’t finished yet.
Nonko: I want you to pull up ATRI. If you can take her where she needs to go, our plan can start again…
Natsuki: ATRI…
Nonko: My clumsy, useless housekeeper.
I was surprised to hear someone as cantankerous as her would employ a maid.
Natsuki: I don’t really know what you want me to do, but I can tell it’s not something I can manage. I am a mess, after all.
Nonko: Pssh, you’re going to let a little thing like losing your leg beat you? You’re not dead yet, boy. Don’t you want to save the world?
Nonko: That island is still out there somewhere on the ocean. You have to find it, Natsuki…
When we reach the pier, Minamo hurriedly hops off the boat.
Minamo: Gah, I’m really, really curious about her, but I’ve got to get to school!
Minamo: Make sure you come to school tomorrow too, Natsuki-kun. There’s something I want to talk to you about.
She runs off without waiting for a reply.
Minamo: Dammit, I’m so late!
ATRI: School…
Catherine: Right, we should get going too.
Natsuki: Where to?
Catherine: Town. We’ve gotta sell this thing, of course.
Catherine: Dunno where yet, but I want to get a few quotes at least.
She hops down from the ship too.
I’m about to jump down myself, when I feel ATRI staring up at me with a strange expression. She’s been cling to my sleeve this whole time.
ATRI: Do you need some help?
Natsuki: Nope, I’ve got this.
I jump down from the swaying deck.
I brace myself with my walking stick as I land, wobbling.
Easy. I could manage that in my sleep.
ATRI follows after me, hurried trotting up to me and grabbing onto my sleeve again.
Natsuki: Let’s go.
ATRI: Affirmative.
We travel all the way into the center of town.
Long ago, the shopping street here was extremely lively.
As times changed it became nearly abandoned, but the economic shock caused by the great sea rise led to it becoming a thriving hub of trade once again.
Now, it’s a chaotic, bustling place, a black market full of stalls and vendors.
Catherine: Ahh, don’t you just love it here? Dirty, grimy, and filled with the absolute scum of the world. The perfect place for someone like me to blend in.
Despite her assertion, this is still only a small town. So outsiders stick out like a sore thumb, Catherine and I included.
Thanks to my hobbling gait, I can usually feel the stares on me wherever I go.
There’s something different today, though. For once, all of the eyes are on the person walking behind me.
Her footsteps, light and pottering, have no trouble keeping up with my slow walk.
The sound of bare feet on concrete is noticeably strange.
Catherine: …Hey, can’t you do something about that noise?
Catherine turns with a sigh and a frown.
ATRI merely stares, still holding on to the hem of my sleeve.
I can’t recall if her feet where always bare, or if she just lost her shoes when we were underwater. I assume, since she’s wearing clothes otherwise, it’s the latter.
Natsuki: What am I supposed to do? I don’t exactly have a collection of small girls’ shoes I can just pull out my ass.
Catherine: Well, it’s gonna make a bad impression. You look like a slave trader or something.
Natsuki: You’re not helping that, you know.
Catherine looks completely out of place here in this country backwater.
I’m pretty sure “Catherine” isn’t even her real name. She’s very obviously completely Japanese, born and bred.
Even though I’ve been working with her, I don’t really know anything about her.
ATRI: May I ask a question? What is this place?
ATRI looks around the stalls.
Natsuki: You must know this place, right? You were my grandmother’s maid.
ATRI: I have no records of this place in my memory.
Natsuki: I suppose that’s understandable. All of the flatland around here was inundated when the waters rose, separating it from the mainland, so it must have changed a lot.
Once a coastal I town, now this is an island.
Suddenly being separated from civilization has caused a lot of problems. Transport, electricity and communications on the island have been disconnected.
Natsuki: This place wasn’t anywhere near as busy when I lived here. It used to be a ghost town, and so peaceful…
The road we took to get here has completely changed too.
It’s like the rising waters have washed away the old town in the same way even precious memories can be lost in a morass of fresh, pointless ones.
Natsuki: Don’t you feel hurt?
Some models of Humanoids are equipped with pain receptors, in order to make them as human-like as possible.
ATRI: I’m fine. I’m high-performance model, after all.
She shows me the bottom of her feet with a triumphant smile.
Her dress kicks up, and I glimpse her bare legs beneath it.
I know that they’re not made of real skin, that they’re not “real” legs, but their slim, gently curved silhouette looks so perfectly human.
I can’t take my eyes off of them.
ATRI: Is something wrong?
Natsuki: …It’s nothing.
I trudge my way through the crowds, propping myself up on my walking stick as I shuffle my creaking leg forward.
The store Catherine is aiming for is way off in the distance.
Natsuki: Hey, can we take a detour? There’s a place want to stop by.
Catherine: Can’t it wait?
Natsuki: I’ll only be a minute.
I turn off of the main road and onto a backstreet.
I stop in front of one particular stall.
Natsuki: So, which do you want?
ATRI: Hm?
ATRI tilts her head quizzically, still clenching my sleeve in her delicate fingers.
It’s a shoe store.
Natsuki: Take your pick. Only from the ones on this shelf, though.
A bunch of particularly cheap children’s shoes are all lined up.
They’re all can afford with how little money I have, so it’s lucky that they’re the perfect size.
ATRI: You’re going to buy these for me?
Natsuki: Yep.
Catherine: Ah, I get you. If it’s got dirty feet, people are gonna try and haggle the price down for it. Good thinking.
ATRI: Hmm…
ATRI looks over the shoes, humming as she does.
Catherine: Hurry up. Shoes are shoes. Just grab a pair.
ATRI: Please wait. There are several criteria for me consider, and I can’t choose so quickly.
ATRI: This pair is more robust, but these are the most aesthetically pleasing. And when you bring cost-performance into account…
Catherine: Tch, you’re an annoying little machine. Can’t you pick for her?
Natsuki: Err…
Taken by surprise, I reach out and pick up the first pair I see.
Natsuki: I think these would suit you best.
It’s a pair of brown loafers. Thankfully, cheap ones.
After I pay, the stall owner politely wipes ATRI’s feet, and she puts then on.
ATRI: Ohhh, they’re the perfect size.
Catherine: Great. Now, let’s go.
ATRI: Hehehe!♪
ATRI walks alongside me, deliberately kicking her feet up high with each step.
She seems pretty happy with her bottom-of-the-barrel footwear.
Natsuki: You really like those shoes that much?
Not that she seemed to mind being barefoot.
ATRI: I do! After all, you were the one that gave them to me!
Somehow, seeing her this happy about them makes me particular uncomfortable.
ATRI: Is it wrong for me to be happy?
Natsuki: No, it’s fine.
ATRI: I knew it. Good!
She exhales with a smile, oddly relieved.
Natsuki: (Is there some kind of rule about robot workers not being allowed to be happy, or something?)
I studied robotics at The Academy, but I don’t know much about the programming of models as old as ATRI.
We soon reach the store Catherine was aiming for.
It’s a junk shop, with all manner of electronics and machinery lying around in ugly heaps.
As I try to enter, I feel a tug at my sleeve.
I turn around. ATRI has stopped walking.
Natsuki: What’s up?
ATRI: Are you going to sell me?
Natsuki: Yep.
ATRI: Umm… I have a request.
ATRI: Could you wait for a little while?
I’m taken aback.
It’s unusual for a robot to make a request of a human.
There must be some particular reason for her to ask something like that.
Natsuki: How long is ‘a little while’ ?
ATRI: Hmm… Forty-five days. After that, I don’t mind.
Natsuki: Why do you want us to wait?
ATRI: umm…
Catherine: Not a chancel! Do you really think we’re just going to let you hang around for that long?
Before ATRI can respond, Catherine butts in.
Catherine: Come on, get in here!
She pulls ATRI by the hand into the store.
I follow along behind, brow furrowed.
The owner is visibly surprised to see ATRI.
Junk Shop Owner: Is that a Humanoid? I didn’t know there were any of those still running.
Catherine: This one’s a real doozy, too. A proper high-performance one, the kind that you can hardly even find in the big cities these days.
The owner eyes Catherine suspiciously.
Junk Shop Owner: You’re that new gal around here, aren’t ya?
Junk Shop Owner: Don’t wanna be rude, but you should get outta this town. This is a quite place, and wo don’t need your kind around here.
Catherine: Don’t you worry, as soon as I’m finished with my business, I’m out. So, how much?
Junk Shop Owner: What, you’re gonna sell this little one?
He glances ATRI up and down.
ATRI: …
Junk Shop Owner: There ain’t no way I’m gonna be able to buy her.
Catherine: Why not?
Junk Shop Owner: You think I’ve got that much cash lyin’ around? I’ve not even got anyone around here to sell her to. Is ’pose l could find you someone who’d be willin’ to take her off your hands, though.
Junk Shop Owner: Give us a look at your serial number, lass.
ATRI: …
She looks over at me as if requesting permission.
I nod, and she lifts up her hair.
There, on the nape of her neck, is the number.
The owner fetches a tattered, yellowing file from his desk, and starts flicking through the pages.
Junk Shop Owner: Hmm… A fourth generation Yamaseki Factories unit…
Junk Shop Owner: This model got recalled after they found a buncha bugs.
Natsuki: So you’re saying she’s not worth anything?
Catherine: That can’t be right! She’s a working, moving humanoid! Even one with a couple of little bugs here and there should be worth something!
She probably right. Most of the robot factories were destroyed by the sea rises, which lead to most companies going bankrupt and a lot of industry secrets being lost.
Their scarcity means ATRI could fetch dozens of times what my grandmother paid for her.
Junk Shop Owner: You got that right…
He starts tapping away at a calculator.
I watch his fingers dance. Tension growing in my chest.
My ship wasn’t the only thing I inherited from my grandmother. With it came a colossal debt.
Even if I worked constantly for years and years, I’d struggle to pay it off.
I found out about it when Catherine turned up at my door just after she died.
Catherine: So, this is the repossession order.
Natsuki: Yeah, and? It’s not like I can just go ‘here, take more money than I have in the world’ and wave you off.
She responds to my exasperation with a cool stare.
Catherine: Yeah, I know that. I didn’t expect you to just hand it over right away.
Catherine: I’m not leaving this town empty-handed, though. I’m a pro, you-know.
She leans in slightly toward me, as if to emphasize her breasts.
Catherine: Let’s work together. I’ve got a very, very interesting proposal for you.
Catherine: I want to salvage Professor Yachigusa’s belongings. I’ve heard that there’s something very valuable in the ruins of her storehouse, at the bottom of the ocean.
Catherine: We’ll raise that up, and split whatever profit we make selling it. Your debt will vanish, just like that, and I’ll make a little on the side too.
Catherine: How, about it, kid?
And so, the mysterious “Catherine” and I started working together.
I don’t know how Catherine knew there was something in the storehouse, but she came to me with a plan to use my grandmother’s submarine to salvage it.
It was, in a very real way, like a drowning man finding a lifeboat.
I have hardly any money at the best of times, and when I do, I’ve better things to spend it on than some old bag’s debts.
Like getting back the things I’ve lost…
Junk Shop Owner: Where did ya find the lass, if ya don’t mind me askin’?
The owner peers peer over at me suspiciously.
That’s understandable, I suppose. Two strangers turn up out of nowhere, with a Humanoid in tow, looking to sell? It’s natural to think they might have procured it through… atypical means.
Natsuki: She was in my grandmother’s storehouse. We salvaged her from the bottom of the ocean.
Junk Shop Owner: Is that true?
ATRI: Yes, absolutely. Natsuki-san pulled me up from the ocean just this morning.
Junk Shop Owner: Huh, gotcha. That’s gotta be nice for ya, right? Musta been mighty cold down there.
ATRI: I was asleep, so I don’t remember.
ATRI: So, do you think you’ll be able to sell me for a high price?
Junk Shop Owner: Hmm… Even though you’re a defective model, they should get about this much for ya.
He holds the calculator out toward us.
I can hardly parse the number on it. All can tell is that it would pay off my grandmother’s debts with plenty left over for me.
Catherine: Aww yeah! I’ve hit the jackpot, baby!
She victoriously thrusts her fists into the air.
All I can do is stand there, speech less.
ATRI: I see. A number befitting of a high-performance model like me. Very satisfying.
Even though we’re discussing selling her, she looks distinctly smug.
Natsuki: (She doesn’t mind being sold off? I suppose she is a robot…)
Junk Shop Owner: I’m sure l can find ya someone to buy her. I’ll be takin’, say, five percent for myself, natch.
Catherine: Tch… Well, I can live with that. How long do you think it’ll take?
Junk Shop Owner: I’m gonna have to go out to the big city for a deal like this… Gimme a month or so.
Catherine: I don’t want to be waiting around forever. You’ll try to find someone quick, right?
Junk Shop Owner: Of course! Ya ain’t the only one who’d appreciate a little cheddar right now.
Junk Shop Owner: So, which one of these two is your master?
ATRI: It’s Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: …
Junk Shop Owner: Ah, gotcha.
Junk Shop Owner: It’s you, then? Silly question, I know a Humanoid’s not gonna get their master wrong, heh.
Natsuki: Yeah, it’s me…
Not that it really feels that way, since we’ve only just met.
Junk Shop Owner: You’re gonna have to be with her when I sell her, right? Can’t sell a Humanoid without their master’s permission.
Natsuki: Understood.
Catherine: I’ll come along too. I don’t want you two running off with my hard-earned cash.
Catherine’s eyes are still sparkling.
Junk Shop Owner: Couldn’t help but notice, but that leg of yours is pretty retro, innit?
He nods downward.
He’s right. My leg’s so old and beat-up it could be something I found on one of these junk heaps on sale here.
Natsuki: Yeah, I know.
Junk Shop Owner: Lotta fancy cybernetics going cheap on the market these days. When ya get ya cash, give me a bell and I’ll get ya one, yeah?
He grins as he holds out a catalogue of expensive-looking cybernetic limbs.
Back in more prosperous times, even people with fully-able bodies would get cybernetic implants to improve their strength or make certain jobs easier.
It’s still pretty common among the rich nowadays.
The catalogue seems to be full of implants aimed at that market.
Natsuki: …I’ll think about it.
I mutter noncommittally, and I leave the store.
Catherine: Phew, let’s go and grab something to eat. I’ve had nothing all day but an apple.
My breakfast, you mean.
I’m even hungrier than her as a result.
Natsuki: Well, that worked out well for you, didn’t it?
ATRI: Huh?
Natsuki: He said it’d take at least a month.
Just like ATRI wanted, the sale’s going to be put off for quite some time.
ATRI: Oh yes, thank you.
Natsuki: But why did you want me to wait?
It’s almost unheard of for a robot to make demands or talk back to a human. They have to have a particularly pressing reason to do so.
ATRI: Before I fell asleep, my master gave an order. I would like to fulfill it before I am sold.
Natsuki: An order?
Robots have always been programmed to obey three laws.
One: A robot may not injure a human being or, though inaction, allow a human being to come to harm.
Two: A robot must obey the orders given it by human beings except where such orders would conflict with the First Law.
Three: A robot must protect its own existence as long as such protection does not conflict with the First or Second Laws.
For most Humanoids, their entire reason for existence is simply to obey those three laws.
ATRI: Would you like a better leg?
Natsuki: I sure would.
ATRI: In that case, for as long as we’re together, I’ll be your leg!
ATRI: It’s the least I can do. You gave me these lovely shoes, after all.♪
She looks proudly down at her feet.
ATRI: I’m sure I’ll make a much better leg than that one you’re using at the moment.
Natsuki: …I’ll pass, thanks.
ATRI: Why!? I’m much more high-performance than that thing!
Natsuki: I’m saying I don’t need you! I’m fine by myself!
Without realizing it, I start to raise my voice.
A real, human girl would probably cower in feat after being shouted at like that, but ATRI just looks confused, unsure of how to react.
Catherine: Snapping at a robot? Jeez, kid…
Natsuki: …Sorry.
Catherine: Right, I think it’d be best if I take care of this thing until the junk guy finds us a buyer. Come on, Let’s go.
Catherine grabs hold of ATRI’s hand.
ATRI: Umm, err…
ATRI looks over at me with a pleading gaze.

A satisfied Catherine trots off with ATRI trudging after her.
ATRI: …
She looks back at me with a melancholic gaze, but says nothing.
Robots are made to obey, after all. Especially if it’s an order from their master.
Natsuki: Don’t give me that look. What else can I do?
Watching them walk off, I start to hobble my own way down the road.
The skies grow dark as I sit boring a hole into the wall with my eyes.
Soft classical music lilts through the room from the radio.
The sound, however, is interrupted constantly by static.
The ship’s lights are flickering unsettlingly too.
The town itself has no electricity. The only power I have is the wind turbine. It’s small and barely able to keep the lights and the radio on, but it’s enough.
But on a still, windless night like this, I’m constantly plunged into darkness.
Natsuki: …
I can feel the night approaching.
A creeping dread like tendrils winding around my legs…
Natsuki: I suppose I’ll try to get some sleep.
I should get into bed while there’s still some light left.
But try as I might, sleep will not come. My stomach is so empty that the pangs of hunger rack my entire body.
Natsuki: I’ll be able to afford a new leg soon…
If I can just manage that, I can start to rebuild my life too.
…And I’m going to sell that girl to do that?
Salvage my grandmother’s inheritance, and sell it. That was the deal. That’s all.
Natsuki: Why should I feel guilty about something like that?
She might look like a human girl, but she’s just a robot.
She was even proud about fetching such a high price. This is fine, right?
ATRI: In that case, for as long as we’re together, I’ll be your leg!
ATRI: It’s the least I can do. You gave me these lovely shoes, after all.♪
Natsuki: Dammit…
I get out of bed, and walk haltingly out onto the deck.
What am I even doing?
Even if I leave the ship, I don’t know where to go.
I never felt the need to ask Catherine where she’s living.
Natsuki: This town isn’t exactly huge. There’s not many places for outsiders to stay, so if I look around…
Yeah, and then what?
I take ATRI back with me, assuage my guilt a little, and…?
Sell her in forty-five days? Really?
Natsuki: …
A wave swells up over the grasses that have become the coastline here, and washes over the tarmac.
This used to be a main road climbing a hill, looking down on the beaches far below.
Now, at high tide it’s swallowed by the sea itself.
Even relatively calm waves like this could pull me and my creaky old leg into the depths.
I can’t even press forward toward the town like this.
I can’t even manage this one, simple thing…
It’s time like these that I feel the emptiness beyond my stump the most acutely.
Frustration burns is my chest as the sun dips below the horizon.
As I stand there, unable to move forward or back, I see a figure approaching me.
Minamo: Hey! Natsu-kun!
Natsuki: Minamo…
Her home is just up the hill. What’s she doing out here?
Minamo: Look, there he is. Her came out to meet you.
ATRI: Natsuki-san…?
Behind Minamo cowers a timid-looking ATRI.
Minamo grabs her hand, and leads her over to me.
Natsuki: Why is she here?
Minamo: I met her when I went out to buy dinner ingredients for mom.
Minamo: It seems like she got lost and has been walking all around town looking for you.
Looking down, I see that her brand new shoes are already caked in mud.
Natsuki: I told you to go with Catherine…
She’s a robot. She can’t disobey my order like this.
ATRI: Yes, I went with her. I fulfilled your command as stated, and returned to you.
“Go with Catherine”… She must have literally gone to wherever Catherine’s staying, and then come back alone.
Minamo: Isn’t this lucky, ATRI-chan?
ATRI: It really is, Minamo. Thank you for leading me here.
Minamo: Hehe, no problem. Don’t get lost again though, you hear?
ATRI: I won’t get lost again. I’ve learned something.
ATRI lets go of Minamo’s hand, and trots over to me. She immediately clings onto my sleeve again.
Minamo: Okay, see you. Ah, Natsu-kun, make sure to come to school tomorrow. We’re having special class meeting.
She waves and runs off.
I’m left alone with ATRI on the flooded pathway.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: …
We stand there, silent. Suddenly, a wave comes crashing over the tarmac, and my prosthetic shudders beneath me.
I start to tip over into the murk-
ATRI reaches out to keep me upright.
ATRI: Well what do you know. Much more high-performance than your leg, right?
Looking at her triumphant smile, I can’t bring myself to respond.
ATRI: It’s dangerous here. We should move, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: O-Okay…
She grabs my hand, and pulls me back down the hill.
Reaching the ship, I come to a stop on the pier.
ATRI: What’s wrong?
The night is so dark by now that I can’t see my feet. The seas are churning below me, a deep, endless expanse of black.
The ship is swaying, drifting back and forth from the pier.
ATRI: Oh, you can’t cross like this, can you? Hehehe, it’s my time to shine!
ATRI suddenly grab hold of me and hoists me up.
Natsuki: Huh!?
Surprised, I flail around, and plant my elbow straight into ATRI’s face.
ATRI: Oww! Tak, that hurts, you know?
Natsuki: S-Sorry!
Even though I gave her a good whack, her response is strangely muted. I suppose robots must be more robust than humans.
ATRI: Just stay still. If you flap around, I could end up dropping you in the sea.
ATRI hops from the pier, holding me tightly against her.
I feel cold water enveloping me, dragging me down into the depths.
This is it. I’m going to die.
Natsuki: Hurk! Hahh, hahh…!
ATRI: Phew, that gave me a shock!
We manage to clamber back up onto the pier.
Natsuki: You idiot! You could have killed me!
ATRI: I’m sorry. I miscalculated my trajectory…
She giggles and sticks out her tongue. Yeah, just try and act cute after almost drowning me…
Not needing to breathe seems to mean that she doesn’t seem to be afraid of sinking at all.
In my case, just touching the cold moon its waters filled me with the fear of death.
Natsuki: Going swimming twice in one day. Lucky me…
I jump over to the ship, soaked to my bones, without her help.
I’m pretty sure there’s no danger of her catching a cold, but nevertheless, we need to dry her clothes.
That, however, comes with a problem.
Natsuki: Wh-What are you doing dressed like that?
ATRI: Oh, should I take these off too? I am all wet, after all.
ATRI: Ah, doing so would be potentially problematic from the standpoint of robotical ehics-
Natsuki: Whatever, just stop!
ATRI: Oh, you’d prefer if I didn’t take them off? What a shame…
What!?
Ahem, anyway, I have by this point changed out of my wet clothes into my pajamas.
Drying off my hair with a towel, I sit on the bed and remove my prosthetic.
ATRI looks at it, and lets out a satisfied puff of air.
ATRI: Yep, I’m far more high-performance than that.
What’s with this weird sense of competition with a second-hard prosthetic leg?
Natsuki: This leg didn’t throw me into the sea, though.
ATRI: That’s not true! It was thanks to that thing that you ended up falling into the water like a chump earlier! It betrayed you!
…She has a point.
When I tried to save ATRI, it came off and dropped me into the drink.
Natsuki: (“Betrayed” ? ”Like a chump”? Is that what it looked like to her?)
ATRI: I’ve got loads more joints than that thing, and I can even walk on my own. And, y’know, other stuff too.
ATRI: What can I do to make you see how useful I really am?
It seems she’s seriously hung up on this nonsense.
Natsuki: (What a strange robot…)
The robots I’ve come into contact with in the past were largely ones that had had their functionality greatly limited. They wouldn’t even speak unless required, let alone have self-doubts like this.
Natsuki: By the way, what was the order you were given?
ATRI: The what?
Natsuki: The order your master gave you just before she put you to sleep.
I completely forgot to ask her before.
ATRI: Umm… Err…
Depending on her answer, I might even help her.
More than anything, I’m just curious what the last thing my grandmother asked of her was.
ATRI: Umm… That data seems to have been lost.
I feel like a fool for expecting a serious response from her.
ATRI: Hmm, what was it? Umm…
Natsuki: Robots can forget things too?
ATRI: Humanoid memories are stored using algorithms that are based on human neural links, so I am as capable of forgetting as anyone.
Natsuki: It’s weird that you’d forget something so important, though.
ATRI: I can’t choose what to remember and what to forget!
I recall learning at The Academy that Humanoids perform optimization on their memory storage while in sleep mode.
They archive data acquire that day, and delete unneeded memories.
But left in sleep mode for too long, it’s possible that memory faults may start to occur.
ATRI: Natsuki-san, umm… What kind of order do you think it was?
Natsuki: How would I know?
Natsuki: (Maybe it had something to do with that “project” she mentioned…)
She told me to salvage ATRI, and take her somewhere.
I really should have listened properly to her words. I’m incredibly curious now.
ATRI: Gah, this is annoying…
ATRI squats down with her head in her hands.
Natsuki: I’m starting to get the feeling that you’re halfway to being a piece of scrap-
ATRI: Hey, that word isn’t allowed!
ATRI: Calling robots that is banned under the Humanoid Anti-Discrimination Statute! You could face a penalty of up to three months in prison, or, err, what was it? Umm…
Natsuki: Once again, I feel stupid for expecting a serious answer.
More than a little exhausted, I flop backward on the bed.
ATRI: I’ll try and remember, I really will!
…
Not getting any response out of me, she sidles up to the bed.
ATRI: Natsuki-saaan…
Natsuki: I’m going to bed. Be quiet. You should get some sleep or something too.
Natsuki: If you want a sleeping bag, there’s one in the drawer over there.
ATRI: I’m fine with just a chair. I can sleep compactly wherever my master wants. I’m high-performance, after all.
Natsuki: Right. Goodnight.
ATRI: Ooh, one last thing, Natsuki-san!
Natsuki: What?
ATRI: Is there anything in particular you want to do when you get your leg back?
Natsuki: Hahh… Why are you asking me that all of a sudden?
ATRI: Well, I’m your leg now. I can’t not ask you, can I?
ATRI: I’ll do anything you want, so use me as you will!
Natsuki: I’m telling you, I don’t need your help!
Feeling a stab of pain in my chest, I turn coldly away from her and lie with my back to her.
The flickering lights finally give out, and the ship is plunged into darkness.
The night is windless.
Melancholy clouds obscure the moonlight, casting the seas in a somber gloom.
The damp air costs my skin in a horrid slickness.
I wonder how long it has been since I closed my eyes.
When I open them, I can see clearly through the gloom.
A creeping discomfort tickles at my nerves.
The radio is silent.
The waves are shallow.
It’s too quiet.
Please, something make a sound.
If I don’t hear something, anything…
Natsuki: (No. Don’t come for me…)
The pain hasn’t even begun yet, and already my breathing is ragged.
It’s like I can feel the weight of the silence crushing down on me.
Natsuki: (Just fall asleep… If I can fall asleep, I’ll be okay…)
“Is there anything in particular you want to do when you get your leg back”
ATRI’s words are still reverberating around my head.
Natsuki: (What do I want…?)
I’ve only ever thought about how to get my leg back.
I always believed that if I just managed to do that, the future I’d lost would be returned to me too.
Natsuki: (I know I’m wrong… I’ve just convinced myself out of desperation…)
I needed a reason to live on, a way to force myself to accept my circumstances.
I was studying in the city, at a school the call The Academy.
An elite institution intended to prepare the new generation’s brightest minds to save this doomed world.
Yeah. That’s right. I was supposed to save the world.
I thought it was possible. I believed it, without a single shred of evidence.
But that’s not a road I can travel anymore.
My father, who had been sending me the money for my tuition from wherever he is, suddenly stopped funding my studies.
A professor I’d clashed with used this as an excuse to have me thrown out of classes.
Natsuki: (Until that point, I though the world was fair, that all you needed to succeed were the right ideals…)
I should have seen the world for what it really was in that tunnel.
The moment that I lost my mother, and my leg.
I should have learned the unfairness of it all.
To pay my tuition, I had to sell my prosthetic leg.
It was a highly-advanced cybernetic model, which fetched quite the price.
I didn’t think about the fact that it was meant to replace the limb I using my entire life. It was like selling the simple ability to stand on my own two feet, just to pay my debts.
Yet somehow, I thought it would work out okay.
I’d been on my own for long time, I was used to handing things myself.
But life without my leg at that Academy, friendless and looked-down-upon, was harder than I could have imagined.
The phantom pain that I though had long disappeared returned.
One morning, my body breaking down from night upon sleepless night, I just ran away.
I dropped out, discarded everything, and came back to this godforsaken town.
“If I just get my leg back, I’ll have a future again.”
As much as I tell myself that, I’m still terrified of the nighttime.
Natsuki: (Everything’s fine like this. I don’t have a future anyway…)
Natsuki: (I’ll just wait to be swallowed up by the sea, just like this wretched world.)
Natsuki: (I’ll just sink into the depths. It’d be so easy to do…)
Just like that day…
The day I lost my leg.
The day I lost my mother.
The day I lost my future.
What better way to get revenge on this world than to deprive it of one of those few remaining, sad little lives it still holds? Just like that day…
Natsuki: (But I don’t want to die. I just don’t want to go yet…)
Natsuki: (Someone, anyone… Save me… Mom… Dad…)
Natsuki: (Anyone… Anyone!)
Somebody reach into this suffocating darkness, and pull me out!
I thrust out my hand, vainly hoping.
I know it’s useless. I know that I’m alone. No one will venture into this dark tunnel to save me.
I’m going to be left behind.
The I feel a touch.
Natsuki: (Huh!?)
What…?
Natsuki: (Don’t I fall asleep?)
Racked by my phantom pain and writhing on the bed, I’ve been holding my hand out into the damp air.
I do that a lot, but somehow it’s different tonight.
There’s another hand, meeting mine.
ATRI: Being able to shout even while asleep is quite the trick. Is that some kind of error in your mental programming?
Natsuki: ATRI…
ATRI: Hmm, his brain might need some maintenance.
Natsuki: If that’s something you can do, go ahead. Cut all the bad memories out of me, and let me live an easy life…
ATRI: I’ll give it a try.
Peering into my eyes with a serious expression, she reaches out to pat my head.
She’s holding a towel in her hand.
ATRI: Let me wipe all of this sweat off of you first, or you’ll catch a cold. Humans aren’t as sturdy as robots, after all.
Of course, those small hands can’t wash away all of the memories. But it’s strange…
Natsuki: (I can feel the pain receding…)
The sickening ache where my leg should be is gradually fading into nothing.
Not lurking like when I sleep, threatening to strike me again at any time…
But soothed completely.
Hot tears begin to well in my eyes.
Tears long held back, my body too overwhelmed with the pain to let them out.
ATRI: Why are you crying? Does it still hurt?
Natsuki: No, it’s not that… I’m…
I try to hold back the tears, my hands shaking and clenched into fists. But I know it’s no use.
I’m tired of it all. Enduring the pain, hiding the fear. I just… I just want, for once, to feel some warmth.
Natsuki: You’re… my leg, aren’t you?
ATRI: Indeed I am! And I’m much more high-performance than your other one!
I take that tiny hand of hers, and pull her closer.
I wrap my arms around her.
ATRI: Oh…?
I hold her fragile form against me.
I bury my face into her chest, and close my eyes.
ATRI: Umm… Natsuki-san, I would prefer to wipe you down first…
Natsuki: I’m fine like this.
ATRI: Are you trying to wipe your sweat on me? Umm, I’m supposed to be a leg, not a towel.
Natsuki: Legs don’t complain.
ATRI: …I’ve learned something.
Natsuki: …
The tears stream down my cheeks in searing rivulets. I feel no pain at all.
I shakingly tighten my grip on ATRI, and whisper.
Natsuki: Will you let me fall asleep like this?
ATRI: Of course.
I open my eyes, seeking that soft voice.
She’s smiling.
A smile I feel spreading through me, like a flood of pure, cleansing water.
Natsuki: (It’s this… This is what I’ve wanted this whole time…)
To have my leg again, and to experience once single peaceful night.
Yet I feel that even the most advanced cybernetics could not give me as gentle and soothing a night as this.
ATRI: Hehe…
ATRI strokes my hair, smiling down at me.
My heart aches with the pain of a thousand sleepless nights.
But now, I’m at rest.
The horrors of the past, and the fears of the future, all gone.
Before long, I feel my consciousness slipping away…
ATRI: Good night, Natsuki-san.
I drift into a tranquil sleep.
When I wake, I feel the gentle rocking of the waves.
Natsuki: …
The wind turbine spins outside of the window, and the comfortable drone of the radio news fills the room.
I can’t remember the last time I woke up so unburdened by pain.
A whisper tickles my ear.
ATRI: Hmmmnmnn…
A sweet, tingling breath.
I slowly open my eyes, and look over to the source.
ATRI: Ahhn... Not there, Natsuki-san… You naughty boy… Hehe♪
Natsuki: …
I carefully slip my arm out from under her, and leave her on the bed.
My head feels completely clear.
That clearness, however, means I remember every pathetic thing I did last night.
Natsuki: …I wish I was dead.
The memories weight heavily on my mind.
ATRI: Mmmn… Nyehehe… Natsuki-saaan…
Natsuki: I didn’t know robots could talk in their sleep. Is she dreaming while she’s in sleep mode?
Humanoids are supposed to use sleep mode to reorganize their memory banks. I wonder if that process appears to them something like a dream.
ATRI: Is there anything in particular you want to do when you get your leg back?
Natsuki: I guess she really forced the answer out of me in the end.
Looking down at her peaceful demeanor, I can’t help but feel a twinge of anger.
I was content to blame everything on my leg.
Blame it on that, and just wander alone through the deep, looking for something I’d never find. That would have been the easy life, I though.
Natsuki: …And yet I ended up finding this thing.
ATRI: Mmn, aaahn… Natsuki-san, you silly boy… ♡
But what do I want now?
Sighing, I pinch ATRI’s cheek.
ATRI: Hehe… That tickles!
Natsuki: I can’t let her see me like that again. I don’t want her acting all smug.
I look up out of the window.
The drizzle and haze of last night has given way to glorious sunshine.
Natsuki: Right, get up, toaster.
ATRI: My name is ATRI… That’s another recognized term of abuse! Your punishment for repeat infringement is… Rocket punch!
Her hand lightly boinks against my belly. It doesn’t hurt one bit.
Natsuki: Huh… I guess being half-asleep somehow lets robots attack humans?
Unless that wasn’t an “attack” ? What was it, then?
Natsuki: Whatever, Get up.
ATRI: Argh!
She looks around the room with bleary eyes.
ATRI: Oh yes… Last night, I slept with him…
Natsuki: Please don’t word it like that.
ATRI: Good morning, Natsuki-san… “yawn”!
Natsuki: I never thought a robot would have this much trouble waking up.
ATRI: I’m a low-voltage model… Mmn, hahh…
What does that even mean?
ATRI sits up on the bed, stretching her neck from side to side.
ATRI: Ugh, I slept in a weird position, and now my joints are all creaky…
Natsuki: Hurry up and put some clothes on. I don’t know where to look right now.
ATRI: Kay…
Natsuki: Plus, well… I’ve decided not to sell you.
ATRI: …Oh?
Natsuki: I don’t want to lose another leg, or a body pillow, or whatever we’re saying you are now.
ATRI: Yeah, I knew you’d come around! Now you realize how high performance I am, right?
Natsuki: Put some damn clothes on!
Maybe I’m just being self-destructive again.
I know that this decision has no future merits beyond the immediate benefits.
Natsuki: (But it’s better than just wasting away, isn’t it?)
My heart wells up with a strange feeling. It’s like the path into extinction I had though to be so easy to walk suddenly diverging, leading me to a very distant destination.
There’s something meditative about brushing your teeth.
Staring into the mirror and mechanically moving my hand, I start to get lost in though.
Natsuki: (It’s all well and good making my own decision, but now do I actually support myself from here on out?)
It’s one thing to say I’m not going to sell ATRI.
But the consequences are another thing entirely-especially when you consider the two in particular that stick out like sore thumbs.
The first of those being my debts.
If I don’t sell ATRI, my grandmother’s debts will likely have to be paid with everything else I own.
If it was just the submarine I might be able to make do, but I losing my boat would mean losing my home.
To tell the truth, though, I’m not entirely sure I believe that repossession order is even real.
Why did I agree to go along with Catherine’s plan despite how shady it seemed, you ask?
Well, it’s all because she was offering me a concreate way to get my hands on at least half of whatever she wanted salvaged from my grandmother’s place.
Natsuki: (I was suspicious of her, for sure, but I had no real choice but to go along with it.)
When I left The Academy and came back here, I found the town half-submerged and my grandmother on her deathbed.
So no matter how suspicious it seemed, it was at least a chance to make something of my
Predicament. I had nothing to lose.
And in the end, there really was a treasure down there.
ATRI: Brushy brushy brushy brushy…
A little tuft of hair been bouncing up and down in the corner of my eye this whole time.
I glance downwards.
Said treasure is brushing her teeth alongside me.
Natsuki: (Robots brush their teeth too?)
Natsuki: (They don’t have to eat though, do they?)
Scientists attempted to research artificial organs that would allow a robot to power themselves with food, but practical models were never completed.
ATRI hasn’t eaten at all since I found her, and she doesn’t seem hungry at all.
Which brings me to my second problem-what do I do with her?
I could think op it as having bought a domestic servant, but somehow that idea sticks in my craw. Would it be better to treat her like a roommate? Shipmate?
ATRI: Brushy brushy brushy brushy… And spit!
Natsuki: (I’m a little bit terrified she’s suddenly going to start wolfing down all of my food…)
Without any income of my own currently, I’ve been surviving on the little money my grandmother had left.
I’m going to have to find some way of making some cash.
Natsuki: (I guess I’ll ask Minamo if she knows anythere in need of workers.)
She’s really the only person in this town I can call a friend.
Natsuki: Oh yeah. She told me to come to school…
ATRI: Nahuhi-shan.
ATRI looks up at me, toothbrush still in her mouth.
Natsuki: Don’t talk with your month full. Yeah?
ATRI: I can’t properly reach my back teeth. Would you brush them for me?
Natsuki: …
I take her toothbrush.
ATRI: Ahhhh.
It’s… not as “meditative” like this, that’s for sure.
ATRI: Ahhhhhhh.
Natsuki: …There you go. Now wash your mouth out.
ATRI: Gurglegurlegurgle… Ptoo!
She spits out into the cup in my hand.
Natsuki: …Why the hell am I the one brushing your teeth?
Wouldn’t it normally be the opposite?
ATRI: Isn’t performance maintenance on their robot an owner’s responsibility?
Natsuki: Ngh… Good point. Annoying, coming from you, but I get it.
I sigh, and rinse my own mouth out.
Natsuki: Just checking, but you don’t actually need to eat or anything, do you?
ATRI: Affirmative. I have no need for nutrition from food.
Natsuki: Great. Well, that’s a weight off of my mind.
Natsuki: Now that I’m not selling you, money’s going to be pretty tight around here. On top of keeping myself alive, I’ve got those debts to pay.
ATRI: I don’t think you need to worry about that so much.

Natsuki: What? I told you, I’m not selling you.
ATRI: You won’t be able to afford a new leg if you don’t, will you?

ATRI: I call it ‘Atri and Natsuki’s Honeymoon Countdown Calendar!’
It’s a roughly-drawn grid of forty-five squares. The last one is labelled “That’s all folks!”
ATRI: I’ll cross off each day as we go. Ah, I should fill in yesterday. Hmhmm…
ATRI: Okay, forty-four days left.
Natsuki: …Whatever.
ATRI: …Natsuki-san?
I turn my back on her, and walk back into the cabin.
Natsuki: (Why am I getting annoyed with her…?)
I thought she was my property, but it really doesn’t feel like that at all sometimes. Why does that get to me, though?
I’m annoyed all over again, this time at myself.
She’s a robot, and I’m her master. If I ordered her to, she’s have to stay with me as I want.
Then why doesn’t it feel that way?
Natsuki: If you’re fine with that, then I don’t care. It’ll make my life a lot easier.
Natsuki: I’ll have a lot less on my plate with you gone, I suppose.
ATRI: Yayyy!
ATRI raises both hands in the air, and starts to bounce up and down. The little tuft of hair sticking up from her head wibbles with each jump.
ATRI: Yay, yay, yayyyyyy!
With her arms raised and her hair flying everywhere, I can finally get a good look at her face.
Due to the difference in our heights, normally all I can see is that little tuft on the top of her head.
Natsuki: What are you so happy about all of a sudden?
ATRI: We’re going to go to school now, right?
Natsuki: What? Not a chance.
ATRI: Oh, come on. At least tell me why not, then?
My only response is a sigh.
ATRI: I know all about school. It’s a place where you can learn all kinds of things, right?
Natsuki: Is that what you’ve got logged in your database?
Humanoid memory has one particular section devoted to a database of terminology, almost like an inbuilt , editable dictionary.
ATRI: Umm… I think somebody told me that a long time ago…
Natsuki: Who, my grandmother?
ATRI: Hmm… Gah, I can’t remember.
It seems like she gets particular frustrated when she can only partially remember things.
ATRI: I want to try learning things!
Natsuki: Wouldn’t you be better off searching for your lost memories before your forty-five days are up, though? It’s hardly the time to be learning new stuff.
ATRI: But when I hear the word ‘school’ I just get strangely interested…
ATRI: I think part of my lost memories might be there.
Natsuki: Huh? Have you been to school before, maybe?
She shakes her head.
It seems less in denial and more not knowing the answer. That must be another thing lost from her memory.
I’m starting to think almost everything from before she was put to sleep in that storehouse gone.

Natsuki: I said no.

ATRI: I want to learn all kind of things, and become the best robot I can possibly be! I want everybody to depend on me!

ATRI: That’s exactly why I want to learn, as quickly as possible!
So she wants to be the best possible robot ready for her next master. That does make sense, even if the though makes my chest tighten…
ATRI: Why don’t you like going to school, Natsuki-san? You started throwing a tantrum when Minamo mentioned too.
That is absolutely, objectively not what I did.
Natsuki: It’s just pointless.

Natsuki: There’s nothing left for me to learn there.
I don’t mean that in a self-aggrandizing way. That’s just the simple reality of the situation.
ATRI: In that case, you can just be my companion.
Natsuki: Why would I do that? Just go on your own.
ATR: I can’t do that. I’m your leg. I can’t exactly leave your side, can I?

Natsuki: I don’t care about that. Go, if you really want to.
Sighing and tutting, I turn my back on the conversation and walk out onto the deck.
ATRI: Where are you going?
Natsuki: For a walk. It’s not like I’ve got anything better to do.
ATRI: Awwww!

Half an hour later…
ATRI: …What is this place?
Natsuki: No idea. I just picked a direction to walk in, I didn’t know where we’d end up.
Standing before us is a half-sunken concrete building.
ATRI: Wow… It’s amazing how half of it is underwater. I don’t have any entries on this kind of avant-garde architecture in my database…
Well, of course not. At the time she was put to sleep, this building would have been on the top of a hill.
ATRI: Searching, searching… Hang on, is this a school?
Natsuki: Huh, well, what do you know? What a coincidence.
ATRI: Heh, I guess you’re out of luck, Natsuki-san. You’re accidentally brought me exactly where I wanted to go.

ATRI: Okay, sounds great!
ATRI grins, utterly clueless. There is one problem with that plan, though.
Natsuki: How the hell do you even get into this place?
The school buildings are tangled up in a thick web of ivy, tree branches infiltrating through cracks in the concrete and shoulder-deep water covering every obvious pathway.
Surely they’ve given this place up to the waves, and moved somewhere else-
Child A: Ah! It’s the Hitman!
Natsuki: Huh?

Natsuki: (There really are people inside.)

Natsuki: Let’s go home. I’ve got a bad feeling about this.

Child A: There he is! He’s got a weapon, and he’s brought his henchman too!
Child B: Oh no, it is him! We’re all gonna diiie!
The children crowed around the window, pointing down at us and babbling in fear.
ATRI: Natsuki-san… I detect hostiles in this area. Time to unleash my true form, and engage offensive maneuvers.

Child A: Don’t worry. I’ll take him down!

Child C: Be careful…
Child A: Leave this guy to me!
Suddenly feeling like a bad guy in some cheesy action flick, I wait until one of the kids comes out of the building.
She slowly paddles over to me in a small boat. Somehow, the scene loses a little of its tension.
Ririka: Here I am, Hitman! Don’t underestimate my power!
Brandishing the paddle like a sword, the little girl stares me down with fiery eyes.
ATRI: If you want Natsuki-san, you’ll have to go through me! And I have the high ground!
ATRI stands imperiously above her, arms outstretched as if daring her to attack.

Natsuki: Yeah, shove off, shorty.

Ririka: Hitman, I challenge you to a duel!

Ririka: Everyone in town’s saying that you’re some kind of assassin. And that you’ve killed three people, and now you’re lying low here.
Ririka: And, and, you’ve got a machine rifle blow dart grenade gun in your cane, and a napalm cannon in your leg! I know all about you!
Natsuki: (That’s really what the people around here think of me?)
ATRI: I-Is that true!?
ATRI turns to me, wide-eyed and pale in the face.
Natsuki: One hundred percent.
I’ll just leave that idea in her head for a while.
ATRI: …I can shoot my fists out like rockets, too. It’s true. They’re, err, even more powerful than his guns…

Ririka: You bet it is!
Natsuki: In that case, I’m getting in.

The government has given up on the low-lying areas that are soon to be completely swallowed up, and simply recommend that everything moves inland.

A robot’s actions and any associated feedback are usually recorded in a log.
They’re useful for troubleshooting in the case of a breakdown or when a robot’s undergoing maintenance. Humanoids record these logs by outputting them to an external source.
Basically, they write them down.
As Humanoid brains are based on the same neuron structure as actual human brains, they’re not capable of outputting directly in a digital format like your average computer.
So it’s necessary to record everything on paper.

The would have been quite some time ago, before the great sea rise-before ATRI was constructed, even.
Compared to the peak of humanity’s population, schools everywhere have dramatically fewer students now.

Ririka: Oooh, you’re so smart, Minamo-chan!

Jeez, she’s celebrating like she’s one of the little kids.
Natsuki: If you rotate a magnet inside a coil, you can make a pretty efficient source of electricity.
Natsuki: You just need to have a way to keep the magnet spinning, and a way of extracting the power from the system.
The motor, essentially the heart of a generator, would be a little beyond some kids to make, hence why I bought one at the junk shop.
We’re just going to make a device that will make it spin.
I start to sketch out a blueprint on the blackboard of how we’re going to assemble our parts.
To tell the truth, I wasn’t sure at all that we’d find exactly what we needed.

There’s a set of robots constructed from a bicycle wheel and “blades” made from fabric from an umbrella, a stand to keep it vertical, and a motor attached to an axle running through the wheel’s center…
It may look like a pile of trash, but it has all the ingredients of a real wind turbine.

The wheel creaks as I try to turn it. I give it a little oiling.
