There’s a perfect breeze blowing outside.
I attach wires to the motor’s outputs, and hook them up to a lightbulb.
It’s a particularly old-fashioned incandescent model, the kind that’s practically unused today. They were being sold for close to nothing at the junk shop.
I cover it with a box with a single pinhole cut into it.

The turbine’s blades pick up the wind, and slowly it starts to turn.

All of the energy that the kid had before has completely vanished in an instant.

The gentle lilt of the radio floats on the shoreline waves.

The ship’s generator has a built-in weather vane, which automatically tilts the robots to the most optimal angle to catch the wind.
It was made by my grandmother to aid with her oceanographical field work. She must have wanted to be able to use electricity no matter how far out to sea she was.

Natsuki: Well, ‘potential energy’ is the energy something has when it’s lifted up in the air, which becomes ‘kinetic energy’ when it falls.
I take the thick book Ririka has been reading from her hands.

It falls into her hands with a heavy thud.
Her face lights up with understanding as she feels the sensation in her fingers.
Natsuki: The heavier the object and the higher you drop it from, the more potential it has.
Natsuki: You can convert electricity into potential energy in order to store it.
Natsuki: For example, you could use spare electricity from a wind turbine to pump water up high, store it, and then release it to drive a water wheel even when there’s no wind to drive your windmill-turning the potential energy back into electricity.
Ririka: Hmm, I see…
Ririka listens intently to my explanation. It seems like it’s getting through to her.
As she learns more and more, she starts asking questions on all kinds of topics.
The impromptu lesson gets more and more in-depth.
Ririka: So you mean that a water wheel can make loads more electricity than a windmill? That means we could make a really bright light if we had one of those, right?

She bites her lip and thinks.

Natsuki: Exactly. You need a clear, uninterrupted running stream, in one direction. Something like a river, or an aqueduct.
No matter how much water we have around here, its flows are so unpredictable that’s not possible to practically dam it off.

Natsuki: If we could create a flow from a high place like that, we could get an efficient source of power. But how do you think we’d lift the water?
Natsuki: In order to get the water high enough to then make it flow down, we’d have to expend more energy than we’d eventually make.
Ririka: That’s, umm, the ‘law of conservation of energy,’ right?
Natsuki: Oh, you’ve already been taught about that?
Ririka: No, I read it in this book.
She answers immediately.
Ririka; So if we wanted to use water power, we’d either need to make things flow better around here, or find a way to get water up high… This sounds kinda tough.

I remember a time when I still had this kind of pure curiosity in me.
Before I entered The Academy… Long before that, even. Before that tunnel collapsed on us, and I lost everything.

Gazing down at that contented little face, I remember something my father told me once.

The Academy claims to be our best hope for finding the people who will save the earth.
But who knows if anybody there can really do that?
Maybe no one can save it. Or maybe it’ll be saved by some curious genius, completely unrelated to The Academy.

These days, radio is the most prolific form of media humanity has.
Television still exists, but there’s hardly anything on the air. It’s a medium purely for the richest now.
The great sea rise threw the planet’s internet infrastructure into chaos, and any devices capable of accessing what’s left of the various walled-off networks are now out of reach of the average person.
Analog radio, once almost forgotten by the people at large, has become mainstream again. It’s much cheaper to make, and cheaper to listen to, after all.

Plastic, naturally, doesn’t rust. And since it’s completely waterproof, it’s not going to rot in seawater either.

The concept of the “uncanny valley” often comes up when talking about Humanoids.
As a robot’s appearance and mannerisms become more human-like, there comes a point when they from appealing to deeply unsettling.
If they’re totally human, the creepiness disappears, but the Humanoids back in the city were firmly in the uncanny valley.
Most of the time you wouldn’t notice, but occasionally there would just be moments where you realized just how alien an object you were looking at.
I haven’t had a single moment like that with ATRI yet.

A robot that doesn’t need food, but still wants to eat crab… What a decadent age she must have been built in.

That little doubt tingles at back of my mind, but who cares, really? It seems crab’s on the menu tonight.
We transport the tins up to one of the empty classrooms at school.
Ryuuji: Yep, these all look in good condition.
Ryuuji opens each can in turn. None of them show any signs of water damage.
There should be more than enough in these five cans for what we’re planning.

Natsuki: I want to make up dam slightly bigger. When I started planning I was envisioning it being made of metal, but now we’re using fiberglass we’re not limited to flat surfaces.
Fiberglass is much easier to mold compared to metals, which would require specialized tools to shape into curves.
Now I can make a much more energy-efficient design.
Ryuuji: Wow, you’re kinda amazing, y’know?

Natsuki: I did learn some stuff there, but mostly I taught myself.
I always used to want to learn everything, no matter what it was. I suppose I picked that up from my grandmother, or my father.

Natsuki: And I guess I’m sorry for assuming you were an idiot, too.
I bow my head to him earnestly.
Ryuuji: Heh, you’re really able to come out and just say that. I’m kinda surprised.
Natsuki: What?
Ryuuji: Heh, you’re a funny dude.
I stare at him nonplussed as he laughs and pats me on the shoulder.
Minamo: They’re ready!
Minamo is standing by a desk that she’s carried down, watching over an enticingly bubbling pot on a portable stove.
In the pot are pair of brights red creatures.
ATRI: Crab, crab, wonderful crab! ♪

There’s nothing in the broth but salt, but the crab is so full of sweetness that it’s still absolutely delicious. You don’t need any seasonings when you have such good base ingredients.
The sea may have stolen all hope from this town when it swallowed up our lives, but you could say it brought some gifts with it. The seas made humanity prosperous in the first place, after all.
Ryuuji: Mmmn, this stuff’s great. Just another piece of top-class work from Nojima Engineering.
Natsuki: I guess so. This takes me back…
Preparing food with everything like this, it’s almost like… What is it? Hmmm…
Minamo: It’s like a school festival or something, isn’t it?
Minamo grims, and everything nods in agreement.
ATRI: What’s a ‘school festival’?
Minamo: It’s an event where all the classes in a school put on some kind of special event, like a play, or a café, or haunted house.
Minamo: To get the classroom ready you normally have to stay at school until really late.
Ryuuji: We used to have them every year before the school got flooded.
ATRI: Ohh, that sounds fun.
Ririka: I was the prince in Snow White when I was in first year!

Ryuuji: We’d definitely need electricity for that. Right?
Natsuki: Yeah. It’s help with the preparations, and allow for a lot more activities.
Ryuuji: We’ll get started on the dam tomorrow. Right, bro?
For some reason the “bro” doesn’t even phase me.
Natsuki: You got it. I’m counting on you.
I respond as naturally as anything.
I never thought for a second that I’d end up actually getting along this guy. I thought we’d never see eye-to-eye.
Natsuki: (I guess that’s the power of crab. Gotta respect the crab.)
It’s just like ATRI said. Delicious things make you happy…
Natsuki: It’s gotten really late…
After we ate our fill of crab, I spent quite a while with Ryuuji examining possible to dam.
By the time we leave the school the tide has risen, and the roads are covered in a layer of glistening water, lapped by the waves.
ATRI: Natsuki-san, watch your step.
Natsuki: I’m fine, okay?
We trudge along the half-submerged pavement, holding hands.
Natsuki: (When did this become normal…?)
We’ve only been living together a few days, and we’re already walking everywhere hand in hand.
It makes me strangely uneasy.
If I become too reliant on ATRI, how will I survive when it’s just me and my own, crappy leg?
Natsuki: (…I’ll be fine, I’m sure. I’ve survived up until now, haven’t?)
As I walk carefully through the gurgling waves, ATRI suddenly stops and pulls at my hand.
ATRI: Wait, there’s something over there.
A strange object is lying across the road, seafoam washing up and over it as the water pushes inland.
Natsuki: …What on earth is that?
ATRI: Ooh, I know, it’s a manatee! I read about those in my textbook. ♪
Catherine: Ughhh… Gurbleburblegurble…
Natsuki: Catherine!?
My erstwhile business partner is lying in the middle of the sunken path.
Catherine: Ugghhh, I’m just so useless… I’m just gonna lie here, and let the sea take me. ♪
Natsuki: Is she drunk?
Another wave rolls in over the pavement.
Catherine: Blurgh… Hurk!
It break against her face, and she starts coughing up salty water.
ATRI: I don’t detect any danger, but we should avoid her just in case.
Natsuki: If we avoid her, she’s going to drown. We should help.
ATRI: But she tried to hurt you, Natsuki-san…
Natsuki: That was partially my fault. You said you’d protect me if things go bad anyway, didn’t you?
ATRI: Of course, but my rocket punch is so powerful that I’d prefer not to use it too often.

ATRI lets go of my hand, and moments later returns with Catherine draped over her shoulder.
ATRI: Okay, let’s go. ♪
Catherine: That goddamn kid… He thinks he’s so good just  because he’s kinda cute… Hic!
Natsuki: …I get the feeling she’s going to raise hell when she wakes up, but we can’t just leave her here.
We head home, begrudgingly bearing our booze-scented burden.
Catherine: Ughhhhhh…
Catherine: …
Ah, here it comes.
Catherine: Where am I…?
Catherine looks around wildly in confusion.
Catherine: That kid’s boat? Ugh…Oww, my head! Just how much did I drink last night?
Catherine: Ughh, I completely blacked out. Wait, if I’m here, does that mean we—
Natsuki: Not in a million years.
Catherine: Whoa!?
The instant she wakes up on the sofa, she starts with her usual nonsense.
I’ve been awake the whole time she’s been lying there snoring.
Spurred on by finding not just the correct materials but a reliable partner too, I’ve been so engrossed in redrawing my blueprints that I’ve not noticed the dawn coming.
Natsuki: (Plus, it’s not like I could just close my eyes for a bit with a potential murderer snoozing on my couch.)
I’d have to be crazy to go to sleep across the room from a drunkard who tried to slit my throat the last time I saw her.
Catherine: Hey… What the hell’s going on?
Natsuki: First, be careful. ATRI’s asleep, but one word from me and she’ll wake up. A robot always obeys its master, after all.
That’s a complete lie, and I know it. This “Low-voltage” piece of scrap wouldn’t wake up if I kicked her in the head.
Catherine: What did you do to me?
Natsuki: Nothing. You were drunk and it looked like you were about to drown, so against my better judgement we brought you here.
Catherine: Huh… Thanks, I guess.
Wow, she didn’t even try to argue with that. I guess she’s had a similar experience before… Unsurprisingly.
Natsuki: I’m sorry about the debt. If you want, take this ship, and the sub, and sell those to make up for it.
She’d get an order of magnitude less money than she would for a Humanoid, but it would probably just about be enough.
Catherine: If I did that, you’d end up homeless.
Natsuki: There’s plenty of empty rooms in the school I could hunker down in. I could even use the showers there.
After diving with ATRI yesterday, we’d borrowed the school showers to wash down. I didn’t want to have ATRI’s hair smelling of the sea.
There’s no hot water, but that’s not a problem at this time of year.
Catherine: Owning a ship like this would be nothing but trouble…
Natsuki: Are you sure about that? Whoever hired you might not care.
Catherine: True…
Catherine stands and walks toward the door.
Catherine: I should apologize too. Not that apologizing really makes up for what happened before…

ATRI: Mmmn… What’s going on, Natsuki-saaan… Is it morning already?
ATRI groggily awakens.
Catherine: Eep!
Catherine: W-Well, see you around. Thanks for the help.
She swiftly makes her exit.
Natsuki: Not so threatening for someone who looked like she could have gladly slashed my throat a few days ago…
Maybe she’s not that evil after all. Was she just bluffing?
ATRI: Ohhhhh? Where did the lady we picked up last night go?
Natsuki: She said thanks, and left. Surprisingly gratefully, all in all.
ATRI: Okaaaay… Mmmnph…
Well, that’s the question of my grandmother’s debts solved for the moment, if not forever…
The next day, construction begins.
Natsuki: So, let’s go over the basics of how this will work again.
Natsuki: Moving a magnet near a coil makes a current flow through the wire. This is electromagnetic induction, as discovered in 1831 by the British physicist, Michael Faraday.
Natsuki: He discovered that an efficient way to generate electricity was to rotate a magnet within a coil.
Natsuki: This simple mechanism forms the basis of most modern electricity generators.
Natsuki: The only question is how you make the magnet spin. What kind of turbine do you use?
Natsuki: There’s a lot different options.
Minamo: Zzz…
Natsuki: Minamo.
Minamo: Y-Yes!?
She jerks out of her seat, standing bolt upright.
It’s rare to see her snoozing in class…
Minamo: Y-Yes, sir?
Natsuki: Tell me a little about some methods of power generation.
Minamo: Well, umm… you can burn fuel, use water… Wind? Geothermal energy? Umm, and…
Ririka: Ooh, me, me! Nuclear fission!
Natsuki: Okay, that’s pretty much all of the major ones. There’s potentially also nuclear fusion, but no one’s ever managed to put that to practical use.
For decades now, people have been saying fusion power is right around the corner. Studying how to practically apply the theories behind it is a major subject at The Academy.
Natsuki: Almost all forms of power generation basically come down to turning a turbine somehow.
Natsuki: Oil-and coal-burning power plants use steam to spin a turbine. A geothermal plant? Steam from boiling water deep in the ground spinning a turbine. Wind power? Just big turbines in the air.
Ririka: What about nuclear power?
Natsuki: They’re just like fuel-burning plants, but the heat is coming from a nuclear reaction instead of burning fossil fuels.
Ryuuji: Even those fancy fusion ones?
I nod.
Natsuki: As colossal as the amounts of nuclear energy involved are, in the end both fission and fusion generators are just spinning a turbine all the same.
Ryuuji: Seriously?
I was just as surprised when I found that out myself.
Natsuki: So basically, all of those methods of generation are just converting the energy from the fuel, water, or wind into electricity through a spinning magnet in a coil.
Natsuki: The key word there is ‘converting’-a generator doesn’t so much ‘generate’ power as it does simply ‘convert’ it from one form to another.
Energy can’t simply be birthed from nothing. That’s the point of the law of conservation of energy.
That means the conversion efficiency of a generator is a key factor. There’s always energy lost in the form of noise or heat, so a hundred joules of energy in won’t necessarily mean a hundred out.
Natsuki: There are some forms of power generation that don’t use turbines, by the way. Solar panels are a common example, but artificial muscle can also generate energy like that.
Natsuki: They’re a pretty interesting concept really. The muscles in the human body move by receiving electrical signals, so…
I can see the obvious lack of enthusiasm for a lecture on advanced biomimetics etched on everyone’s faces.
Natsuki: …Okay, back to the point. What we’re going to be doing is making a generator that utilizes a water turbine.
Ryuuji: Just like a regular hydroelectric dam, right?
I shake my head.
Natsuki: Strictly speaking, it’s a slightly different mechanism. This is tidal power.
That means that we’re going to be converting the energy of the incoming ocean tides into electricity.
Natsuki: I’m going to explain the specifics of the turbine we’re going to make, so try to follow along as best you can.
This is going to be like a big science experiment.
We’re going to need everyone understanding what’s going on as much as possible if we want to make this work, regardless of their age.
Natsuki: Right, let’s go and inspect the location.
I lead everyone down to an empty classroom on the second floor.
It’s low tide, and the floor is free of water.
Natsuki: First, we’re going to smash a hole through here.
I tap my prosthetic leg against the floor.
Natsuki: That will allow for water to flow down into the first floor.
The classroom below is already inundated with the sea.
Natsuki: We’ll be positioning the turbine in this hole.
Natsuki: This floor will fill with water when the tide comes in, and then drain again when it goes out.
Natsuki: It will naturally flow through the hole we made, and we’ll convert the energy of that movement into electricity.
Minamo: It sounds simple when you put it like that…
Natsuki: As I mentioned earlier, the key is going to be how we get the draining water to actually drive the turbine. What happens when you, say, suddenly pull the plug out of a sink?
Ririka: I know, I know! It makes a whirlpool!
Ririka throws her hand up, and doesn’t even wait for me to call on her.
Natsuki: Exactly. And we’re going to use that whirlpool.
Natsuki: We’ll make energy from both the rotational force of it, as well as the water falling.
There are quite a few ways to design a hydroelectric generator.
Most people will have seen hydroelectric dams, but it’s also possible to install water wheels in irrigation ditches, pipes, or any other kind of running water.
The key is that there has to be smooth flow in one direction.
Unfortunately, the water on the second floor flows in in one direction, and back out in the other.
There’s one way we can take advantage of that-a turbine with an axle aligned vertically, not horizontally. It’ll be able to turn efficiently regardless of what direction the water is coming from.
Ryuuji: So, what exactly do we have to do?
Natsuki: There’s three major things we need. First, we need to smash open that hole. I’ll walk you through the process to do that now.
Ryuuji: It’s easy enough to say that, but this is gonna be tough, y’know? We won’t be able to use any electricity drills or anything.
True, we don’t have electricity until we generate it ourselves.
Ryuuji: Well, we’ll manage it somehow. What’s second on the to-do list?
Natsuki: So the tide comes flowing up from the first-floor corridor, right?
At high tide, it rises up the stairs and floors the second floor.
The stairs are currently the only path in or out for the water.
Ryuuji: Year, and it goes back the same way.
Natsuki: If all of the water takes the path of least resistance and flows down the stairs, our hole will be useless.
Natsuki: So we need a value-in other words, a dam that will let the water in but prevents it from leaving again. That will create a reservoir that’s guaranteed to drain through our turbine.
Ryuuji: We’ll have to have a think about how we construct that, but I think we can manage it.
Natsuki: The third thing, of course, is the most important. We can’t make a generator without a turbine.
Natsuki: I want it to be about a meter in diameter, and it’ll need to be tall enough that the axle is above the water line at high tide.
I unfurl the blueprints and show them to him.
My scribbles here are more detailed than the last set, the product of a long, hard night.
Natsuki: We’ll be making it out of fiberglass, using the resin we salvaged yesterday. Sound good?
There are two important things when it comes to designing power plants.
Lifespan, and fixability.
A power plant should ideally be able to be operated safely for as long as possible. Entire communities can depend on them, and they need a sustainable source of power.
But no matter how long a plant is meant to last, there’s always the chance that it will run into problems. It must be constructed to allow maintenance, and be rebuilt easily if it fails completely.
Fiberglass is perfect for our needs in both respects.
It won’t rust in seawater like metal, and as long as you have the molds and plants you used originally, you can rebuild the same structure over and over again.
And most importantly, it’s easy to work with without electricity tools.
Ryuuji: …Sound good, mostly. Got a couple of problems, though.
He stares at the plants with a knitted brow.
Natsuki: I tried to give it as large a surface area as possible to get the most out of our limited flow of water…
Ryuuji: That’s fine. The blades will be easy to make in fiberglass. The problem is these parts, where we attach them to the axle. They’re too complicated. Think you can simplify them?
Natsuki: Then how about this?
Ryuuji: That might make it too weak, right? You sure about that?
Natsuki: Then maybe we can trim these parts down…
Ririka: Minamo-chan, can we go back to the classroom?
Minamo: I suppose so. It seems like this might take a while.
We’re so engrossed in our discussion that we hardly notice everyone leaving us completely alone.
Thus construction gets underway.
The first order of business is to carve some large polystyrene blocks into shape.
These will from the molds for the different parts of the turbine, which will be layered with fiberglass resin and left until it sets into shape.
Fiberglass’ ability to be molded like this is one reason why it’s such a widely-used material.
Also, its high strength to weight ratio makes it perfect for car fenders and boat hulls.
Minamo: And a bit there, and there…
Ririka: It kinda looks like snow when you carve it like that!
Child C: Whoa, yeah!
The kids are mostly treating this like fun, but they’re still doing good work. Once they reach a certain point, however, I have to step in to do the more delicate parts.
ATRI: Let me help too, Natsuki-san.
She looks up at me with puppy-dog eyes.
Natsuki: Not a chance. You’ll break everything into a million pieces.
ATRI: Aww, such is the fate of a killing machine. I must learn to control my horrific powers…
Natsuki: We’ve got limited resources here. We can’t afford too many failures.
Natsuki: I’m going to go and check up on how it’s going downstairs. Come give me a hand.
ATRI: Okaaaay…
She takes my hand with a disconsolate pout.
We can tell that work is going on as soon as we approach the stairs to the second floor.
The sound of clanging metal echoes off of the old concrete walls.
The sound stops as we approach the classroom.
Ryuuji: Damn, this stuff’s hard!
Ryuuji rests his pickaxe against the wall, and takes off his gloves.
His hands are red, raw and calloused.
Natsuki: This might be more difficult than I anticipated.
Ryuuji: I thought I could manage it, but at this rate it’s gonna take a whole month just to get the hole made.
This dilapidated old building is more sturdy than I ever could have imagined. We’ve only just started, and I’m already starting to think we’ve been a little naïve.
Natsuki: Maybe I should help out too.
Ryuuji: Nah, I’m the only one around here built for the rough stuff. I’m sure I’ll manage it.
He dons his gloves again, and grabs his pick.
Natsuki: …
To be honest, I’d prefer if he was freed up to help with the more complicated parts of making the turbine, parts that might require some of his particular specialist knowledge.
But I can’t exactly do this kind of job with my leg.
I suppose it will have to be him who handles the manual work…
Natsuki: …Ah. ATRI!
ATRI: Yes?
Sometimes it’s hard to remember because she looks like such a small, fragile girl, but she’s definitely the strongest among us.
Her strength is pretty much the only thing she’s useful for, unless you’ve got a real hankering for some crab.
Natsuki: Can you help me out?
ATRI: Absolutely! Whatever you want!
Natsuki: I want you to take this pickaxe, and open up a hole here. Just knock out all of the concrete in this circle.
A line marking out the size of the turbine is drawn on the floor.
Ryuuji: Seriously? You’re gonna make her do it?
ATRI: Hehe, this’ll be easy as pie! ♪
Natsuki: Let her give it a try.

ATRI: Wham!
Ryuuji: Whoa… She cracked straight through it.

Natsuki: Don’t listen to that idiot.
ATRI: Ah, it’s super-ultra-top-secret, so you can’t tell anyone, by the way.
Ryuuji: Jeez, seriously?
He can’t actually believe her, can he?
Natsuki: Well, keep that up, ATRI. We’re going to do some work upstairs.
ATRI: …
ATRI’s triumphant smile vanishes.
Natsuki: Hmm? What’s wrong?
ATRI: I’m supposed to be your leg. I should be by your side at all times.
Natsuki: You know what would be really useful? A leg you could take off and have knock out a floor for you. What a high-performance leg that would be, eh?
Natsuki: So don’t worry about me. Everyone else is up there to look after me.
ATRI: …
ATRI throws aside the pickaxe and trots over to me.
She grabs a hold of my shirt sleeve.
ATRI: As a robot, my operational priorities are hard-code, and being by your side is my highest priority.
Natsuki: Right… Well, it looks like I’m staying here. I’m worried that you won’t stick to the line anyway.

Ryuuji: Gotcha. Any problems, just yell.
With Ryuuji gone, ATRI reverts to a wide, gleeful smile.
ATRI: Okay then, in accordance with your wishes, it’s time to show you just how high-performance a demolition machine I can be!
She happily goes about swinging the pickaxe.
Natsuki: (Why does she hate being separated from me so much?)
I can’t tell whether it’s a part of her programming, or that she just wants me to see her working hard.
Whatever the case, I’m happy to have her strength to help out.
For a while, I have nothing to do but watch over her as she bangs away.
When the sun begins to dip, and the high tides threaten to invade the second floor, I take ATRI up to see everyone.
Natsuki: How are things up here?
Ryuuji: Going great.
Child B: Come back here!

Everyone hungrily chomps through the little packets of salty rice.
Everyone’s so famished from our long day of work that they all disappear with astonishing speed.
Natsuki: …
Minamo: What’s up, Natsu-kun? Don’t you like them?
Natsuki: No, they’re great…
It’s the absolute simplest of foods, and yet it somehow tastes so much better than anything I can imagine some big-shot chef making.
The crab yesterday was great too, but you can’t really mess up crab.
Natsuki: Better after a hard day’s work, huh…?
I savor the salty taste against my tongue, thinking about how long it’s been since I ate such a filling meal.
For a while every day passes by at this languid pace. We work from sunrise to sunset, enjoy Minamo’s feast, and then head home.
We reach the end of another long, exhausting day.
Natsuki: The hole is pretty much done, I think.
ATRI: Almost, yeah!
Natsuki: Hey, brats.
Child B: Why you gotta call us that, Hitman? Or, err, I guess maybe ‘Foreman’ makes more sense now…
I really don’t need another nickname.

Ririka: O-Okay…
Ririka nods earnestly.

Ryuuji: The molds are all finished. We can start layering the fiberglass in them now.
Natsuki: I’ll help too when I have a hand to spare.
Ryuuji: Thanks, we’ll need all the help we can get.
Minamo: Hehe, this really does feel just like we’re getting ready for a school festival or something.
Minamo: Did they have festival at your last school, Natsu-kun?
Natsuki: Well, it wasn’t really that kind of place. Everyone was too engrossed in their studies or personal research to enjoy those kinds of frivolous things.
Ryuuji: It was a high school, right? What kinda high school kid does ‘research’?
Natsuki: At that place, as long as you could get good results, you could study whatever specialist subject you wanted. Even I did.
Minamo: What kind of thing did you research?
Natsuki: The basics of robot construction, and potential applications of robots in extreme environments.
Minamo: Robot construction? Wow…
Ririka: Whoa, that’s kinda amazing! I don’t know anything about that kinda stuff, but it’s probably, y’know, amazing!
Ryuuji: Huh. So how did you go from fancy research and all that jazz to slumming it in a backwater like this?
Natsuki: Well, it wasn’t exactly by choice…
I laugh darkly, taking a seat and stretching out my right leg.
I undo the straps on my prosthetic limb.
Natsuki: I was eight years old when I lost my leg in a tunnel collapse.
Natsuki: That was the reason why I first came to this town.
Natsuki: My mother died in that same accident. The doctors said that I should recuperate somewhere peaceful, and so I was left with my grandmother.

A few days of construction pass.
We’ve now moved on to one of the most important parts of the process: molding the fiberglass.
We’ve now moved on to one of the most important parts of the process: molding the fiberglass.
Fiberglass is made by forming glass matting over a mold, in our case made of polystyrene, and then applying a hardening plastic resin.
Glass matting is comprised of woven glass fibers, with are impregnated by the resin.
You then layer these impregnated mats on top of each other in your mold, so they take the shape you need.
After hardening and polishing the surface, you’re left with a hard, glass-reinforced plastic.
It’s strong, durable, and water-resistant enough to be used for boat hulls and numerous other applications. It’s not the most exciting material to make, but it’s simple and easy to work with.
In our case, we’ll be making the central part of our generator, the water turbine.
And I’m thankful to say that after several days of molding, our turbine blades are coming together.
Ryuuji: It’s gonna be a while before these things harden up properly.
When fiberglass cures, it gives off a horrendous stench. Even with the windows open, it’s tough to even stay in the same room at this stage of the process.
Natsuki: Maybe we should go shopping while this is drying.
We make our way to the market district.
Junk Shop Owner: What you asked for just came in, lad.
I’ve been waiting for this-the real heart of our generator is here.
The main part of the core is the motor. This one’s basic second-hand model, but if we can make it spin, the magnet rotating inside the internal coil will generate electricity.
To convert that electricity into a useful voltage, we’ve got some wires and a transformer to attach it to.
Natsuki: We’ve already got a battery, haven’t we?
Ryuuji: The old junker we’ve been keeping at my place has got one in it. That’ll be good enough, right?
Natsuki: Yeah, more than enough.
One of the problems with renewable energy resources is that the amount of power they generate throughout the day isn’t very inconsistent.
But by storing some of the surplus energy generated in a battery when conditions are good or power usage is low, you then have a backup for when your usage exceeds what you’re generating.
Natsuki: How much will that be?
He taps away at his calculator.
Junk Shop Owner: This should be good. I’m cuttin’ my margins pretty fine for you on this one, y’know.
Even so, it’s an amount that would stretch the purse strings of any high schooler.
Ryuuji, Minamo, and I all have to pool our resources in order to afford it.

This strange, unpredictable robot girl.
A Humanoid who had been sleeping beneath the sea for years upon years.

There are few ways to ameliorate the phenomenon.
One method is to reflect the opposite limb in a mirror, and make it appear as if it’s not missing at all.
The brain will be fooled by this, and the pain will stop.
An artificial limb can help too, by what seems to be a similar mechanism.
Back when I had just lost my leg, I suffered horrendous phantom pains all the time. The cybernetic leg my father gave me completely cured it.
It was such a high-tech model that it felt like I had my real leg back.
But when I was forced to sell it, the agony returned.

This involves another round of managing the ballast tanks.
When surfaced, the tanks are filled with air, which is then purged and replaced with water when you need to dive. This reduces the sub’s buoyancy, and causes it to sink.
In order to surface again, you need to purge the tanks of water.
This is done by flushing them with compressed air.
It’s stored in cylinders attached to the sub, but a vessel this size can only hold a limited amount. Running out means you’re unable to surface, so you have to limit yourself to one dive per voyage.
Of course, if for some reason I did run out at the bottom of the sea, I have the crane to pull me up. That’s something I’d rather not have to rely on, however.
I pull on levers and flick switches, and air rushes into the ballast tanks.

Rumors have been spreading about our business since our first, successful job, and the customers have been coming in thick and fast since then.
Today we’re using our free time to go searching for some of the more difficult request, but we’ve hit a pretty big snag.
We have a client who wants us to retrieve an heirloom that was lost in a shipwreck in a storm several years ago, but we can’t even find the ship.
Ryuuji: These are the coordinates, though. It’s gotta be here somewhere.
Natsuki: That ship’s been down here a long time. It could have drifted away on the current.
ATRI, swimming alongside the sub holding on to its chassis, suddenly taps on the window and gives me some kid of gesture.

She points, and I turn the rudder.
There’s something lying on the bottom of the ocean.

ATRI swims over, and lifts the object up.
It’s a long, thin object. For a second I’m about to write it off as a lost mooring rope, but I pause.
Natsuki: Hang on… Is that an undersea cable?
It’s attached to some kind of small relay on the seafloor. ATRI pulls on it, but it’s impossible to see just how far away it stretches.
Natsuki: Be careful with that. It might still be functioning.
I wonder if it’s the kind of optical fiber cable that used to connect islands to mainland communication networks.
Natsuki: …Going by the map, there’s not any other land masses out in that direction for a long way. I wonder it leads?
In the past, cables this used to criss-cross the entirety of the Pacific ocean, connecting Japan to countries far across the sea.
Ryuuji: Did you find something?
Natsuki: Nothing pertinent to the job in hand, unfortunately.
Ryuuji: Well, it’s almost sundown. You’d better get back up here before it gets dark.

ATRI: …
She grabs hold of the Serpens Albus, and I fire up the compressed air tanks to send up upwards.

Ririka hands me my cane, and I finally feel able to breathe.

Ryuuji: Yeah, it’s just open sea out there.
Maybe there’s some kind of outpost stationed our in the ocean?
Ryuuji: Guess we’re outta luck today, though. Damn, I knew that job was.
Salvaging from sunken houses is made significantly easier by being able using maps. Unfortunately, heading further out to hunt shipwrecks probably requires specialized techniques.
Ryuuji: Eh, lucky we agreed a fee just for searching, even if we didn’t find it.
Natsuki: I don’t feel particular good about taking money for a failure. though.
The people that come to us often want us to salvage more than just an object. They’re looking for their memories.
The vast majority of the requests we get are to find things that have far more sentimental value than they do monetary.
Today’s failed salvage was just the same.
Natsuki: I think we should camp out here for the night, and search again in the morning.
Ryuuji: Sounds like plan.
If we tried to make our way back ashore from his far out in the dark, we may well end up joining our client’s ship on the seabed.

She trots off, leaving little wet footprints on the way to the bathroom.
After a slightly early dinner, we all engage ourselves in our own business.
Ryuuji listens to his favorite radio program. The radio waves are barely reaching this far out, and the sound of fuzzy guitars has to fight to be heard over the static.
Ririka is poring through my modest collection of books, happily devouring all manner of things she can’t find on the library shelves.
I’m simply lying around bored.

Ririka: She said that she was popping outside.
Natsuki: Huh, I see.
It’s rare for her to leave my side without good reason.
Ryuuji: Dammit, the reception out here sucks…
While Ryuuji tries every trick in the book to will the radio waves into the antenna, turning it to every angle and jamming it up against his ear, I pass by him and walk out onto the deck.
ATRI is sitting on the edge of the bow, dangling her feet over the water. She’s gazing off listlessly into the far distance.
Looking at her face, thrown into profile against the evening calm by the light of the ship, a sudden pang of something akin to homesickness washes over me. I intended to call out to her, but I find myself simply watching her in silence.
ATRI: Hm…? Is something wrong, Natsuki-san?
Natsuki: No…
Natsuki: Are you all right? You’re just staring into space.
ATRI: I thought I saw something… Or heard something…
ATRI: Something calling to me. Someone I know… It’s a strange sensation. I’m finding it difficult to process.
She turns her eyes back to the still ocean.
Natsuki: “The sea is our mother, the cloud is our brother, the waves are our comrades all”… They say humans all have a connection to the sea. Maybe even you do too.
ATRI: …
She turns away form me with an odd look, almost… guilty.
A heavy silence falls over us. I have no idea what to say.
The sea is so still that even the waves off us no comfort.
Natsuki: …I want to hear that song again.
ATRI: Oh…?
Natsuki: Would you sing for me?
ATRI: …
She pauses, and nods. Then takes a soft, quiet breath.
She starts to sing, at first in a quiet, faltering tone.
She hums softly as if searching long-buried memories for that old melody.
It’s like she’s piecing the notes together from deep in her memory banks.
Gradually, the fragments come together.
ATRI: Hmmhmm… ♪
She sings, clear and lilting.
It seems like it’s all coming back to her.
Her voice resounds across the soft orange glow of the ocean.
The lone witness to this beautiful spectacle, I stand bewitched.
I think back to the days when I learned this song. I never had the slightest doubt about my future back then-I was sure life would be filled with happiness.
I thought the joy I felt would last forever. I believed that, without any proof, without even a single shred of evidence.
And then I lost my mother, and my leg…
I can never go back to those innocent days.
And yet it feels like I they’re right here again, in the form of this song.
My cheeks feel warm.
I suddenly realize that it’s because of the tears running down them.
I don’t wipe then away. I’m too enthralled to care.
Before I know it, the seas are silent again.
There is nothing but the soft whistle of the wind around us.
ATRI: Hahhh…
ATRI lets out a sigh, quiet and yet filled with emotion.
She puts her hand to her chest as she speaks.
ATRI: This song was so precious to me, but I’d forgotten it completely.
ATRI: You salvaged this memory for me, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: Oh, no… It was you, you…
The words simply won’t come out.
I don’t know if I know how to express what I want to say.

She speaks slowly, every word so careful and delicate.
ATRI: I felt like we had met long ago, when you were just a boy.
Natsuki: ATRI… So it was you…
She reaches out a hand to gently, so gently, wipe away my tears.
ATRI: It’s been a long time, hasn’t it? You’ve really grown up.
She smile at me, the sweetest of smiles, and I feel myself fall in love for the second time.
…
In the middle of the night, I’m awoken by a horrendously hot, heavy sense of humidity.
Ryuuji: Hrmm, nngh…

Ryuuji and Ririka are both squashed into this cramped bed with me.
I had laid out a sheet on the floor, but I struggled to get to sleep down there.

It’s completely black outside of the window, but it’s not too far from the dawn.
ATRI: Zzz, mmn…
ATRI is sitting in a chair, comfortably snoozing away.
“It’s been a long time, hasn’t it? You’ve really grown up.”

I felt so bashful around ATRI after that moment that I locked myself up in the cabin and said nothing to her for the rest of the night.
Natsuki: I’d sort of already realized this, but I’m really not as experienced with regular human relationships as I should be…
Until I dropped out of The Academy and came here, Minamo was the only friend I’d ever made.
And obviously, I’ve never had a girlfriend.
I thought such things were below me…
Natsuki: I guess this is the kind of situation you end up in if you don’t build up a knowledge base…
I’d always acted as if I was above everyone else, but looking back at the past few weeks, that could hardly be less true.
Natsuki: I’m just a man who’s good at studying, I suppose…
I look back on the me that thought he could save the world all by himself with acute embarrassment. I sit on the bed with my head in my hands.
Natsuki: Ugh, it’s too hot in here…
This cabin, and furthermore this bed, isn’t suited to this kind of population density.
I carefully extricate myself from the tangle of bodies, and quietly make my way outside.
Natsuki: …Huh? Why is it so foggy?
The entire area is coated in a thick layer of cloudy mist.
It should be about time for the sun to begin to peek above the horizon, but there’s not a single trace of its rays.
The wind is still, and yet the waves are buffeting the ship.
The deck is swaying enough to almost toss me off of my feet.
I have to grab onto the railing to keep myself form being swept into the briney deep.
Natsuki: I should head back to bed.
As I go to turn around, the fog grows somehow even darker.
Natsuki: What…?

An enormous silhouette looms over me through the mist.

It towers over the ship, gleaming with red lights.
Natsuki: Is that the lighthouse? No, it wouldn’t be in that direction…
That’s further out at sea, nowhere near the town.

The fog is so thick that I can’t make out anything else around us.

Some kind of huge ferry? Or…
Natsuki: A monster?
Perhaps I’m dreaming? This is just a strange nightmare, brought about by the muggy heat of the night. I shake with fear, rooted to the spot by the swaying of the deck.

I breathe a sigh of relief as I’m finally freed from this personal hell.
Catherine’s Voice: Boys, you can come back down now!
Catherine shouts up from the classroom window.
I’ve never been so glad to hear that voice.
All of the boys looks surprisingly serious. It seems like they took… something from the class.
Ryuuji: So, yeah, give it all you’ve got, Natsu.
Natsuki: Yeah, right…
I have absolutely no idea what I should be doing, but I’m happy he’s cheering me on, at least.
ATRI: Ah, Natsuki-san!
As soon as I enter the classroom, ATRI rushes over and grabs my hand.
ATRI: Welcome back!
Natsuki: Err, nice to be back…
ATRI: Is something wrong?
Natsuki: It’s, umm, nothing.
I squeeze her hand ever so slightly.
Ryuuji: Minamo, what kind of stuff did you learn about?
Minamo: Err… We’re not supposed to tell you!
Ryuuji: Aww, c’mon, you’ve gotta be able to tell us something!
Yoko: Tsk, you’re a real perv, Ryuuji-kun.

Minamo: Umm, in a way…

Ririka: I’ve taken my first steps toward adulthood…
Ryuuji: Huhwha!?
Ririka: I’ve learned the true meaning of loving hamburgers.
Ryuuji: …What?

Natsuki: Yeah, it was so “hardcore” I had no idea what was going on half the time.
I’m not lying.
Yoko: …Whoa. You, err, go guys.
Minamo: Eep… I’m getting embarrassed just thinking about it.
And so our “sex education” ended, with a distinctly strange atmosphere between the boys and girls of the school.
It’s not long before the day as a whole comes to a close.
I’m on cleaning duty, so I stay behind sweeping in the halls.
From the outside this place may look like a wreck, but the inside is keep surprisingly spotless.
ATRI: Natsuki-saaan.
Natsuki: Yeah?
ATRI: I’ve got club activities, so you can go home ahead of me today.
Natsuki: Understood. You seem to be trying really hard in the cooking club.

We haven’t exactly got much choice of clubs at such a small school. Over half of the girls here have become Minamo’s subjects.
Natsuki: I hope you’re getting along with everyone there.
ATRI: Of course I am!

I pat her soft hair.
ATRI: Well, if you say so…
She’s pacified a little by this gentle little exchange, but she still looks a little put out at not having to be around me constantly now.
Natsuki: I won’t be going home by myself anyway. I’ve made plans with Ryuuji.
ATRI: That idiot!
ATRI: Grr, I am detecting my jealousy circuits firing…
Natsuki: …Your what?
ATRI: Err, nothing. I’m supposed to keep that s secret from the boys…
She wanders back into the classroom, muttering to herself.
After I return home after spending the afternoon with Ryuuji, I start flicking once again through my grandmother’s papers.
I’m still looking for clues to ATRI’s lost memories whenever I get a chance.
Natsuki: She remembers me, which means she was living in this town eight years ago.
Natsuki: The order that ATRI is trying to remember must be something to do with the last project my grandmother was working on.
I’ve been trying to work out the nature of this project from whatever fragments of information I can find.
I’m slowly piecing together some kind of vague outline.
And yet I can’t for the life of me work our what ATRI has to do with it.
Natsuki: …
I relax for a moment, and instantly my concentration is gone. I look out of the window, and see the sun dipping below the horizon.
Natsuki: ATRI’s late…
Apparently the girls have made plans to go and grab some food after club activities.
I’m glad that ATRI’s making friends like this, but I have to admit there’s a tinge of loneliness to the situation too.
But I suppose being in the position to feel this particular loneliness just shows how lucky I am.
I look lazily around the room, until my gaze settles on object on the wall-the calendar.
When the forty-five-day countdown has finished, ATRI will be leaving. At least, that’s what she says.
I wonder how I’d feel if she really did disappear. The loneliness I feel in this moment, left by myself on this ship, would probably feel like absolutely nothing in comparison.
Natsuki: …Ugh, what’s wrong with me? I feel like I’m crying all the time lately.
During my time at Tha Academy, I’d always prided myself on not shedding a single tear in even the hardest moments.
Maybe I’m just making up for lost time.
Natsuki: It feels so nice just to let go, and cry…
I’ve started to look back on who I was, all the things I did, and think myself a fool. Exactly what senseless price was I fighting so hard to keep intact?
And how do I fight to protect peaceful days I’ve now found?
I hear a creak from the pier outside.
Footsteps.
In an instant, my heart leaps up from the bleak depths to which it had sunk, and pounds vitally in my chest.
ATRI: I’m baaaaaak! ♪
As soon as ATRI slams open the cabin door, she flings her shopping bag onto the bed and throws herself at me.
Natsuki: H-Hey now! Calm down…
ATRI: Hehehe, I’ve spent so much of today away from you, though! I need a good, close-up does of Natsuki-san!
ATRI: Did you miss me?
She bounces up and down, her adorable little cowlick bobbing as she grins up at me.
Natsuki: I-I can tell from that smile that you don’t need me to answer that.
ATRI: Hehe, I know how lonely you get. Without me here to keep you company, you even end up crying.
Natsuki: …
So it’s that obvious?
ATRI: You’ve got to be hungry, right? In that case, I’ll put my high-performance culinary skills to good use and make you a feast fit for a king!
Natsuki: Or not.
ATRI: What!? You can’t just cut me down like that! Where did the sweet mood we had going go!?
Natsuki: I really appreciate the sentiment, but please allow me to refuse. I value my stomach.
ATRI: But the only food we’ve got is stuff that would need cooking.
Peeking inside the shopping bag, I find little else expect minced beef and onions.
ATRI: The butcher asked me if I was “the young professor’s girl,” and gave me a discount. ♪
You’re famous, Natsuki-san!
Natsuki: Okay, I’ll get cooking.
ATRI: No way! This is my territory!
When I try to walk to the kitchen, ATRI stands before me and pushes me back with the strength of a sumo wrestler.
As ominous it sounds, it seems like tonight I have no choice but to eat ATRI’s creations.
In the kitchen, ATRI assumes an expression of utmost seriousness.
ATRI: First, knead the meet a little…
ATRI: Fifteen turns to the left, fifteen to the right…
ATRI: Eggs in the bowl, a little flour, a little salt… Form into a mass. Knead fifteen times. Flatten the air out, and turn five times.
Natsuki: (This is less like cooking, and more like some kind of science experiment.)
She gradually works her way through some kind of recipe in her mind, measuring weights and numbers with expect precision.
ATRI: Dinner’s ready!
ATRI: Could you clear the table for me? Be quick about it, or the food will go cold.
I sweep the assorted files littering the table onto the floor.
ATRI brings over a set of plates.
ATRI: There you go, Natsuki-san! How’s this?
I don’t even have to look at it to know exactly what it’s going to be.
I’ve been able to tell all along from the sweet smell wafting from the kitchen.
And yet, now that I’m actually looking at what she’s made first-hand, it’s even more wonderful than I could have expected.
She’s made a Hamburg steak with demiglace sauce, and a steamed vegetable salad.
Natsuki: This looks delicious…
ATRI: I know, right? Heh!
As someone without too much of an appetite, normally I can go entire days without eating if I’m concentrating on something else.
But with a dish like this in front of me, even I’m salivating.
Natsuki: Can I really eat this?
ATRI: Of course, go ahead!
Natsuki: Well, okay, here goes…
I eagerly cut out a piece of steak, and pop it in my mouth.
ATRI: Ba-dump ba-dump…
Natsuki: It’s great!
ATRI: Really?
Natsuki: Yeah. It’s as tasty as the ones I used to have in reataurants in the big city.
ATRI: I did it… really did it, President Minamo!
Natsuki: You learned this in the cooking club?
ATRI: Yeah! President Minamo and the other girls taught me everything-how to make the steak, how to season it, the proper cooking time.
Natsuki: That must have been hard for you to learn all of that…
ATRI: Not at all! I just wanted to be able to feed you something nice so much.
I feel the sincerity in her words.
Robots can’t lie, after all. Even someone as untrusting as me can’t really doubt her.
Natsuki: It really is delicious. Thank you.
ATRI: Ehehe, yayy, you actually complimented me!
It really must have been difficult for her to get this good. Compared to studying, she’ pretty useless at anything this delicate.
I wolf down the wonderful plate in front of me, savoring every mouthful with the pride of a parent eating their child’s first meal.
ATRI watches me with a broad smile the whole time.
ATRI: You’ve got a bit of sauce on your cheek.
Natsuki: Where? Can you wipe it off for me?
ATRI: Oh you, you’re such a spoiled kid, Natsuki-san.
She wipes it off with her finger, and laps up the sauce.
I turn away, my face tinged red.
ATRI: By the way, do you have any plans for tomorrow?
Natsuki: Umm, nothing in particular.
ATRI: Then would you like to go somewhere, just the two of us?
Natsuki: Okay then. Where do you want to go?
That “somewhere” is suspiciously vague. For a robot to ask something like that, she’d have to have some particular objective in mind.
ATRI: Anywhere is fine with me. I just want to go somewhere where the two of us can relax.
Natsuki: …Well, okay then.
ATRI giggles cutely.
ATRI: Ehehe… I can’t wait. ♪
She fidgets bashfully, bouncing up and down on her heels.
The next day, we wake up a little late.
We make ourselves a light breakfast, and go through our usual teeth-brushing rouline.
Before long I’m ready to go out. Now I’m simply waiting for ATRI to finish preparing our lunches.
ATRI: There we go, all done! ♪
She happily closes the lunchboxes, and smile over at me.

Just like we decided last night, we’re about to head out to spend the day together.
We have no clear destination in mind.
All we’ve planned is that we’re going to have a relaxing day.
Natsuki: Okay, let’s get going.
ATRI: Ah, wait just one second.
ATRI trots over to the calendar, and crosses off another day.
Eighteen days left…
ATRI: Right, let’s go.
Natsuki: Okay…
ATRI: Hmmhmmhmhmmm. ♪
As always, ATRI holds my hand as we walk and kicks up her feet with each step, showing off her shoes.
That little tuft of hair bounces on the top of her head.
Natsuki: Those shoes are starting to look pretty scruffy.
ATRI: That just shows how hard I’m working to be your leg!
She says that with her voice full of pride.
Although she might look like just a cute girl, ATRI’s strong enough to break through a concrete floor with a pickaxe. Those shoes are probably being worn down faster than they normally would.
Natsuki: Where should we go first?
ATRI: Umm…
She pulls a piece of paper our of her dress pocket, and starts looking over it.
Natsuki: What are you reading?
ATRI: It’s a secret!
She hurriedly puts away the mysterious note.
ATRI: One of the fundamental activities appears to be going shopping.
Fundamental activities? Of what?
I don’t have a clue what she means by that, but I may as well go along with her idea.
On the weekends, the market is rather lively.
There are even stalls open that aren’t here during the week.
We walk hand-in-hand through the crowds, perusing everyone’s wares.
Store owners call out to us, shouting “Good morning, professor”, and “You two are looking cute as always!”
I try to keep my conversations with people as short as possible, so I know very little about the lives of anyone here. They, however, seem to know all about us.
A lot of the shouts are specifically for ATRI. “You’re so cute today, ATRI!”, “You’re with the professor today?”, and so on. People seem surprised, since she’s been without me so much lately.

Natsuki: No, they all just think you’re cute. Everyone at school likes you more than me, too.
ATRI gets along with everyone there, even the students that I hardly talk to apart from to teach them.

He’s selling sticks of fruit, mostly pineapple and melon, carved into cylinders and arranged on skewers.

ATRI: Mmn… *munch* *munch*!

Given how much shorter than me she is, I’d have to stoop just to bite it. It’d be embarrassing to have everyone see that…
Natsuki: (…Who cares about that, though? Am I really going to let this little slice of happiness escape just our of embarrassment?)

Natsuki: Wow, it really is tart…

Natsuki: It’s still delicious, though.

Natsuki: (Hmm, should we go into a café or something? We did just eat that fruit, though.)
Although we’d originally planned to just wander around without any kind of plan today, somehow the knowledge that this is a “date” has changed the atmosphere.

Natsuki: (Gah, if I start panicking just because this is a date, what kind of man will she think I am?)
I don’s know much about romance, but I’ve heard enough stories to know that girls don’t like men who can’t keep themselves together.
Knowing that I’m on a date with the girl I love for the very first time, even if she probably doesn’t quite understand the situation, weight heavily on my mind.
Staring nervously down into the ground, I’m hit by a sudden idea.
Natsuki: Ah, I know! Let’s go and look at some shoes.
ATRI: Oh? Okay then.
We make our way to one of the shoe stalls in the market that sell pairs a young girl might like.
In front, racks are lined with sneakers, heels, and fancy leather shoes.

I sign.
ATRI: Umm…?
This is supposed to be a date. I just wanted to treat ATRI like a normal girl, not a robot.

Natsuki: So you want those ones?

They’re a pair of sandals, with a wooden base with a slightly raised heel and a leather strap.
I’d struggle to call these “practical” or “functional.”

A stylish pair of sandals like these really would be a perfect fit on those delicate feet of hers.

We leave the market, and then the residential area as a whole.
After a short walk, we find ourselves on the island’s edge.
She’s lead me to and old park atop a hill.
Half of the area is submerged, but a part on the upper side of the slope still sticks out of the sea. On it are bench and a few things for children to play on.
Natsuki: I’m surprised that you know about a place like this.
I’ve never even seen this park before, having been the kind of child who hardly left the house.
ATRI: Hehe, I’ve collected some useful information from a few sources.
I see her glance down at that piece of paper again.
Natsuki: Ah, so Minamo?
ATRI: Among others, yes.
By which I assume she means the cooking club.
Natsuki: (Seems like they gave her some pretty good advice…)
This park seems like it used to be a raised spot where you could get a good view of the sea. Now, you can see all the way to the horizon.
The waves are lapping at the playthings that have been partially swallowed by the sea. It’s a rather uncanny sight.
ATRI: Okay, Let’s have our lunches.
I’ve really worked up an appetite on the way here.
ATRI sits on the bench and starts to take the lunch boxes out of her bag.
ATRI: There we go.
Inside, I see… Hamburg steak sandwiches, grilled meat squashed between two slices of toasted bread.

Putting them in a sandwich is at least a new spin on it. That’s enough for me.
ATRI: Hehe, well, okay then. Eat up!
Natsuki: Gladly. *munch*…
Natsuki: Hngh! Hurk! *cough* *cough*!
ATRI: Natsuki-san, what’s wrong!?
Natsuki: I-It’s nothing…
ATRI: It doesn’t look like nothing! You’re crying…
ATRI: reaches out a hand to wipe away my tears.
Natsuki: It’s just, err, so tasty that I got a little emotional.
ATRI: Hmm… Cyber-eyes, engage! Zoom, and enhance!

Natsuki: It’s fine, really! This just makes it more… stimulating!
I stuff the sandwich into my mouth even as the spiciness makes my nose run.
To be honest, even with that intense mustardy tang, it’s still delicious.
ATRI: Ahh… I just wanted to make you happy, and I’ve gone and messed it up…
ATRI pulls the remaining sandwiches apart and wipes off some of the mustard.
Natsuki: Not everything has to be perfect, you know. I prefer them like this, if anything.
ATRI: …What does that mean?
ATRI forward at me with a disbelieving pout. It’s like she’s looking at a madman.
I’m going to have to convince her.
Natsuki: It seems like you’ve put more soul into it this way.
ATRI: More… soul?
Natsuki: Yeah.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: ATRI?
ATRI: …You’re a strange person, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: I’m going to choose to take that as a compliment.
I chuckle.
I’m getting more than used to these cute little misunderstandings.
Natsuki: I’m not lying about these being tasty, by the way. Did you think that adding mustard would make it a little different to dinner last night?
ATRI: What a fantastic deduction, Natsuki-san! You really are smart.
ATRI: Can I eat some too?
Natsuki: Yeah, you should always enjoy the fruit of your own labor.
ATRI: Mmm, *chomp*… It’s pretty spicy, but it’s still tasty.
ATRI: I really made this, just for Natsuki-san…
ATRI falls silent as she eats her way through the sandwich.
ATRI: I’ve got it! I will call the sandwiches I make for you “Natsuki-san’s Miracle”!
Natsuki: What, all of them? That might get a little confusing.
ATRI: I’ll just have to add an identification number to each one. Let’s call these Mirace-001.
Well, that’s one solution…
We spend an awfully long time simply sitting there, relaxing as we eat much and sip tea. Even so, there’s still a lot of daylight left.
I while away the time sitting on the bench reading a book.
Instead of my usual engineering texts or academic papers, today I’m perusing a children’s book Ririka recommended to me.
I have a little trouble following along with all of the strange, crazy twists of fantasy novels like this, but it’s surprisingly fun when I get used to it.
All the while, ATRI is amusing herself.
ATRI: Ahaha, it’s so cold.
ATRI: Natsuki-san, come over here! It feels so nice in the water!
She splashes through the water submerging the lower half of the park, shoes in hand.
The gentle waves glimmer in the afternoon sun, the spray framing her in sparking light.
ATRI: Are you listening to me, Natsuki-san?
Natsuki: Yeah, yeah…
ATRI: Grr… Take this! ♪
ATRI kicks up a huge splash in my direction.
Natsuki: Hey…!
ATRI: Hahaha! C’mon, come over here! ♪
Natsuki: You’ll regret saying that…!
I throw off my shoes, and rush over to her without even picking up my walking stick.
I scoop up a handful of water and throw it over her.
ATRI: Ahhh!
ATRI: Grr, you’ve done it now! Take this! And this! ♪
Natsuki: Hurk!
ATRI: Haha, what a silly face!

Many decades ago, at the height of humanity’s prosperity, humans even walked on the moon. When the seas began to rise, a plan to build a base on its surface was already underway.
It was meant to be a staging post for exploration of other planets, and even humans spreading into space, but matters on earth suddenly became more pressing. Abandoned up in the stars, the project now seems like nothing but a faraway dream.

Natsuki: …No, no no. Calm yourself, Natsuki. Even if, as her master, you have every right to read her logs, she did say…

Instead of the usual music programme, it’s playing a talk show.
Radio DJ: Our next postcard comes in from ‘Choppy!’

Radio: I’ve always heard the first kiss tastes like lemon, but mine… It tasted of garlic! He’d been to an Italian restaurant just before he came to meet me!
Radio DJ: Hoo boy, that’s a real hum-dinger! I’m guessin’ he though he wasn’t gonna get any that night!
The show goes on with the DJ pleading the boyfriend’s case.

I wonder how she felt about it…
I need to read it.

Natsuki: (There! She has written about it!)

I kissed Natsuki-san. Kiss, definition: A show of affection, often between human lovers, performed by pressing together both party’s lips. I am unable to ascertain the meaning of this action.
I was unsure of how to respond, but I approximated a reaction based on the materials loaned to me by Minamo. Natsuki-san did not appear to find this reaction unnaturalConclusion:
I selected the appropriate reaction.
Natsuki: …Huh?
My blood runs cold.
Natsuki: What… What is this?

All of those little moments, the sweet and innocent times we spent together, every single thing is written here… Written in words that make my heart freeze.
I read on. I have to.
On the way to school, he told me that he ‘loved’ me. I replied that I ‘loved’ him too.
However, I was able to determine from Catherine’s class that the meaning of ‘love’ that I had transmitted to him contrary to that intended by Natsuki-san. Conclusion: Error in evaluation.
My reply had not been in line with Natsuki-san’s expectations.
Action: In accordance with newly learned data, I have recorded in my internal database that Natsuki-san’s definition of love with respect to me is one of romantic love
New evaluation: Natsuki-san desired to form a romantic bond with me. Further simulation was required. Action: In order to fulfill this desire, I employed a falsehood.
Content: /”…Even after that, I want to stay with you.
“Simulations indicated this would be the desired response.
Evaluation: Natsuki-san did not appear to find this response unnatural. Reaction correlated to expected response based on emotional simulation based on learned data.
Conclusion: Natsuki-san was satisfied.
My hands are shaking.
The walls seem to twist and warp around me.
Natsuki: It was all fake…
The log falls to the floor.
The heavy thud resounds in the silence.
ATRI: …
ATRI slowly raises her head to look at me.
ATRI: Hmm… Natsuki-san?

ATRI: Hehehe… You’ll hug me to sleep again tonight, won’t you? We’re lovers now, after all.

She freezes up, an expression of bewilderment etched on her face.
Until now, I would have looked at her pausing like this and just assumed she was confused.
I know the truth now. Faced with an unrecognized emotional pattern, she’s running emotional simulations and working out the best option to take.
ATRI: …
She notices the notebook.
ATRI: Hey! Have you been reading my logs!?

Natsuki: That’s enough. Stop that.

ATRI: …
A robot cannot disobey a human.
In an instant, her cute expression sinks into a blank void, like an emotionless mask.
That’s her response.
Her response to my order, and her confirmation of what I said. If she had real emotions, she would have continued to argue with me as she always does, lively and lovely.
But there is no heart in ATRI.
Natsuki: You feel nothing at all, don’t you?
ATRI: I am not equipped with the prerequisite functionality to experience emotion.
Natsuki: …It was all an act, wasn’t it?

ATRI: I observe humans, learn from them, use my learned knowledge to perform simulations, and output action accordingly.

Natsuki: Even…

If I could rip into my chest and crush my raw heart…

I told her that I’d make her happy.

ATRI is a robot, built to serve humans. The answer that makes her master the most satisfied must be the best answer for her.
I almost feel touched. She’s been working so hard to read my emotions, and select the response that would make me the happiest.
But all of that was just so she wouldn’t be scrapped…

School. The cooking club. The days spent together with me. Every page is filled with detailed recordings of the past weeks, cold and dispassionate.

ATRI: Soon, I will cease operation.
Humanoids have a limited lifespan.
Just like for humans, death is unavoidable.
And for ATRI, that day is approaching. ATRI has been struggling to wake up because her body is starting to break down.
The way that her eyes went dull this morning is a common sign that a Humanoid is close to complete systematic shutdown.
Even before then, I had a suspicion that it was coming. Her eyes just confirmed it.
I glance over at the calendar.
Natsuki: You said that you’d stay with me even after the time came… You just said that to make me happy, didn’t you?
She nods.
ATRI: It was not my true intention, but if it is what you wish, that is what I will do.
For a Humanoid, death means the cessation of their mental faculties.
Their brains can’t be refurbished, and their memories can’t be transferred to another storage system.
You may wonder why a robot needs to die. The answer is that is was simply an ethical issue.
People would have feared and hated a being that looks like a human but is, for all intents and purposes, immortal.
Humanity may well have even lost its position as the dominant special on the planet.
As a result, it was made a legal obligation that all humanoids were programmed to have a limited lifespan-designed obsolescence.
It would be wasteful to simply scrap their bodies, though.
So rather than having their bodies degrade and die, it was decided that their minds would die instead.
If their memories were entirely erased, their bodies could be reused. They’d be like an entirely different person.
So what ATRI is telling me, essentially, is that she’s willing to stay with me, but not as herself—she would have the same body, but an entirely different mind.
ATRI: My intention was for you to sell my body, and buy an appropriately high-performance leg to replaced me.
ATRI: I estimated that that will provide you the optimum amount of happiness.

I don’t know why, but I don’t even cry.
After I lost my mother and my leg in that crash, I was sent to rest at my mother’s old home.
They said I should go somewhere quiet and peaceful to rest.
It was a beautiful coastal town, where a gentle sea breeze always blew.
The endless, changeless days soothed me as I coped with the shock of loss.
But though I did not show it on the surface, I kept a great well of despair built up deep inside of me.
Even as I struggled with the pain and the sadness, my father did not come to see me even once.
I realized her had abandoned me, and knowing this, I chose to die.
I remember the view from that clifftop was breathtaking.
Just an endless horizon.
My wheelchair creaks as I wheel it up the unpaved path.
The cliff isn’t high enough to kill anybody who falls from it on impact.
But below it is nothing but deep blue sea. If I fall from here in my wheelchair, no one can save me.
I want this to be the last thing I see before I die.
My mother always used to take me here when we went for walks. It’s a place that’s so full of happy memories for me.
Natsuki: …Huh?
There’s already someone standing on the precipice.
Her sliver still hair flutters in the wind, glowing gold in the soft light of the sunset.
She’s beautiful.
She seems to be four or five years older than I am. She’s taller than me, yet somehow her face seems so innocent compared to mine.
She’s standing right on the edge.

I wail and sob as I pour my heart out. I have no idea what pain spilled from my mouth, but I’m sure it was full of love for my mother, pleas for my father, and hate for my grandmother.

Natsuki: “Concept for humankind migrating to floating cities”… ”Plan for self-sustaining seastead”… “Prototype construction”…
A “seastead” is an artificial floating island, on which human settlements are built.
In a manner of speaking, my ship is my own seastead. It has the benefit of being able to adapt to rising and falling sea levels.
These plans, however, are for something much, much larger than this boat. These seems to detail a floating island that could carry an entire town.
These kind of projects are pretty common, and some examples of seasteads have already been built.
My grandmother’s plan has one big difference, however: Self-sustainability. The seastead would contain everything necessary to support a full community without needing to important supplies.
It would be an artificial island on a scale previously unheard of, equipped with systems to manufacture food and water and recycle waste.
Like the Garden of Eden, it would be an entirely new starting point for humanity.
I never knew my grandmother was involved with such an important project.
But that’s not the thing I’m surprised about the most.

The photographs tracking the construction of the first prototype instantly take me back to that time…

ATRI is sleeping alone in the bed.

So far, she has obeyed that perfectly.

Although her expression is completely blank, we’re still holding hands as we always do. ATRI is still my “leg,” no matter what the situation is between us.

Catherine: Looking forward to summer vacation? I bet you are. Well, before that, we’re having end-of-term exams.
Everyone cries out in despair.
It’s the sound of a class that’s swelled to almost thirty students having their hearts broken.
Ryuuji: Aww man, tests are so lame!
Yoko: I know, right!

That’s the day of the rocket launch…

ATRI scuttles busily from table to table.

ATRI’s grades have risen to become the best among all of the students. She’s been helping out the other students while I’ve been out of the classroom.

Natsuki: Maybe a little.

Just as I ordered her to, she acts completely normal around everyone else. It’s hard for me to respond to her fake feelings the way I used to, though.

Ryuuji: …

After school, Ryuuji takes me into the market to the candy store he regularly hangs out at.
We sit on the bench, sipping on room-temperature cola.
Ryuuji: Aww man, I wish we had some proper cold drinks around here!
When it’s this lukewarm, the sweetness of the cola sticks unpleasantly in your throat.
After a couple of gulps, Ryuuji starts up a conversation.

I was surprised to hear that, but maybe now that the launch has been confirmed their costs have gone somehow.
Natsuki: I suppose he’s trying to make up for never doing anything else father-like in his life.
Natsuki: He just wants to assuage his guilt…
As much as I understand that, I no longer have the energy to put up any direct resistance.
Ryuuji: Well, that just shows how strongly he feels about you, doesn’t it? The man’s not gonna feel guilty towards some one he doesn’t care about.
Natsuki: …
He might be right. As much as I don’t want to admit it, I’ve started to understand just a little about how my father must feel.
He’s just trying to do exactly what I said I had to…
Natsuki: I have to save the world.
Natsuki: If I can’t save the world, how can I be saved?
He suddenly lost his wife, and his son was gravely injured.
When assailed with such an unreasonable quick of fate, a person has to find a way keep on going, lest they completely fall apart.
Maybe my father feels he needs to save the world in order to keep from breaking down, even if it means discarding his family.
If he can’t, it would be a betrayal of his lost wife.
Natsuki: …I don’t want to go back to The Academy.

He grins, and reaches out to rustle my hair.
Ryuuji: You’re a real cutie, Natsu.
Natsuki: H-Hey, stop that.
As embarrassing as I find the way he fools arounds with me, I can’t help but smile back.
I’m finally used to life here in this town.
I’m not going to throw away the happiness I’ve found here to go back to The Academy.

Ryuuji doesn’t say it, but I can tell he really was worried that I was just revolting against my father’s wishes.
Ryuuji: I’m glad that you wanna stick around, though. I don’t want my best bud skipping out on me!
He smiles, and takes a swig of cola.
Looking at that relieved expression, resolve wells up in my heart.
Natsuki: Ryuuji, there’s something I want to talk to you about.

Natsuki: Well, it’s what she did. I found the notes from its construction in her files. She worked with some organization to build it, but their factories have long sunk.
Ryuuji: So is it, like, some kind of weapon? Like a secret base full of missiles or something?
Natsuki: You’ve watched too many old movies. The island’s a prototype, meant to show that it’s possible to create an entirely self-sustaining seastead.
Natsuki: They called it”Eden.”
Natsuki: My grandmother theorized in the course of her oceanographic research that there would be mass sea level rises, and she started researching how humanity could live long after that.
Ryuuji: Man, your family’s really something else. Dad builds rockets, Gran builds islands…
Ryuuji: But why do you wanna go there? Thinking of carrying on her research or something?
Natsuki: I want to take ATRI there.
Natsuki: She received some kind of last order from my grandmother, and I want her to be able to fulfill it.

Ryuuji: Can’t count on anyone but you best bud, right? Well, in that case, I’m not gonna turn you down.

Natsuki: As soon as possible. We don’t have much time.
Ryuuji: Gotcha. Well, as soon as we’re finished with exams, we’ll set out.
That will be the start of summer break, which sounds perfect to me.
It does mean wasting another few precious days beforehand…
Ryuuji: ATRI’s late, isn’t she?
Natsuki: She should be back soon…
She went off on her own to get ingredients for dinner.
No sooner does Ryuuji mention her than she comes tottering along the street, holding her shopping bags. Rather than coming over to us, however, she trots over to the butcher’s stall.
ATRI: Beef please!

I watch the two of them go at each other with a smile, but inwardly there’s a tinge of sadness in my heart. Out of the corner of my eye, I notice a strange figure.
Someone: …
Being a man who spends most of my time cooped up in my ship, there are a lot of people in this town I don’t know.
And yet, there’s something particular uncanny about that person…

When we return to the ship, ATRI takes the shopping bags into the kitchen.

When I fall silent, so does ATRI. She makes no attempt to speak unless spoken to.
Being around her like this makes my chest tighten agonizingly. I end up wanting more than anything to see those bounding emotions she used to express, even if they merely were a façade.
But it’s no use. I just have to accept that this is the true face of a Humanoid.
Natsuki: (The only reason I told her that I loved her was that I thought she had a heart that could love me back.)
That’s all meaningless now, past events that may as well not have happened.
As I chew on the delicious food, tears start to well in my eyes. The subtle, beautiful flavors make it all the more painful.

I’m so happy to hear her concerned voice that I can only let out the smallest of words.

Gritting my teeth, I snatch the pillow from her, and throw it down on the floor with the “NO” side upwards.
ATRI: Ah, so that is your answer… Unfortunate.
For a moment I think I see the ghost of a frown cross her face, but I know that that’s just my imagination.
ATRI slowly picks up the pillow, and returns it to the bed.

Ryuuji’s face goes ever so slightly pale, but I remain entirely composed.

Attached to it is a rope, linking it to buoy on the surface.
It’s a market that will indicate the position of this cable, should we need it.
Naturally, this is another item from my grandmother’s old stock of research equipment. We’ve used buoys like this in our salvage work a few times.

ATRI winds her rope around the cable and the weight, tying the two together.
This won’t just stop the cable drifting off, it’ll also allow us to pull it up with the crane should we need to.
