Inside the cabin, Ryuuji is listening to the radio at an absurd volume.
He’s had his head practically attached to the thing all day.
Because he only has a battery-powered radio at home, he’s extremely envious of my wind-powered ship where I hardly have to scrimp and save on power.
Natsuki: Eden will probably be drifting in from the west. The fog should come soon…
I can feel the moist sea air climbing portentously to my skin already.
ATRI: I see.
Natsuki: It’s almost time… Time for you to carry out your last order.
It has to be the place, surely. I don’t know why it would be calling out to her otherwise.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: Aren’t you happy?
ATRI: I do not know how to experience “happiness.”
Natsuki: …Of course.
Natsuki: Can I ask you something?
ATRI: Yes?
Natsuki: You knew all this time that you were going to shut down, didn’t you?
ATRI: Affirmative.
Natsuki: So… Why did you want to study?
ATRI: I do not understand the meaning of your question.
Natsuki: Well, when your brain shuts down, you’ll lose all of your memories, won’t you? So what’s the point in going to school, and learning everything you have?
No human that knew their death was approaching would choose to spend their days at school. It would be pointless, surely?
ATRI: I desired to become a more useful Humanoid.
Natsuki: By, say, learning to cook so that you could feed me?
She nods.
Humanoids are programmed to do everything they can to be of greatest use to their masters…
Natsuki: But what about everything else you studied? Was that just to make me happier, as your teacher?
She shakes her head strongly.
ATRI: That was also to achieve a greater degree of usefulness.
Natsuki: Why, though? What were you going to use all of that knowledge for?
ATRI: I do not know when my accrued knowledge will become useful. I have not been equipped with the necessary faculties to achieve precognition.
There’s something about the coldness of her words that makes my blood boil.
Natsuki: Then it’s pointless, surely? When do you think the stuff you’ve been learning is ever going to come in useful? After all, you’re about to…
ATRI: I am about to… What?
Natsuki: …Nothing. I’m sorry. I didn’t mean to say it like that.
ATRI: I do not mind. I do not have feelings to hurt. Please say that you were going to say.
Natsuki: I don’t want to say it.
ATRI: Understood.
…
With no other words to say, we both fall silent.
Then, almost as if she’s trying to prove her usefulness by making conversation, ATRI raises a question.
ATRI: Why aren’t you going to return to The Academy?
Natsuki: This again… I told you. I prefer living here.
ATRI: Will you be able to save the world while living here?
Natsuki: No, and I don’t plan to try.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: Everyone has their limits. Maybe it’s okay if everyone just tries to save everyone in, say, a five meter radius. If every person did the same, wouldn’t that mean everyone was saved?
Natsuki: I’ve always lived so selfishly, but recently, I’ve realized that nothing is going to change if I keep being like that.
Natsuki: You might not understand, but for humans, this is happiness.
ATRI: That is not happiness.
Natsuki: Who are you to judge what happiness is?
ATRI: It is not a judgement. It is an objective observation. This is not happiness.
Natsuki: I’ll decide what makes me happy, thanks.
ATRI: I perceive that if you insist that your current situation is one of happiness, happiness would be a meaningless concept.
Natsuki: Then what would be happiness for me!?
ATRI: Well-
Ryuuji: Hey, Natsu!
Ryuuji pops his head out of the cabin door.
Ryuuji: Wanna warm up the dinners Minamo made us? I’m getting hungry in here.
Natsuki: Okay, let’s do that.
I stop the ship, and drop the anchor.
It look like this is where we’ll be staying for the night.
Natsuki: Let’s go, ATRI.
ATRI: Okay! ♪
No longer alone, ATRI reverts to her usual, carefree smile.
I wake in the night to discover the ship swaying on the waves.
It’s still dark outside. But the clock says that the sun should be rising right about now.
The ship creaks as it rolls on the waves.
Natsuki: We must have hit a rough patch…
I put on my prosthetic leg, and start to stand up from the bed.
ATRI: Natsuki-san.
ATRI is already awake.
ATRI: I hear something calling to me from close by.
Exiting the cabin, we find the ship enveloped in a fog so thick that it completely blots out the morning light.
In the gloom shines one single spot of red light.
The ship rocks as the heavy waves batter its sides.
ATRI grabs me and keeps me upright.
Natsuki: Thanks…
ATRI: There is no need to thank me. This is my duty.
An enormous shadow looms out of the fog.
A colossal shape, unfathomably dark and unnerving.
Natsuki: That’s Eden…
ATRI: It’s calling to me… The signal is definitely coming from there.
Natsuki: Ryuuji! Wake up!
Ryuuji: Dude, what’s going on…?
He comes out onto the deck, rubbing his bleary eyes.
Ryuuji: Whoa! What the hell!?
Natsuki: That’s Eden. It’s come to us!
It passes by right in front of where we’re anchored.
Natsuki: It’s faster than I thought it would be. We’ll have to chase it down!
Ryuuji: Hold on a sec, we should pull back first!
I stumble across the deck as it rocks in the island’s wake, like a tiny, fragile leaf.
I hoist the anchor, and fire up the engine.
Ryuuji: Wait, look at that!
The island is surrounded by a ring of billowing waves, as if it’s trying to prevent anything coming close.
Natsuki: The waves are coming from Eden itself…
With the seas rolling so intensely, making land on the island seems like it could be impossible.
But we have no choice but to try.
Ryuuji: Dude, we’re seriously gonna capsize at this rate! We should pull back and think about this!
Natsuki: We don’t have time for that! If we let it get away, it might be days before we find it again!
Ryuuji: Then we’ll just have to wait! That’s fine, right?
Natsuki: No, it’s not! ATRI could die before we see it again!
Ryuuji: What!?
Natsuki: Argh!
I’m thrown from the control cabin as a wave crashes right into the side of the ship.
I look up from the deck to see that Eden is so close that it’s almost scraping hulls with my ship.
Ryuuji: That thing’s gonna hit us! We need to get out of here!
Ryuuji rushes to the cabin and tries to slam the engines into reverse.
Natsuki: Wait, we might still be able to land on it! I have to save ATRI!
ATRI: It’s too dangerous, Natsuki-san!
Another wave rocks the ship.
The shock rips my hands from the railings, and my body goes flying through the air.
ATRI: Natsuki-san!?
Time seems to freeze. I stare into that red light shining through the fog.
Until I hit the water, and sink into the inky blackness.
I awaken to the sound of twittering birds.
There’s a strange, tingling pain in my cheeks.
Natsuki: Ugh…
I open my eyes to a blue sky so bright that it’s almost blinging.
Natsuki: What happened…?
I move my head, and feel the sensation of grass against my skin.
I slowly sit up.
Natsuki: Where am I…?
A completely alien landscape stretches out before me.
The sky is a brilliant cyan, hanging over a field of flowers.
Little birds twitter and flitter around me.
Looking around, I set my eyes on a particular striking object.
Natsuki: A tower? Is that… a lighthouse?
The strangely-shaped tower stretches up into the cloudless sky.
It’s swaying, back and forth…
Natsuki: No, wait. It’s the ground that’s moving.
Amidist the twittering of the birds, I can hear the sound of waves.
I try to stand up, but I instantly realize that something’s missing.
Natsuki: My prosthetic’s gone…
I can’t see anything around me that looks-like it.
My clothes and my hair are a little damp.
Finally, the last few moments before I passed out come back to me.
Natsuki: I got thrown off of the ship…
All I can remember after that is sinking into the sea.
I have no idea how I ended up here, but this must be Eden.
My prosthetic probably came off when I fell overboard, but somehow I made it here on one leg.
It’s lucky that I have plenty of experience doing things without my prosthetic on, like when I get out of the shower or immediately after waking up. I should be able to move around perfectly well like this.
Natsuki: What a beautiful island…
Standing up, I take in my surroundings properly.
A wide expanse of green stretches out in front of me, broken only by a clear, sparkling stream flowing through it. Birds frolic in the skies.
This place is like some kind of paradise.
If I was a religious man, I would have thought that I’d drowned in the ocean and gone to heaven.
I approach the stream, and scoop up some water in my hands.
Natsuki: It seems so pure…
Where is it flowing from?
This island cant’ be that big. This can’t all just be rainwater, can it?
I follow the stream up in search of its source.
The water seems to be flowing out of some kind of man-made building.
Natsuki: What is this building? It doesn’t seem to just be some kind of huge water purifier…
I examine its walls, finding a little green insect clinging to it.
Natsuki: There are bugs on this island?
The birds here must survive by feeding on these.
I’m no insectologist, but this bug doesn’t seem to be any kind I’ve ever seen before. I’m curious about how the ecosystem on this island functions.
Peering closely at it, I notice something odd.
Natsuki: It’s eating the wall…
I know that snails can eat concrete and incorporate it into their shells, but this insect has no such protection.
There’s something coming out of its rear, though.
It seems like it’s digesting the concrete and excreting some kind of glue…
I pick the insect up in my fingers.
Natsuki: I knew it. This isn’t a real bug.
It’s just a robot in the shape of one.
Natsuki: Is it repairing the walls!?
It seems like it’s chewing up damaged parts and filling them in with whatever it’s excreting.
Looking around, I can see a lot of similar insects on the building’s walls.
Natsuki: These must be some kind of automatic maintenance robots…
While on the surface this island may look like an all-natural paradise, it’s evidently being kept in that state by the power of science.
Natsuki: This building is making the fresh water too… This is amazing. This place is incredible!
Natsuki: Right, ATRI!?
In my excitement I instinctively call out for her, only to realize that she’s not there.
Natsuki: Oh yeah, where is she…?
ATRI: Natsuki-san!?
She jumped into the sea after me.
Natsuki: ATRI!
I hope around frantically, searching for her.
Natsuki: No way. She didn’t sink, did she…?
Natsuki: ATRIIIIIIII!
Natsuki: Whoa!
My foot catches on something, and I go tumbling across the soft grass.
Natsuki: Owww…
ATRI: Are you okay, Natsuki-san?
Natsuki: ATRI!?
The thing I tripped over is a prone ATRI, staring motionlessly up into the sky.
ATRI: Good… You’re safe…
Natsuki: ATRI, are you all right!? Are you damaged!?
I examine her body, but I can’t find any sign of external injuries.
ATRI: I am fin. I simply expended a large amount of energy rescuing you, and have had to temporarily power down several systems.
Natsuki: You can’t swim, can you? How did you manage to save me?
ATRI: I learned to swim in our gym class.
ATRI: You just have to scoop the water with your hands, and move your feet like a dolphin’s tail.
She weakly tries to demonstrate, but it seems like she can hardly move.
ATRI: If I take a big breath, I can achieve a certain degree of buoyancy. Then it is merely a case of using my hands and feet properly.
Natsuki: So you grabbed me out of the ocean, and pulled me up here?
ATRI: Affirmative.
Natsuki: Why would you risk drowning like that?
ATRI: Oh? Do I need a reason to act in your aid, Natsuki-san?
Natsuki: …Well, I guess it’s my fault you ended up like this.
ATRI: Indeed. Please refrain from reckless action in future.
Relief and regret welling in my chest, tears start to stream down my cheek and fall down onto ATRI’s face.
She reaches up to gently wlpe my eyes.
ATRI: Humans cry so easily. Or are you simply cleaning the sea water out of your optical receptors?
Natsuki: I’m just so glad that you’re safe…
I grab ATRI and pull her into an embrace, crying on her shoulder.
She frowns, but she offers no resistance.
Natsuki: What happened to the ship?
ATRI: I do not know.
Looking out to sea, I see nothing but an expanse of blue.
The fog has completely cleared up, but the waters around the island are as rough as they were when hit the ship.
Natsuki: Does it make the waves deliberately, to stop people making land here?
It’s certainly possible, but it could also be just a problem with the construction. This island is only a prototype, after all.
ATRI: …Oh?
A little bird comes down to sit on the unmoving ATRI’s head, peering curiously at her face.
ATRI: Do you have some business with me?
Natsuki: I think it wants to play with you…
ATRI: It’s quite rude of it to sit on my face…
She reaches up to weakly stroke the bird’s back.
More birds soon join their friend, sitting on her chest and shoulders.
Natsuki: Seems like you’re popular around here.
ATRI: It’s ever so slightly annoying.
Despite this, she doesn’t shoo them away.
While she entertains her new friends, I start to strip off a branch to make a walking stick.
ATRI: You don’t need that. I’m here.
Natsuki: You can’t even more. Just rest here, and I’ll take a look around.
Propping myself up on the stick, I start to examine our surroundings.
In the center of the island is the large building. I can’t tell if there’s a way in, or what exactly it is.
Natsuki: If you looked at just this, you’d think this was some kind of military installation.
It could pass for some kind of secret weapon.
Surrounding it, however, is a verdant field of green.
This island is teeming with birds, insects, and those odd little maintenance robots.
Natsuki: There’s fruit on the trees, and fresh water, so it doesn’t seem like we’re in danger of starving…
The island is truly astounding to look at, almost paradise, and I soon realize exactly what is keeping it so beautiful.
Just like the robotic insects I saw before, there are all manner of mechanical creatures seemingly keeping the island running.
They come in all kind of shapes, from butterflies to spiders.
Natsuki: ATRI…
ATRI: Welcome back, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: Look, I found you a new friend.
I hold out one of the insects in front of her.
ATRI: Oh… It’s another robot.
Natsuki: Yeah. All of the robots here seem to have some kind of role in maintaining the island.
Natsuki: Some of them repair buildings, some of them seem to be keeping the grass and the trees healthy… And when they die, they’re buried in the soil and decompose.
ATRI: So it’s a system that use multiple types of maintenance robots to maintain the ecosystem?
By splitting up their roles like this, this huge island can be maintained by nothing more than these tiny machines.
Natsuki: These seem so much more technologically-advanced than anything I’ve been before. Just when did my grandmother invent these?
My grandmother was still young in the era when humanity was at its technological peak. She must have been predicting the sea rises even that long ago…
ATRI: …
The only other thing this advanced I’ve ever come across is ATRI herself. A Humanoid like her would be practically impossible to build from scratch these days.
Natsuki: This island is incredible…
ATRI: It is quite high performance…
Natsuki: Err, what’s up with you?
ATRI: Nothing. I’m just tired, so I’m going to sleep.
Lying on the grass, she instantly goes into sleep mode.
It’s probably my imagination again, but she almost seems to be pouting.
ATRI doesn’t open her eyes again until sunset.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: Ah, you’re awake. Good morning.
ATRI: Is it morning? It appears to be sunset to me.
Natsuki: Yeah, it’s the evening.
ATRI: Then why did you say “good morning”? You should have said “good evening” or something.
Natsuki: Well, I guess I won’t make that joke again…
ATRI: By the way, why are you naked?
Natsuki: My clothes are drying. And I’m not naked, I’ve just taken my shirt off.
ATRI: And why am I naked?
Natsuki: Your clothes are drying too.
ATRI: Oh, so you stripped me? I believe that would legally be viewed as sexual harassment.
Natsuki: You sleep like that next to me every night, and you’re worried about it now?
ATRI: …Did you do something to me while I was asleep?
Natsuki: No comment.
ATRI: Ah. Yes, definitely sexual harassment.
Natsuki: I was joking, I didn’t do anything. I’m not pathetic enough to play around with a sleeping girl.
ATRI: I wonder about that. You seem more pathetic than you used to be.
ATRI: When you were a child, you had a much stronger will.
Natsuki: I’ve just learned to see the world for how it really is.
Natsuki: Can you stand up?
ATRI: If necessary, yes, but I have yet to recover all of my functionality.
Natsuki: Okay, well, don’t push yourself.
Natsuki: I went and picked some fruit. Eat up.
ATRI: …
ATRI looks at me with dissatisfaction.
Natsuki: Don’t you want any?
ATRI: I do not require the nutrition.
Natsuki: Delicious things make you happy, though, don’t they? Come on…
I peel one of the fruits and hold it in front of her mouth.
ATRI just stares at it.
ATRI: Did you harvest these? Without your leg?
Natsuki: Well, I didn’t have much else to do when you were dozing away.
ATRI: And now you’re peeling them for me.
Natsuki: Well, that part’s easy.
ATRI: This is somewhat harmful to my pride as a robot.
ATRI: This should have been my duty… I suppose I really am a piece of scrap.
Natsuki: It can’t be helped in this situation. Looking after his robot is a master’s job, right?
Just like I clean her teeth every morning, in fact.
ATRI: If only I really were a military robot, I wouldn’t have ended up like this…
She takes a chomp of the fruit. Her face contorts.
ATRI: It’s really sour… But it’s tasty.
Natsuki: There’s still a lot on the trees over there. We’ll probably be having them tomorrow too.
ATRI: I will pick them tomorrow. I should be fully functional by then.
Natsuki: …
ATRI: …Why do you look so disappointed?
Natsuki: I was just thinking that I quite like you like this.
ATRI: What, of no use whatsoever?
Natsuki: You’re always helping me out, but I never get the chance to be the one caring for you. It’s nice to dote on you for a change.
ATRI: I’m not sure I would describe this as “doting”…
ATRI: But very well, if that is what you wish.
ATRI: Come a little closer, please.
Natsuki: Huh?
I lean in.
ATRI throws her arms around me and pulls me into an embrace.
ATRI: This is my best spoiled baby Natsuki impression. I don’t know how else to be doted on.
Natsuki: Do I really act like this?
ATRI: Affirmative.
She says nothing else. She merely closes her eyes.
Natsuki: Are you going to sleep again?
ATRI: …Ahhhhn.
ATRI opens her mouth wide, and I gladly shove another piece of fruit in it.
Natsuki: You like that?
ATRI: It’s lovely and sour…
Natsuki: Good. There’s plenty where that came from, so eat up and get better.
ATRI: I cannot actually process the nutrition they contain, so eating more would be meaningless. I’m sorry, I really am a piece of scrap…
There’s something so adorable about her apologies that I can’t help but peel another piece to give to her.
By nightfall, she seems to have perked up a little.
Natsuki: It’s getting a little cold, isn’t it?
The wind is bringing an ocean chill onto the island.
I put my now-dry shirt back on.
Natsuki: You should put your clothes on too, ATRI.
ATRI: If that is what you wish.
Natsuki: It very much is.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: …What’s with that look?
ATRI: I have been taught that human expressions can be used as a silent substitute for questions. In this case, “Do you really not want me lying here half-naked and defenseless any more?”
Natsuki: Err, no. Put some clothes no.
She begrudgingly slips into her dress.
Natsuki: So, have you remembered what your last order was?
ATRI: falls silent for a moment, frowning.
ATRI: Sorry, I can’t remember it at all.
Natsuki: Do you know anything about this island? My grandmother had something that she wanted you to do here.
ATRI: I can’t remember anything…
Natsuki: Huh, right…
I have to admit that I’d assumed that just arriving on the island would revive her memories, but I guess that was naïve of me.
Natsuki: I suppose we’ll have to go exploring, and find exactly what you’re supposed to do here.
Natsuki: When the sun comes up tomorrow, we’ll look for a way inside that building.
ATRI: Umm…
Natsuki: What?
ATRI: Would it be acceptable if I had you dote on me a little more?
Natsuki: Fine by me, but it’s not like you to ask for that.
I suppose she just feels vulnerable when she’s weak like this.
That said, that would only be a learned response, right? She shouldn’t be showing her fake emotions around me.
ATRI: The only way I can aid you currently is to let you dote on me.
Natsuki: What, and you think I want to do that?
ATRI: When you did it earlier, you did not appear to be displeased.
Natsuki: …
Things have been so awkward between the two of us these past few days.
Ever since I discovered that ATRI’s emotions are just simulations, I haven’t really known how to act around her.
Natsuki: Well, if that’s what you want, then I will gladly oblige.
ATRI: Okay then…
She leans against me, and I wrap my arms around her.
Natsuki: I’m really nice warm like this.
ATRI: Me too…
ATRI: My temperature is lower than normal due to my reduced power output… I can feel your body warmth, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: I suppose I’ll have to keep you good and warm, then.
ATRI: That will have no effect on my functionality, so it is unnecessary.
That’s a surprisingly cold reaction…
Natsuki: Well, I suppose I won’t, then.
I try to pull away, but ATRI holds onto me.
ATRI: Please don’t stop.
Natsuki: Why not? You said yourself, it’s unnecessary.
ATRI: It is indeed unnecessary, but… Being by your side is soothing.
Natsuki: So it feels good?
ATRI: I do not feel anything. I do not have a heart.
She replies apologetically.
Natsuki: Well, I don’t care about that. I still think that you have emotions, and I still love you.
Natsuki: So I’m more than happy to hold you like this.
ATRI: You’re quite easy to please if this is all it takes. Very efficient.
Natsuki: That’s just how high-performance you are. Just being close to you soothes my soul.
ATRI: So I am high performance…
Mumbling with seeming surprise, she clings onto my arm.
Everything falls silent.
The birds have returned to their nests, and the only sound that can be heard is the occasional rustles of maintenance robots in the grass.
In the distance, the waves wash against the island’s shore.
It’s a beautiful, peaceful night.
So tranquil that I could almost forget that we were shipwrecked here.
Natsuki: Maybe the two of us should just live on this island…
I mumble idly to myself.
Natsuki: This place is like paradise. We’ve got all the food and water we could ever need.
Natsuki: I can see why they called this Eden. You really could start a whole new life here. A whole new world, even.
It feels just like we’re a modern Adam and Eve…
ATRI: …I may be high performance, but unfortunately I am not equipped with the necessary functionality for reproduction.
ATRI: You would require at least one more human to start a new society.
Natsuki: The world’s going to be swallowed up by the sea anyway. We don’t have to worry about that kind of thing.
Any new world we started would just end anyway.
ATRI: …
ATRI: Have we been saved?
Natsuki: Maybe. This feeling of relief, this peace… Maybe this is salvation.
This surely must be the most serene experience I’ve had since the day I lost my leg.
ATRI: So simply accepting our doom and living lazily here until we die would be salvation.
ATRI: My database makes a clear distinction between the worlds “paradise” and “graveyard,” but it seems you do not.
ATRI: Should you not, if you have any life left, strive to survive as best you can?
The harshness of her words instantly brings me back to reality.
Natsuki: Is that why you spent the last days before you stop functioning studying?
Soon, her memories will completely break down. While she may physically be able to go on living, the current ATRI may as well be dead.
Everything in her mind will be lost, including everything she’s studied.
Natsuki: Isn’t that pointless? You understand that, right?
ATRI: Is something pointless because you will one day die? Does that not make all of human life pointless?
ATRI: In that case it would be more efficient for all humans to simply die.
That would make all of human progress meaningless, wouldn’t it?
Even the Earth itself will one day be swallowed by the sun. The universe too will one day reach its heat death.
But… But I…
Natsuki: I can’t live that way, ATRI. Even though I know that you’re going to be leaving me so soon…
I don’t know how I’m going to go on when she isn’t here.
I can hardly remember how l lived before she came back into my life.
ATRI: May I ask a question?
Natsuki: Yeah?
ATRI: You believe that me studying even though I am going to die is pointless?
Natsuki: Well, of course.
ATRI: In that case, why did you tell me that you love me?
Natsuki: What…?
ATRI: You had already realized that I was dying, hadn’t you? So what was the point in telling me you loved me, if our love could only ever last a few days?
ATRI turns and stares at me.
As expressionless as her face is, there’s something approaching expectation in her eyes.
Natsuki: Well, yeah, I’d worked it out.
Natsuki: But still… I had to tell you. I needed you to know that I love you.
Natsuki: I don’t know why. I’ve never felt this way about someone before.
I lived my whole life thinking I could never fall in love with anyone, but when she came into my life, it felt like she reawakened that natural instinct within me.
ATRI: Let me add a further question. Was that pointless?
Natsuki: What, telling you how I felt?
She nods.
After I told her I loved her, we lived out those few wonderful days as boyfriend and girlfriend.
Of course, it was all just a façade, a robot’s attempt at giving me the illusion of happiness.
I want to tell her it wasn’t all meaningless, but… I don’t have the confidence in my own words to say it.
Natsuki: (I knew that the end was coming for her, and I just wanted her last days to be happy…)
I wanted to make her dying days have some kind of meaning.
She looked so happy…
I thought I’d managed to bring some joy to her short life.
It was only when I read those logs that I realized what a folly that was.
I was just doing it for my own satisfaction. I was letting my fantasies of the good life completely take over me.
Natsuki: It… It might have been pointless after all, yes.
ATRI: I see…
ATRI: I would not make the same judgement. The time I spent as your lover was of much greater utility than the time that I was not.
ATRI: That has not changed. The time I spend together with you is infinitely preferable to the time we are apart.
Natsuki: I wish I could be as strong as you, ATRI…
ATRI: I am merely a robot. I do not have feelings to hurt.
Natsuki: I look at you, and all I can see is a cute girl.
ATRI: …
ATRI: That was how my outer shell was designed. It is not a functionality I selected or achieved myself.
ATRI: I would like to attain an existence that is valued for the knowledge and skills I have acquired.
With her dying day approaching, she really wants to fulfill that wish.
It’s such a pure and noble motive, compared to my desperation…
Natsuki: Can I ask you a question, ATRI?
ATRI: Of course.
Natsuki: It’s about what we were talking about on the ship, when we were interrupted. What do you think happiness would be for me?
She believes that I’m not happy currently.
She was about to explain what she meant before…
ATRI: A future.
ATRI: You have so much more time left on this earth compared to me. There are so many things you could create.
ATRI: Please don’t throw away your future.
Natsuki: So you’re telling me to go back to The Academy?
She nods.
Natsuki: You think that’s where my future lies?
ATRI: Affirmative.
ATRI: You said it yourself. If you don’t save the world, you won’t be saved.
Natsuki: Haha…
I turn away, laughing a hollow laugh.
Natsuki: ATRI… Are you trying to make fun of me? Or is it just an accident?
ATRI: Oh?
Natsuki: I’m not the person you and everyone else seems to think I am.
ATRI: What do you mean by that?
Natsuki: I was a dropout. A dropout, ATRI!
ATRI: You were…?
Natsuki: Yeah. A dropout, but too proud to admit it.
ATRI: But weren’t you a top student at The Academy?
Natsuki: I was at first. I looked down on all of the other pupils, and even the teachers.
Natsuki: I even thought that I could be the one teaching them.
Natsuki: But that was only the first couple of years.
Natsuki: The more I studied, the more I understand the truth… That there’s no way to save the world.
Natsuki: And the harder I worked to convince myself otherwise, the more it drained me. My grades started to nosedive.
Natsuki: That was when everyone started to pay me back for all of the arrogance and disregard I’d shown them.
Natsuki: I lost my scholarship, and suddenly I had to pay my way again. I had no money, and I had to sell my cybernetic leg.
Natsuki: I though that if I just tried my hardest again, I could get back to the top of the class.
Natsuki: But I just didn’t have the concentration to do that. Not without an objective, not without any reason to go on.
Natsuki: I couldn’t keep on living there, with no leg, and no friends.
When I sold my cybernetic leg, my phantom pain came back. Every night was hell.
Exhausted, my grades dropped so how you could count my test scores on your fingers.
Natsuki: Even if I did go back to the Academy, there’s no guarantee that I could return to the level of achievement I had initially.
Natsuki: I’m… I’m scared to find out just how worthless I really am.
That, above everything else, was why I ran away from The Academy.
Not being able to afford the tuition fees was nothing but an excuse. I was using that and my leg to justify giving up.
While I turn over those regrets in my mind, ATRI mumbles dejectedly.
ATRI: So there’s no way to save the world…
ATRI: And no way to save me…
Natsuki: ATRI…?
Her normally blank and expressionless face is tinged with sadness.
Natsuki: Don’t worry. Even if I can’t save the world, I can at least save you.
Natsuki: That’s why we’ve come to this island.
ATRI: I see…
For all the upheaval we’ve experienced, one thing hasn’t changed-I want to make ATRI happy.
ATRI: What am I…?
A heartbreakingly forlorn look passes over her blank face.
After a night with ATRI in my arms, morning arrives. I set out to explore the island again.
This time, a fully-rested ATRI accompanies me, lending me her shoulder to lean on.
ATRI: I suppose that I actually am a highly useful, helpful robot after all.
She expressionlessly looks down on the tiny maintenance robots busily working away on the island.
Natsuki: (Does she really feel the need to compete with other machines?)
In the light of the morning, I’m astounded again by the island’s construction.
Natsuki: This place is pretty huge. There’s so much foliage that I’m not sure we can even walk over to the other side.
Natsuki: I can’t believe that my grandmother had a hand in this…
Although I say that, but if there’s one person who could make this island, it would be her.
It probably took her and her team years to gradually build it up, just like how the robotic insects build their hives.
But just building it wouldn’t be enough. Floating out here on the ocean, eventually something would come along and damage it somehow. To prevent that, she had to make it self-sustaining.
She truly was trying to create an entirely new way for humanity to live on after all of our lands sunk beneath the seas.
Natsuki: So this is an option too…
When I was studying at The Academy, I only ever considered possibilities such as somehow stopping the sea rise, or colonizing space.
The received wisdom was that seasteading wasn’t practical. I never even considered it.
But my grandmother was the kind of person who would pour absolutely everything to her research.
Even her closet relatives though she was eccentric. Mad, even.
Natsuki: ATRI, are you sensing anything?
ATRI: I can feel something calling me from that direction…
With ATRI guiding me, we manage to find what appears to be an entrance to the concrete building.
Unfortunately, it’s not just locked. It’s blocked up by a huge wall of tree roots.
Natsuki: Dammit, we’re never going to be able to get in there.
I try to pull away some of the roots, but they don’t budge.
Natsuki: ATRI, do you think you can do anything about this?
ATRI: …
Natsuki: ATRI?
ATRI: If I disengage my power limiter, I could break through. However, I would not recommend it.
Natsuki: Why not?
ATRI: It may leave me without the necessary power required to assist in getting off the island.
Natsuki: You want to fulfill your old master’s last wish though, don’t you? The key to that could be right behind this door.
ATRI: That is true. However, I cannot allow you to come to harm in the process.
Natsuki: I’m not going to die here or anything. I could live forever on this island.
ATRI: Do you intend to live here alone even after I have ceased functioning?
Natsuki: …
Without ATRI, I wouldn’t care what happened to me.
Natsuki: Well, we don’t have any way off of the island for now. We should prioritize doing what we can here.
ATRI: …
ATRI silently places a hand on the wall of the building.
The instant she touches it, it shudders.
Natsuki: It opened? How did you do that?
ATRI: I simply commanded it to open.
I’m just about able to squeeze through the roots covering the door, and get inside.
ATRI joins me, and we examine our surroundings.
Inside is a large, strangely tranquil hall. It almost feels like a temple.
Natsuki: What is this room?
ATRI: It is the central control room. All of Eden’s functions are controlled from here.
Unexpectedly, ATRI is able to answer my question.
Natsuki: How do you know that?
ATRI: I am connected to it.
Natsuki: What?
ATRI: I have linked with the central control computer. It has welcomed me, as Eden’s core.
Natsuki: It… “Welcomed” you?
I don’t understand a word she’s saying.
ATRI: Allow me to show you some schematics.
Lights flicker across the walls. A second later, an enormous window-like object opens up above us.
Natsuki: Wow… That’s a hologram!
You don’t see them at all these days. The only one I’ve ever seen was at The Academy, an old relic from humanity’s peak.
On the hologram is displayed a detailed plan of what looks like the entire island.
Natsuki: Are you… Eden’s control unit?
ATRI: …
ATRI: I’m remembering something… Something about the role Yachigusa Nonko gave to me.
Natsuki: Really? What do you remember?
ATRI: Nonko created me to manage the systems on this island.
ATRI: An ecosystem this advanced cannot be maintained by a normal A.I.
Natsuki: So this was her last order…
I mumble to myself as I survey the holograms.
Natsuki: Wait a second. This part here, does this mean…?
The instant I realize the meaning of what I’m reading, my blood runs cold.
Natsuki: You’ll…
ATRI: Yes, I will die.
My grandmother didn’t need ATRI herself-just her brain.
ATRI is supposed to connect to the computer in this room, and meld with it.
However, her brain is soon to cease functioning. It won’t be enough for her just to plug herself into the island.
The capsule that I found ATRI in was a cold sleep chamber, capable of preventing a Humanoid’s lifespan winding down as long as it’s inside of it.
And here, there’s an almost identical device.
This won’t merely preserve her, though. It will meld ATRI’s mind with the island, and completely remove everything that makes her her.
In other words… It’s a machine made to kill ATRI.
Natsuki: So this is what you wanted for her? You evil old hag!
My shout reverberates through the hall.
Natsuki: ATRI, I am your master now! You don’t have to obey her orders!
ATRI: That is correct.
Her reply is swift and calm.
ATRI: However, there is one correction I must make.
Natsuki: What?
ATRI: According to the memory data I have just recovered, Yachigusa Nonko was never my master.
ATRI: This is not the final order that I have been seeking.
Natsuki: You… What?
Natsuki: So who is your master?
ATRI: I do not know.
My head is spinning with confusion. How can this possibly be? It wasn’t my grandmother that gave her her final order?
Everything I thought I knew, from the objective we’ve been striving for to the level of technology we’re dealing with, has completely changed.
Natsuki: I just don’t understand… What did we even come here for!?
As I hold my head in my hands, trying not to scream, the window in front of me changes.
ATRI has brought up a new screen. It’s a view of the sea.
ATRI: This is a live video.
Natsuki: …The ship! Is that Ryuuji?
ATRI: Audio analysis indicates the presence of loud, energetic, late-twentieth-century rock music.
ATRI: I detect no signs of intelligent life. Therefore it is logical to assume that Ryuuji is indeed on board.
Natsuki: He must have followed along to try and save us!
ATRI: Let’s go.
Natsuki: Shouldn’t we investigate all of the computer files here first?
ATRI: I must prioritize your wellbeing first.
ATRI takes me by the hand, and starts to lead me out.
ATRI: There it is. That is our ship.
ATRI: HEEEEEYYY!
ATRI: Grr, it seems like he’s not paying attention. Natsuki-san, hand me your stick.
She grabs the stick off of me suddenly.
She pulls off her dress, and wrap it around the end.
She waves her makeshift white flag energetically over her head.
ATRI: RYUUJI, YOU DUMMY!
ATRI: Natsuki-san, can you help me with this?
Natsuki: RYUUJIIIII!
ATRI: No, no, you have to add the “dummy” part too… Ah, it looks like he’s seen us. The ship’s turned this way.
She hands me her stick and puts her dress back on.
ATRI: It’s time to go.
Natsuki: Right…
ATRI: Please refrain from being too upset until we are safely back on the ship.
In accordance with the three laws of robotics that they are programmed with, Humanoids must prioritize the safety of human beings.
ATRI could never put her own gain ahead of my safety.
Natsuki: How are we going to get onto the ship?
The island is thronged as always by high waves, stopping anything coming near.
ATRI: …I have no idea.
Natsuki: …
Thankfully, I have put a least a little thought into how to conquer this problem.
Natsuki: We just have to float a little way out to sea, and wait for him to pick us up.
ATRI: Understood.
Natsuki: We’ll need to use the vines from that tree, as well as this stick.
ATRI: How will those help us float?
Natsuki: You’ll see. Just do what I tell you.
I pick off some of the tree’s thick, study vines, and wind them together into a rope.
I tie them around one end of the stick.
Natsuki: I need you to throw this, like a javelin, somewhere close to the ship.
ATRI: I’ll gave it a try.
ATRI: …Hup!
The stick files through the air, all the way to the ship’s port side.
Ryuuji seemingly catches on quickly, and ties the vine rope around a ring buoy.
I pull the rope back, bringing the ring along with it.
ATRI: Ohh, I see.
Natsuki: While you were sleeping, I though of a few ways to get off the island.
This one in particular was for the occasion that Ryuuji was able to help us.
I had other plans in case a fishing boat came by, or, in the worst case, we would have had to fashion a raft from the trees and vines here.
Natsuki: Okay, let’s go.
ATRI: Affirmative.
I put the ring around ATRI’s waist, take a deep breath, and hold her close to me.
Natsuki: Don’t let go of me, okay?
ATRI: Do not worry. I have already learned the proper procedure for this.
ATRI starts to run toward the shore, and leaps…
Natsuki: (I told her not to let go, dammit!)
I desperately flail around, just managing to grab a hold of her leg.
Natsuki: Mmnph!?
Natsuki: Hahh, hahh…
ATRI: I’m sorry, Natsuki-san. My hand slipped.
Natsuki: I thought I was going to die, you idiot!
ATRI: Yes, I am indeed a idiot piece of scrap. I apologize.
Ryuuji: Natsu! ATRI!
Ryuuji brings the ship closer, and throws us a rope.
He pulls up ATRI first, and the two then work together to lift me up onto the deck.
Natsuki: Phew, that was close…
Flopping over like freshly-fished salmon, I close my eyes and take a moment to appreciate the simple joy of being alive.
Ryuuji: Man, I’m so glad that you guys are safe… I thought you’d drowned!
Natsuki: Thanks. You’re a lifesaver, literally.
Ryuuji: No need to thank me! This is what best buds do, right, looking out for each other?
Seeing him simple at me with tears in his eyes, my bosom wells with happiness.
Not even a single person at The Academy would have cried for me like this.
While we sit on the deck recovering, the island floats off into the distance.
Natsuki: (We didn’t find any way of saving ATRI…)
ATRI: …Ah!
Natsuki: What’s wrong?
ATRI: I can’t find it…
She turns pale, frantically patting away at the pocket of dress.
ATRI: I don’t have my logbook.
Natsuki: Did you drop it on the island?
Maybe it was when she used her dress as a flag. The worst-case scenario would be that it came out in the water…
ATRI: I’d logged every single thing every day since you salvaged me…
Natsuki: Well, we’ll have to go and buy you a new one.
ATRI: Okay…
ATRI stares out dejectedly at the island as it retreats toward the horizon.
Natsuki: Oh, it’s morning…
Since returning from Eden, I’ve been struggling my way through more of my grandmother’s files.
I must have dropped off while reading them again. Well, it’s some sleep, at least.
I need to know exactly what Eden is, and the only way I’m going to find that out from what few files she left on the ship is to read them front to back.
Natsuki: (This might be entirely pointless, but I have to try…)_
No matter how much I search, I can’t find anything that seems to relate to ATRI’s last order. I don’t even know who her previous master was.
At that moment, I hear her rustle on the bed behind me.
ATRI: Good morning… Hahhh…
Natsuki: Looks like you’re a little more lively this morning.
ATRI: I’ll go and get breakfast ready… Mmn…?
She stands up and starts to wobble her way over to the kitchen.
Natsuki: ATRI? ATRI!?
ATRI: Owww… Sorry, I was still half-asleep.
Natsuki: You’ve not hurt, are you?
ATRI: My body is sturdier than a human’s. A fall like this isn’t enough to damage me.
Natsuki: That’s not an excuse to bumble around carelessly…
She sets about cooking as if nothing had happened.
I’ve never been one for big breakfasts. Before ATRI came into my life, I’d normally have just a piece of fruit, or even nothing at all.
These days, however, there’s always the smell of bacon wafting through the air in the morning to stimulate my appetite.
I clear all of the scattered papers off of the table.
Natsuki: …Huh?
Natsuki: ATRI, is something burning?
ATRI: Hmm… It does smell like it.
She quickly turns off the heat, taken by surprise.
After a moment, she comes over holding a plate.
Natsuki: Wow… What on earth happened?
ATRI: Hm…?
Atop the plate is an grim, ominous mass of burned… something.
Natsuki: It’s been a long time since you messed up a meal like this. What, did you try a recipe you haven’t cooked before?
ATRI: …
Natsuki: It’s not a big deal, I suppose. It’s kind of nostalgic, in a way.
It takes me back to that first day ATRI came to my ship.
Just like then, today’s menu is a bacon that resembles shards of burnt bark from a tree that’s been struck by lightning, and toast you could kill a man with.
I’m amazed that I manage to finish it, albeit only by forcing it down my throat with a constant stream of water.
ATRI: How was it?
Natsuki: It was… delicious. Umm, thanks.
ATRI: …
ATRI: This is the first time you’ve ever complimented my cooking. I’m normally so bad at it that I start to worry that I’m really some kind or military robot or something.
Natsuki: What are you talking about? I’ve complimented before, I’m sure I… Ah…
ATRI: Hm…?
Natsuki: Umm, it’s nothing. Forge it.
The conversation comes to an abrupt end, but an uneasy tension hangs in the air.
Feeling the need to say something, I try to ask something that I’ve been curious about.
Natsuki: So Yachigusa Nonko was never your master?
ATRI: Yachigusa Nonko… Who is that?
Natsuki: What? You said that you’d remember her. It’s this woman.
I show her a photograph form one of her files.
ATRI: Oh… Yes, that person was not my master.
Well, that’s a pretty firm answer.
A Humanoid never forgets its master. My grandmaster can’t have been ATRI’s.
Natsuki: Do you remember anything about her?
ATRI: Umm… Only that she was a horrible old bag.
Natsuki: Well, you’ve remembered the important things, I see.
This one detail being confirmed only leaves me with more questions.
Why was she in my grandmother’s storehouse?
What did she do before she ended up there?
And most obviously of all, who was her master?
Natsuki: (If she remember her master, maybe she’ll remember her final order too?)
It might just be the key we need to unlock the last parts of her memory.
Natsuki: Do you member anything at all about who your previous master was?
ATRI: …
A flash of sadness seems to pass across her face.
It sends a jolt of coldness through my body. It takes me back to that very first time we met.
When she was trying to kill herself…
ATRI: I think I may have been abandoned by my master.
Natsuki: Abandoned?
ATRI: Yes. I seem to remember my master disappearing.
Natsuki: Disappearing’ how? Was that when they gave you your final order?
ATRI: Excuse me for a second.
ATRI grabs my arm, and pulls me downward.
She holds my head closely against her chest.
Natsuki: H-Hang on a second…!
I flush red, but I can tell this is her trying to recreate a part of her lost memories. I can’t exactly stop her.
ATRI: They held me like this, and said something to me…
ATRI: But I have no recollection of what they said.
She lightly taps me on the head.
It seems like she’s still trying to remember something.
Natsuki: Do you know when this happened?
ATRI: All I can remember is that it was before I went to sleep under the sea… Ah!
ATRI: That’s right, it was around the time I first met you.
Natsuki: Really? Then what would make it eight years ago.
So she was abandoned by her master, and wanted to kill herself.
Did my grandmother take her in after that?
That cliff was close to her house, so it’s not beyond the realms of possibility.
But what happened to ATRI after that?
Natsuki: umm, ATRI, could you let go of me now?
ATRI: NO.
She squeezes me even more tightly against her chest.
ATRI: It’s been a long time since I held you like this. I don’t want to let you go.
Natsuki: …
It’s certainly not a request I feel like denying. I’m so sleep-deprived I could just doze off like this.
Natsuki: You’ve got club activities to go to, haven’t you?
Minamo stooped by yesterday to invite ATRI to some cooking club practice. Even summer vacation doesn’t stop Minamo.
ATRI: Oh yes.
Natsuki: Learn to make something nice, okay?
ATRI: Roger.
She reluctantly lets go of me.
We clean up our plates, and get ready to leave the ship. On the threshold, ATRI hesitates.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: What’s wrong?
ATRI: If I don’t have a notebook, I won’t be able to record any new recipes.
Natsuki: Oh yeah, you lost your last your last one. We’ll stop somewhere on the way to buy a new one.
ATRI: Thank you.
From the ship, we head to the market district.
The plan is to do a little shopping here, and then head to school to pick up our exam results.
Natsuki: I don’t really care about my own grades, but I’m curious to see how well you’ve done, ATRI.
ATRI: Hehehe, get ready for a big, high-performance surprise! Heh!
ATRI is as bright and lively as always in front of other people.
We pop inside the stationery shop.
ATRI: Hmm, which one should I pick?
She eagerly runs her eye over all of notebooks.
Natsuki: Why not just get the same kind we did before?
She’d decided on that one after some quite intense deliberation too.
ATRI: The same kind…?
She glances around the shop.
ATRI: I think I want a different one.
She begins to pick up each one in turn, and examine them closely.
Natsuki: I feel like this could take a while… I’m going to pop to the junk store, so come and meet me when you’ve decided.
ATRI: Okaaaay.
Handing her the money, I leave the store.
I’ve been hobbling around on my walking stick ever since I lost my prosthetic leg trying  to get to Eden.
I’ve never been more acutely aware of how lucky I am to have ATRI to help me walk than when I’m trying to stumble around on my own like this.
I slowly make my way to the junk shop deep in the back of the market.
Junk Shop Owner: Hey there lad. You came at just the right time, I was about to get in touch with you.
Natsuki: What about?
Junk Shop Owner: I’ve found someone who might wanna be buying that bot off you. Says he’s workin’ with some group who’s tryin’ to start up a new Humanoid business.
Junk Shop Owner: He’s got some backers givin’ him the fundin’ to research the tech, and he just needs a workin’ example. Said he doesn’t mind it being a recalled model. In fact, that’d be even better.
Natsuki: I thought I’d mentioned that I’m not going to be selling her.
I’d passed on the message to him when I made the decision to have ATRI stay with me.
Junk Shop Owner: Well, you might wanna at least have a chat, right?
Junk Shop Owner: She’s gonna be needin’ a reset soon, anyway.
A “reset”… Her current memories vanishing, in order words.
Junk Shop Owner: Judgin’ from when she was made, I’m surprised she hasn’t had one already.
Natsuki: Even so, I’m not selling her.
Junk Shop Owner: What use would it be, keeping her body around after she conks out?
Natsuki: Putting that aside, I wanted to ask you something. Why was ATRI’s particular model recalled anyway?
Junk Shop Owner: Umm, lemme see what the old files said…
He pulls out a folder of yellowing papers and flicks through them. It seems to be some kind of catalogue of all manner of Humanoids throughout the decades.
Junk Shop Owner: Huh, says here there was a fatal error in the programming. Caused some kinda accident.
Natsuki: An accident?
Junk Shop Owner: That’s all it says. No concrete details or anythin’.
I can imagine a few ways in which it might have happened. I have been thrown into sea by that piece of scrap multiple times.
If that kind of thing had happened at the height of the proliferation of Humanoids, it could have been huge new.
Natsuki: (Why was ATRI never recalled herself, though?)
PR disasters like recalls could ruin a manufacture’s business. They’d be so desperate to prevent further accidents that they’d take those robots back almost by force.
Did ATRI get spared simply because she was hidden in my grandmother’s storehouse?
Or maybe she was accompanying her on a research expedition out at sea.
My grandmother could have found her useful, and just refused to hand her back. No one would’ve been able to take that woman’s things without a fight.
Natsuki: (But she wasn’t ATRI’s master…)
Natsuki: When was the recall?
Junk Shop Owner: Hmm, thirty-one years ago, two years after model production started.
That’s long, long before I was born. The dates aren’t adding up here.
Junk Shop Owner: According’ to the specs, that model should have a lifespan of twenty-five years. She sure has lived a long time for a Humanoid.
Natsuki: Is it possible that she’s been reset once before, and had her memory modules swapped out?
Junk Shop Owner: What company’s gonna do that for a defective model?
In order to reuse a robot body that’s been reset, you’d need to have the whole cybernetic brain refreshed. It’s hard for anyone but the manufacture to do that.
Natsuki: (Even my grandmother probably couldn’t do that…)
She was just a marine geologist. As technologically-advanced as Eden is, I doubt she made the maintenance robots. There had to be someone on her team more experienced with robotics.
There’s a possibility that that someone could have modified ATRI, but unauthorized modification of a Humanoids is very, very illegal.
Natsuki: (If she had been reset, wouldn’t it logically work out that she’d still have several years left to live?)
You can’t believe how much I wish that was the truth.
Natsuki: Thanks for the information.
Junk Shop Owner: Give what I said a think, okay?
When I leave the store, ATRI is still nowhere to be seen.
Natsuki: Is she still choosing her notebook?
I turn onto the street where stationery shop is located to find her standing in the middle of the path.
Natsuki: Hey, ATRI. What are you standing there for? You’ll get in people’s way…
What…?
ATRI is stood frozen, seemingly halfway into a stride. It’s like she’s completely run out of power. People passing by stare at her in bemusement.
The light has completely faded from her eyes.
Natsuki: No way, you can’t…
Natsuki: Wake up! Store messing around like this! The calendar still hasn’t ran out yet!
A tiny red spark flicker up in her eyes.
ATRI: …Ah!
ATRI: Was just taking a little nap there… *schlurp*!
Slurping back a thick glob of drool, she glances around as if trying to work out where she is.
I clean her face off with a handkerchief.
Natsuki: You’ve been acting strange all morning. What’s wrong with you?
ATRI: I’m completely fine. Look, I’m feeling happy enough to dance! And a one, and a two…
She starts to twirl around in the middle of the street. It makes what just happened seem like some kind of uncanny pantomime.
Natsuki: Okay, okay, I get it. Stop that.
ATRI: Aww, I was just getting to the good part…
Natsuki: Did you get a notebook?
ATRI: Of course, look!
ATRI: I found one with the exactly right mix of functionality and price. I’m absolutely sure this is the perfect one!
She proudly flourishes in front of her… the exact same notebook as before.
ATRI: Have you done what you needed?
Natsuki: Yeah, I’m done.
ATRI: So, let’s go to school!
Natsuki: I need to stop by the library first. You go on ahead of me.
The town’s library was spared from the rising waves by being located high up on a hill, in the opposite direction to the school from here.
ATRI: Will you be okay on your own?
Natsuki: To be completely honest, I would prefer if you came with me.
ATRI: Ohh… you really are in spoiled baby mode today, aren’t you?
Natsuki: You’ve got club activities though, don’t you?
ATRI: Yes, and President Minamo gave me a real struggle session when I took those days off…
Natsuki: So you’ve got to go, right? Don’t worry about me.
ATRI: I’ll be extra sure to make it up to you later. I’ll be all over you as soon as I get home!
Natsuki: Can you not shout that kind of thing in public?
ATRI: Okay, Comrade ATRI, shipping out!
She give me an elaborate salute, and runs off toward the school.
Natsuki: Guess I should get going too…
I need to search for any kind of clues as to why ATRI’s model was recalled.
Ryuuji: Natsu!
Ryuuji comes toward me from the direction I’m walking.
Natsuki: Oh, hey.

A few days earlier, just after we’d returned from Eden…
Natsuki: Eden is a prototype of a floating city intended to support an entire self-sustaining ecosystem.
Natsuki: There’s a lot of things in my grandmother’s research that I initially thought were completely unrelated to that.
Natsuki: But I get the feeling that some of those might not be as unconnected as I thought.
Safely back on the ship, I set about explaining to Ryuuji something that’s been on my mind for the past couple of days.
Natsuki: For one thing, there’s the island’s electricity generation technology.
Natsuki: The whole island is acting like one huge hydroelectric power generator. I had a feeling about this when I saw how the waves around it move. They’re being sucked into a huge turbine.
That’s how it’s able to produce enough power to maintain all of the functions of the ecosystem.
Natsuki: And that undersea cable… It might just have been intended to link Eden to that mainland, and power the town.
Natsuki: My grandmother knew all about the sea rise could damage humanity’s infrastructure, so it’s only natural that she might come up with an idea like this.
Natsuki: Since that cable’s already connected, it’s likely that they experimented with using the prototype like that.
Natsuki: There’d have to be some kind of transformer substation to sync the power with the town’s grid. And they probably would have made sure to build it somewhere that wouldn’t end up underwater.
Natsuki: Is it possible that you could help me find somewhere around here like that?
With that, Ryuuji set about searching the town.
Ryuuji: So apparently some university worked on a project, and they built this. It’s just like you said.
The substation is near to the park on the top of the hill.
We’re accompanied by someone from the town hall, and the mayor-Minamo’s father.
Electrical infrastructure like this wouldn’t have been able to be built by private industries without local government permission, so naturally he knew all about it.
Natsuki: So basically, this was built so that the electricity coming from Eden could be wired up to the town grid.
Electricity has the unfortunate property of losing energy when transmitted over long distances. However, you can minimize the power loss by transmitting at a higher voltage.
Standard high-capacity lines carrying electricity from town to town run at voltages in the hundreds of thousands.
That voltage, of course, would fry any regular household appliance. It needs to be lowered considerably if it’s going to be of any practical use.
Which is where the transformer comes in.
Eden’s undersea power cable should be transmitting at a particularly high voltage, so the town would need a substation with a step-down transformer to handle the incoming energy.
As expected, this substation is attached to the cable.
The machinery is all still functioning.
Natsuki: I’m really surprised how quickly all of the adults started believing me about Eden. It seems such a ridiculous story at first hearing.
On the way back, Ryuuji lends me his shoulder and props me up.
Going through the series of events in my head, I can’t quite believe the mayor accepted a story based on the recollections of some children so easily.
The legendary phantom island being an experiment by Yachigusa Nonko, connected to the mainland by a cable that could power the whole town? Who would believe that?
Ryuuji: I guess that’s just the kinda weight “the young professor’s” words’ve got around here now, I guess.
Ryuuji: Since you brought light back to the school, everyone respects you, man.

Natsuki: …Well, if you say so.

There’s a good reason for his grin afterall. We’ve just landed ourselves one massive salvage job.
We’re going to be working with an electricity company to pull up and refit the undersea cable.
There’s probably many more broken segments of the cable town there aside from the one we found, and we’ll be charged with finding them and pulling them up.
And when they’ve been refurbished, we’ll be helping to lay them again.

Natsuki: Well, about that…

Natsuki: NO. Humanoid lifespans are as hard-set as our own.

Eden when he’s as upset as I am, he’s still worried about me first…

Natsuki: Ryuuji…
I can’t believe it. I’d convinced myself that I was going to be left completely alone when ATRI left… It’s a proposal that sounds so amazing, so life-changing, that I can hardly control the emotion welling up in my chest.
Natsuki: …I’ll think about it.
Ryuuji: Aww, c’mon, dude, don’t blueball me! This is one of those moments where you’re supposed to say “yes,” and we start bro-hugging, and bro-crying, and stuff…
He laughs, and jabs my shoulder.
Natsuki: Thank you, Ryuuji, for everything. For hanging around with a pathetic guy like me…
Ryuuji: Pssh, don’t give me that bull. I’m always counting on you, y’know, man.
Hands around each other’s shoulders, we slowly make our way back into town.
We say out goodbyes in the market, and I head to the library to search for clues about ATRI.
I need to work out what happened to her in the time since she was made, over thirty years ago, and that moment eight years ago when we met.
One route to finding some kind of thread to follow might be to look into her model’s backstory.
“What am I?”
Natsuki: …
Unfortunately, I come up with nothing. Her model was such an obscure, Iow-volume one that I can’t find any concrete details about it.
The only thing I have to go on are manufacturer’s specifications and vague references elsewhere.
My slow hobble means it’s already evening by the time I arrive at school.
Just coming this far is exhausting.
Natsuki: Jeez, I hope ATRI’s still here…
She knows that I’m coming. She surely wouldn’t have gone anywhere.

No matter how close a relationship we may form with them, one day they may become our enemies.

08/21/xx
Nonko gave me a duty. I am Eden’s central management system. I am part of a machine that will save the world. However, it is not time yet. I will be entering sleep mode until Eden is complete. While in the capsule, my body will not degrade. I will wait there to be awoken.

08/12/xx
Nonko came over to me while I was looking at the sea. She told me that I should come home. If I was found outside I would be captured and disassembled. It is dangerous to go outside.
08/08/xx
A boy spoke to me by the sea. He was in a wheelchair. He was missing his right leg.
I cannot destroy myself.
The boy refused to help me. He did not want to become a criminal. I accepted this as a logical position. I stopped him. Why did I do this?
In accordance with the three laws of robotics, I must always prioritize preserving human life over all else.
However, I can ascertain that I look this action for a different reason. It was commanded to by my master. If I was to allow him to commit suicide, I would be ignoring my master’s command. I cannot allow this contradiction. Perhaps I “wanted” to do this. The boy began to cry, and I comforted him.
I copied a technique used by my master. The boy stopped crying.
The boy said he would go to school.
He said; “I have to save the world.” I replied;
“Does the world include me?”
I want to know the meaning of “happiness.”
If I learn this, my master can be saved. Then I will be saved too. I have the suspicion that this boy may be my new master. However, I cannot be sure.
06/02/xx
“I want to talk to you, so wait for me in the place.” My master gave me that command. I waited, but she did not come.
This was because she was dead. In Humanoid terms, she had ceased to function.
Without my master, I have no purpose. Without a purpose, my existence is unnecessary. I am a defective model, created by mistake. I thus determine that it would be best for me to be destroyed.
05/29/xx
I am avoiding human contact. I will be disassembled if I am discovered. I do not understand why this is undesirable. My assessment is that it would be preferable for me to be destroyed.

06/02/xx
“I want to talk to you, so wait for me in that place I mentioned.” My master gave me that command. I waited, but she did not come. This was because she was dead. In Humanoid terms, she had ceased to function. Without my master, I have no purpose. Without a purpose, my existence is unnecessary. I am a defective model, created by mistake. I thus determine that it would be best for me to be destroyed.
Yasuda: My, how touching. But you are reading far too much emotion into nothing but standard Humanoid programming.
Natsuki: You’re saying I’m just feeling the same kind of empathy as we do for animals, or other objects?
Yasuda: Exactly.
Natsuki: Well, look a little closer.
Yasuda: Oh…?
Yasuda: “Dead”… How odd. The world is smudged. Why would that be?
Natsuki: It’s been blurred by her tears. When she realized what she was writing, she started to cry.
Yasuda: What nonsense… It was probably just a stray droplet of eye-cleaning fluid.
Natsuki: It’s not just there, though. Look at the other pages.
I read through the entire log in the truck on the way here.
It records in intricate, mechanical detail every single thing that happened to ATRI from her creation to the day she lost her memories.
Every single terrible thing she went through…
And yet, it’s all written with absolute dispassion. It almost seems cold and cruel.
It was only when I saw those small, seemingly insignificant marks that I realized.

We’re suddenly blinded by the lights turning on, and deafened by the sound of party poppers.

ATRI: Umm, no. My optical sensors could see you even in the dark.

ATRI: Heh, don’t underestimate how high performance my senses are!

ATRI: Okay!
Minamo: Aww yeah, let’s party! ♪
And thus the Crab Worshipper’s Association Summer Party-Err, ATRI’s birthday party begins.
There is, thankfully, a lot more food available than just crab.
Since everybody has each brought something along, there’s also a huge pile of candy and drinks.
Everyone sits around happily chatting, eating, and generally having fun.
Everyone has given their presents to ATRI, and now Ryuuji is busy strumming away on his guitar.
Ryuuji: Man, being able to power an amp and rock out is the best!
The school is one of the only places in the town that you can use anything electrical. The only other places use gasoline generators, which are extremely expensive to run.
Ryuuji twiddles away on his “axe,” as he for some reason calls it, enjoying the fuzzy sound of the amplifier.
Natsuki: We don’t have infinite power, you know. Be careful.
Ryuuji: I know, I know, dude.
It might not be infinite, but our generator is far more efficient than it was when we first made it. All of the improvements we’ve made should mean it can last the whole night.
We’ve also brought the piano back downstairs. A party needs music, after all.
Natsuki: Hmm, maybe I’ll play something too.
Ririka: Oooh, you’re going to give us a tune?
Ryuuji: Oh, sweet. Let’s jam, dude.
The two of us play together, surrounded by our happily-celebrating friends.
One person, however, is conspicuously absent.
ATRI: Crab… I love you, crab. You’re so delicious…
ATRI is still busy stuffing herself.

This is her birthday party, but also her farewell party. It’s a last, precious chance to see her off.
So many people want to say their goodbyes that soon we’re unable to fit everyone in one classroom.

Natsuki: Oh, is she still upset about that?
Serious-minded teacher, or feckless drunkard? I really don’t know what to make of her sometimes.
ATRI: Catherine? She’s been standing over there for a while now.
Catherine: …
ATRI points over at the door, where an eye can be seen peering through the gap.
Catherine: Gah!

ATRI: …

ATRI eagerly drags a blushing Catherine toward the classroom.

Somes adults are more difficult to deal with than kids.
When Minamo and Ryuuji initially told me their plan, I assumed this was just going to be a small gathering of only the people closest to ATRI.
That was, at least initially, the idea of things.
But instead it’s ended up being a party for the whole town.
In just the short time since I pulled up from the bottom of the ocean, the people here have accepted ATRI, and she’s become a figure they’ll all miss.

…

As soon as we’re a safe distance away, it goes arcing off into the sky with a whinnying whine.
Then, for a moment, all is silent.
An enormous spray of glimmering sparks lights up the night sky.
ATRI: Whoaaaa… It’s so pretty…
Ryuuji: Phew, that’s a bigger!
Ririka: Wowwwwwww!
Minamo: It’s so beautiful…
Catherine: …
It fizzles in the sky with the sound of a hundred little sparkles. It’s small compared to the kinds that I saw at festivals as a child, but that makes it all the more precious.
Everyone stares at it in wonder.
It lasts only a brief moment, before fading away as if it never existed.
Ryuuji: Ahh, that was a hell of a lot of fun. Guess we’ve gotta clean up now, though.
Catherine: Make sure everything’s completely out. Put all your sparklers and such in the bucket.
With everything used up, we start to clear the trash away.
ATRI stands staring into the jet black sky.
ATRI: …I always though that goodbye could only be sad.
Natsuki: Hmm?
ATRI: It’s still sad to see it end, but… That’s only because it’s been so fun.
ATRI: If none of this had happened, I would have felt neither of those things…
Even as she gazes out into the complete darkness, I can still see a brilliant sparkle in her eye.
ATRI: So I knew happiness all along…
Natsuki: …
ATRI has completely forgotten the conversation we shared at the bottom of the sea.
Everything I said, and what she told me-“I don’t want to die.”
But I think that tonight, she has finally understand what happiness is.
ATRI: I… I’ve loved this place.
Saying farewell is only sad because the time that she spent here was special.
She doesn’t seem to quite have realized the real sentiment that lies beyond those words-not wanting to die.
But at least she has, if only for a moment, truly experienced what it means to be happy.
And in that brief moment, the days she spent here, learning together with everyone, gained meaning.
Ririka: See ya, everyone!
Ryuuji: Night, guys!
Catherine: Take care on the way back, okay?
Minamo: Good night!
As everyone walks home, people gradually splinter off. Eventually, the only people left are Minamo, ATRI, and I. A hint of loneliness begins to seep into the air.
Soon comes the time for Minamo to leave us alone.
ATRI: Thank you for holding a party for me, Minamo.
ATRI: I’m happy that so many people wanted to celebrate my birth with me.
Minamo: I’m happy that we had the chance to, as well.
ATRI: Thank you for everything else you’ve done as well. You’ve always been so nice to me.
Minamo: Oh, there’s no need to thank me. It’s too early for that, anyway. You’re going to watch the rocket launch together with us, aren’t you?
ATRI: …
ATRI silently shakes her head.
Minamo: Huh…? Why not? Natsu-kun…?
Natsuki: Why not, ATRI?
She should have just enough time left to watch it.

Minamo throws her arms around ATRI and clings onto her.
Minamo: WAAAHHHHHH!

Natsuki: Well, of course she has. She’s sad that she has to say goodbye to you.
ATRI: …Having a heart really is a nuisance, isn’t it?
She sighs, and tears start to roll down her cheeks.
Notching them, she blinks as if trying to force them back.
She’s actually trying to control her emotions.
She’s even I learned to do that…
ATRI: There there, Minamo. Don’t cry…
Minamo: No way, I’m going to cry all night!

ATRI: He’s the kind of person who gets so focused on his goal that he can’t think of anything else. He’ll work himself so hard that he gets to the drink of breaking down.

Minamo wipes away her tears.
ATRI becomes me over. Looks like whatever secret business they’ve been doing is over.
Natsuki: What were you talking about?
I can’t help but be extremely curious.
ATRI: That’s confidential, girls-only.
Minamo: Y-Yep, top secret.
Minamo: Well, I’ll head home then. Goodnight, you two.
ATRI: Goodbye, Minamo.
Natsuki: Good night.
Minamo: …Bye bye!
She smiles at ATRI, and then quickly turns away, running off into the distance.
We set out on our way home. Our bodies tingles with the lingering excitement of the party, only tempered by the sadness of parting.
Natsuki: Tonight was really fun, wasn’t it?
If we return to the ship, the day will be over.
Our steps start to grow more and more languid, not wanting the night to end.
ATRI: …
ATRI stops, and pulls at my hand.
Natsuki: What’s wrong?
ATRI: There’s something I want to ask of you.
ATRI: …I want you to let me cease functioning before my time is over.
Natsuki: What…?
ATRI: When the time comes, I will forget everything. Everything about tonight, about Minamo, Ryuuji and Ririka, and everyone in the town… Everything about you.
ATRI: I don’t want that…
ATRI: So please…
ATRI: Destroy me before I forget it all.
The ship rocks atop the waves.
The wind is strong. It’s spinning the wind turbine so quickly that the radio is coming through loud and clear.
Radio: With two days left until the launch, the rocket’s engineering team is reporting that preparations are progressing according to plan…
Normally at this time of night there would be mellow classical music playing, but tonight it’s a special news bulletin.
But there’s still a niggling thought floating in the back of my mind.
“Do I really need a future?”
As a man who will lose the person he loves tomorrow, what does the future mean to me?
“Destroy me before I forget it all.”
How will I live on after tomorrow?
What worth is there in a world without her?
ATRI: Okay then…
ATRI: Time for bed.
ATRI takes off her clothes, and walks over to the bed.
Natsuki: …
After all of the night’s excitement, I’m particular nervous.
Natsuki: Yeah, it is…
ATRI: …
Natsuki: …
We can’t look each other in the eyes, but we can both feel the sense of expectation in the air.
Natsuki: (While she’s looking away, I’ll turn the pillow over to “YES”…)
Tonight, of all nights…
ATRI: Natsuki-san.

ATRI: …
Blushing bright red, she picks up the pillow.
Natsuki: (She’s not going to throw it outside again, is she!?)
ATRI: …
Natsuki: Hmm?

ATRI: …
Natsuki: Umm, what are you doing?

She starts whacking me over the head with it.

Natsuki: …”YES”
ATRI: Gahhh…
She stop, and clutches the pillow to herself.
She sits on the bed.
ATRI: I-I’m going to sleep. In this position, with my lap and my sides completely defenseless.
ATRI: Once I’m asleep, I’ll be absolutely oblivious to whatever you do to me, ahem…
ATRI: So, umm, sleepy time. Zzz… Zzz…
She lowers her head, and apparently falls asleep.
Natsuki: (Wow, really convincing acting. She’s holding out the “YES,” so I suppose it’s all right to hug her.)
I’d much prefer if she’d just throw her arms open and welcome me in like normal.
It’s really hard to come out and say it myself!
Natsuki: (No, dammit, Natsuki, you have to do it!)
She’s a young girl with emotions. That means she can feel embarrassed. I can’t just except her to cater to my every whim, can I?
Natsuki: (I have to take the lead!)
The bed creaks as I sit next to her.
ATRI: Eep!
ATRI twitches.
Natsuki: ATRI, are you asleep?

I wrap my arms around her like I did on that very first night.
ATRI: Aaahn!

ATRI: (Argh… I might have a limiter for a pain, but not embarrassment!)

That was bad acting even for me.
ATRI: Natsuki-san…
ATRI’s voice is full of nervous excitement.
Natsuki: You could stroke my hair all you wanted right now, zzz…
She starts to run her delicate fingers through it.
At first her touch is hesitant, but she soon starts to get more and more confident.
ATRI: Hehe, you’re so cute, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: Zzz… Zzz…
I’m too embarrassed to da anything but keep pretending to be asleep.
ATRI: Rub rub, stroke stroke…
Ahh, it feels so nice…
When she holds me like this, it’s like all of those nights I spent tortured by my phantom pain were nothing.
I want her to stay with me forever.
But I can’t tell her that, can I? It would only hurt her.
ATRI: Natsuki-san, are you asleep?
Natsuki: Zzz… Zzz…
ATRI: …
ATRI: Please… Don’t forget me.

Natsuki: Of course I won’t forget you.
ATRI: …Are you talking in your sleep?
Natsuki: Zzz… Zzz…
ATRI: Hehe, he’s even sweet when he’s asleep.
She stokes my hair again.
It feels so nice that I might really drift off after all.
But I don’t want this feeling to be cut even a second short.
Natsuki: (Even if I have to force myself… I’m staying awake…)
ATRI: Please, take me to Eden tomorrow.
Natsuki: …
ATRI: I want to see everyone smile.
ATRI: I want to make them happy. I want to know happiness myself. I want to be happy with them…
ATRI: I want to see the whole town bathed in light.
Natsuki: …Okay.
ATRI: I love you, Natsuki-san.
Soothed by the blissful feeling of her touch, I find myself slipping into a peaceful sleep…
The next morning…
ATRI: Brushy bryshy, brushy brushy…
Like we do every morning, we wake up and go through the exact same motions.
ATRI: Natshuki-shan… Aaaaahn.
She opens her mouth like a baby bird waiting to be fed.
As always, I stick her toothbrush in and brush her back teeth.
Natsuki: There you go.
ATRI: Mmnph, *spit*. Thank you.
I rinse my mouth and finish up too.
ATRI: The weather’s nice today. Perfect for drying the laundry!
Natsuki: Yeah, it’s really sunny.
I look out to the distant horizon, an enormous column of fluffy white cloud is the only blemish on an otherwise brilliantly blue sky.
ATRI: Here you go!
ATRI brings over a tray with my breakfast on it.

Natsuki: Don’t worry, I’ll keep that in the mind.
ATRI: Good, please do.
As always, our morning consists of a wonderful, nutritionally-balanced breakfast, the cleaning and the laundry. Afterwards, we start making the preparations to set sail for Eden.
ATRI: On yeah! Natsuki-san, do you know what this is?

“It would be a violation of our own humanity and in ignorance of yours to destroy you despite your possession of a soul.””But an animal that hurts a human gets put down. Robots are the same.””The only thing I can do for you is to give you a place far away from prying eyes.”

In exchange for giving up her autonomy and becoming one with Eden’s central control system, she was able to fall asleep with her memories of the world intact.

The mind of the first robot in the world able to feel emotions, ATRI.
