Everyone turns to me.
Natsuki: The sea rises will stop eventually. There’s only so much water on earth.
Natsuki: It won’t be enough to cover the land completely. Space isn’t our last hope.
That’s why my grandmother pushed forward with her plants for floating cities.
As I am now, I wouldn’t be able to continue her work. I need to learn and grow to truly understand Eden.
Ryuuji: …I see. I thought you were gonna say that.
Minamo: It’s going to be lonely without you…
Ririka: You’re really leaving?
Catherine: Of course he is. This brat’s wasted out here in the sticks.
Natsuki: I’ll be waiting for you there.
I pat Ririka’s head.
Ririka: I’ll keep studying and catch up to you in no time!
I turn to Ryuuji, Minamo, and all of the assemble students.
Natsuki: This place… This place has taught me so much, Even if I leave, it will always be my home.
I’m setting out on a journey into a new future… One without ATRI.
A journey that I hope will one day lead me back home.
I’ll fulfill my promise, and one day, finally, I will save her.
Bad End
Minamo slams into Yasuda’s side, and the stungun’s blast fires off into nothing.
Yasuda: Gah! You little bitch, don’t get in my way!
Minamo: Arrghh!
ATRI: Ah!
Yasuda’s metal arm slams into the side of Minamo’s head with a sickening crunch.
She collapses on the concrete, completely unmoving.
In that instant, ATRI feels something well up inside her, like raging flames turning her entire world red.
It burns inside her, a sensation she’s never felt before…
Minamo’s Voice: Nooooooooooo!
Natsuki: What!?
As I try to hobble my way to the roof, I hear a high-pitched, strained scream. It’s unmistakably Minamo.
Natsuki: No! Dammit, I have to get there!
I try to run, but I can’t with just my leg and my stick.
All I can do is hobble forward hardly faster than a normal walking pace.
If only I had a prosthetic, even some piece of junk…
Natsuki: (ATRI… ATRI!)
Screaming her name in my heart and praying for her safety, I fight my way up the stairs.
Natsuki: ATRI!
Heaving open the heavy steel door to the roof, my eyes are met with a truly horrendous sight.
ATRI: …
ATRI is standing there, expression completely blank.
Her clothes, and her fists, are soaked crimson red.
Sickly red liquid drips from her fingertips.
A man lies crumpled at her feet.
It seems like it might be the man I saw before, but his face is so distorted and blooded that I cannot be sure.
Minamo is lying completely still beside them.
Natsuki: ATRI…?
ATRI: Do not worry. Minamo is merely unconscious.
Her voice is cold, without a hint of emotion.
A chilling breeze whips around us, rustling her blood-stained skirt.
ATRI: I remember it now. Everything…
ATRI: I am a monster. Look…
She holds up her hands, fresh ichor glistening down her arms.
Natsuki: No, that’s not right. You’re…
ATRI: I will put an end to this myself.
She walks calmly to the edge of the roof.
Without a word, she climbs over the railing.
Natsuki: ATRI, no, what are you doing!?
ATR: I should have done this before.
Natsuki: No, stop-
ATRI: Goodbye.
Natsuki: ATRIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIII!!!
Time slows, and ATRI seems to float in the air. It’s like the sky itself is pulling her away from me. As she disappears, I see glimmer in those ruby-red eyes…
ATRI: Master, I have finished the laundry.
A torn-up scrap of fabric is hanging up to dry.
Until an hour ago, that was some kind of clothing.
ATRI: …
ATRI stares up at me, waiting for my appraisal.
She doesn’t even realize that she’s ruined it.
Natsuki: Great, thanks.
She nods stiffly.
When ATRI jumped from the roof, her motors and joints were heavily damaged.
They’re beyond the point of repair.
She suffered a lot of other injures, but nothing fatal. It’s lucky she fell into the water.
But her body is not what has taken the worst damage.
ATRI: I will prepare breakfast.
Natsuki: Okay…
She unsteadily totters back into the cabin, bare feet struggling to keep her balanced on the swaying deck.
She has forgotten everything.
Everything from before the day I salvaged her, and everything she experienced afterward.
I’m not quite sure if it’s a result of the damage she’s taken, or if she chose to erase her own memory.
Even showing her her logs does nothing. Her memories are gone, as are those emotions she used to show me every day.
To her, it’s as if we’ve never met before.
When I step back into the cabin, I’m greeted by the stench of charred carbon.
Natsuki: ATRI, is something burning?
ATRI: Hmm…?
She looks at me with confusion etched on her face.
Natsuki: …Forget I said that.
ATRI: Okay.
Waiting for my food, I stare at the calendar.
Not a single box has been crossed off since that day.
That doesn’t mean that her final days are not approaching, however.
ATRI: Breakfast is ready. Please sit down.
I sit on the sofa, waiting for her to bring over my tray.
Natsuki: …Huh?
There’s something underneath my foot.
I look down. There’s a shoe.
A single, beaten-up old loafer.
I remember instantly where the other is. She was wearing it when she plunged into the sea.
Natsuki: …
ATRI: Oh…
When ATRI sees the shoe, she stops in her tracks.
Natsuki: Do you remember this? This is your…
ATRI: Is that garbage? It is trash collection day, so I will throw it away.
She swiftly takes the shoe from my hand, and disposes of it.
She turns back to me as if nothing has happened.
ATRI: Please enjoy breakfast.
Natsuki: …Thanks.
I force the blackened, obliterated matter down my throat with a heavy gulp of water. While I struggle, ATRI goes to throw out the trash.
The ashen taste coats the inside of my mouth.
If I’d just been faster.
If I could have ran…
I chew. And I gulp. And I chew. And I gulp. And I chew and gulp and chew and gulp…
Natsuki: Huh…?
After some moments, I hear ATRI walking back to the ship. There’s something different about her footsteps.
Or, half of them, at least.
Natsuki: ATRI… Is that, umm…?
She’s wearing a shoe on one foot.
ATRI: This shoe appears to still be functional. I adjust it to be of adequate use for protecting my foot.
ATRI: Would this be acceptable to you?
Natsuki: Yeah…
ATRI gazes down at her feet with her dull, blood-red eyes.
ATRI: It is the perfect size…
Natsuki: It really suits you.
ATRI: …Understand.
She nods impassively, and starts to turn away to return to her duties.
Suddenly, she stops.
Natsuki: Hmm? What’s up?
ATRI: Am I helpful?
Natsuki: Of course you are. You’re a lifesaver.
ATRI: I see. Excellent.
Two days later, ATRI ceased to function.
She died remembering nothing.
True End
It has been sixty years since humanity took its first steps back toward the stars.
The sea rises threw our way of life into flux. Yet even as civilization has been faced with greater and greater challenges, we have pushed on without our spirit ever breaking.
Maybe it was that shing line in the sky that showed us the way through an uncertain future.
As long as there is a light to walk toward, people can follow it.
It was thirty years ago now that the first new floating city, Noah, was completed.
Noahs 2 and 3 followed on shortly afterward, and now approximately a quarter of humanity lives on self-sustaining artificial islands.
I, Kamishiro Natsuki, am one of them.
My research has delved into various fields throughout my life in academia.
One of those fields, research into floating cities, was the continuation of my grandmother’s work.
Another, the further development of A.I.
Kokoro: Master, should I change your diaper?
Natsuki: There’s no need for that… She’ll do that for me…
Lying on what I know is destined to be my deathbed, I can hardly speak in more than a whisper.
Natsuki’s Wife: Honestly, dear, I’m not doing that. That’s what we bought the robot to do.
“The Lost Decades”-that’s how historians refer to the twenty years across which the sea levels rose dramatically.
Most of earth’s land mass was swallowed by the ocean, and much of our technology and prosperity vanished into the deep.
Then followed another decade of despair as humanity simply clung on to existence.
The Academy was established amid the chaos with a noble objective in mind:
“To keep open the paths to humanity’s future.”
It’s academics would strive to relearn our lost knowledge, further developing it to be put to practical use.
I gave myself the objective of rebuilding the science of robotics, and finding applications for it in humanity’s future.
It was my research, in fact, that lead to the singularity.
Our civilization was totally turned on its head by the technological revolution that began when humanoids reached the point where they were not simply workers in our society, but our friends too.
There are still philosophical debates as to whether robots truly possess souls, but regardless, the near-miraculous speed at which their capabilities increased played a crucial role in saving humanity.
I don’t doubt that I will be remembered in history as one of the fathers of the A.I. age.
It is what the world will read in my obituary tomorrow.
Natsuki: …
Kokoro: Master, what is that song?
I start to hum of familiar tune in my weak, exhausted voice. My maid, Kokoro, looks at me with soft bemusement.
Natsuki’s Wife: It’s a song an old friend of ours used to sing. Ahh, you haven’t sung that in years…
Natsuki: I remember we used to have this second-hand piano someone had donated to our dilapidated old school.
Natsuki’s Wife: My darling would play, and our friend would sing…
Kokoro: That sounds very sweet, but I must say you’re not the best of singers.
Natsuki: Well, sorry that this dying man’s not quite Pavarotti, toaster…
Kokoro: That is anti-robot discrimination. Please rescind those words.
Natsuki: Shut up…
Natsuki’s Wife: Hehe, this sure takes me back…
That school where I spent such a brief but precious time, and the whole town surrounding it, are now at the bottom of the sea.
Catherine continued teaching there until the very last.
Thanks to her efforts, that tiny school was able to produce three Academy students.
The first of them was Nanami Ririka, the nuclear scientist responsible for perfecting the world’s first small-scale fusion reactor.
My old friend Nojima Ryuuji took advantage of his popularity and leadership to become the first mayor of Noah, and supported Ririka’s research financially.
A petal comes floating in through the open window.
There are many out there who decry humanity’s current circumstance as ‘unnatural.’
This petal too is from a tree that has been genetically modified to be perfectly suited to our current climate.
I can understand those who think it’s somehow horrific for humanity to have such control over nature.
But what other choice do we have? The only other option was to accept our end.
If those people want to give up, then they can die alone.
Our civilization has taken its first steps into space. Manned missions to Mars are soon to begin, launched from the staging post to the moon.
It may be decades, or even longer, before we are able to turn Mars into a new home for humanity, but one day I am sure we will be able to control other planets the way we do our own.
Of course, you can still debate the morality of that.
But we won’t give up on our future.
Natsuki: Dear… Turn the TV on…
Natsuki’ Wife: TV on.
At her command, a hologram window opens up before me.
My voice is too weak to even be picked up by the A.I. now.
Natsuki: I invented the damn thing, and it won’t even listen to me…
Natsuki’s Wife: You never know what kind of problems old age is going to bring until you actually get old, right?
News Reporter: The final preparations have been made for the decommissioning of the floating island, Eden.
News Reporter: The pioneering engineering project that set the stage for the development of all of our current seasteading projects stopped being used as a research station several years ago.
New Reporter: With concerns about its structural integrity preventing its reuse as a residential facility, the island will be scuttled to be used as a wreck diving site tomorrow.
Natsuki: …
Natsuki’s Wife: Ah, that takes me back…
She sighs deeply.
Natsuki’s Wife: I wonder if she’s still there…
Natsuki: …
My wife looks at me with a gentle smile as I stare at the picture on the television.
Natsuki: Minamo… Thank you for being by my side, all these years.
Natsuki’s Wife: …
She blushes a little. We’re so used to calling each other by little pet names that it feels like it’s been decades since I used that name.
She pouts and frowns at me.
Natsuki’s Wife: It’s not fair, springing that on me all of a sudden…
Natsuki: Well… This is the end, after all…
Natsuki: Don’t worry. Do what you have to do. I know that you’ve never forgotten her.
Natsuki’s Wife: It’ll make me happy, too. You weren’t the only person who loved her.
Natsuki: Thank you…
Natsuki: So you’re really going to meet her…
Natsuki: Yes… I promised her… one last day…
My health has been deteriorating for several years now. The doctors said I could die at any time.
I could have had all manner of cyborg implants to prolong my life, but I have lived long enough already.
I have only kept going as long as I have so that I could see this moment.
Natsuki: Kokoro… Connect me to the network…
Kokoro: Yes, master.
I feel information rush into my brain.
It’s been partially cyborgized, allowing me to connect my consciousness to the internet.
The technology is still experimental. It may be some years before it becomes widespread in society.
Kokoro: Diving in ten, nine, eight, seven…
Natsuki: I’ll be back…
Natsuki’s Wife: See you later, Natsu-kun. Say hello to ATRI-chan for me.
A petal flutters in through the open window-
My consciousness floats out of my body, and sinks deep into the inky black of the electronic ocean…
…
Soon, I am within Eden.
The place where our future began.
It has now served its purpose. It cannot escape the ravages of age.
It’s hydroelectric power system just can’t compete with nuclear fusion in terms of efficiency.
Its computer systems are outdated technology, too expensive to keep updating.
Its life coming to an end, it will sink to the bottom of the sea.
The public doesn’t know that this place can be said to be where the singularity all started.
No one knows that the very first robot with a soul sleeps here.
Natsuki: (ATRI…)
I call her name, and feel a ripple in the electronic ocean.
The waves stir softly around me.
ATRI has become one with these waters.
It is impossible to say where her consciousness begins and Eden’s systems end.
She has melted into it like sugar into tea.
These waters as a whole are both ATRI, and not ATRI.
Natsuki: (ATRI…!)
I shout for her, and waves call back.
I sink into the deepest depths of the sea of information.
I have to save her from drowning in these waters.
I will salvage every scrap of ATRI’s being.
Every single one.
Even if I find them all, I know that it won’t bring her back.
It’s nothing but fragments of her mind.
At the  bottom of the digital sea is a town.
Natsuki: (I can’t tell if these are my memories, or ATRI’s…)
They are probably mine.
I am forming my own image of the electronic ocean to make it easier for my mind to process.
I have to walk on.
I suddenly find myself in the cockpit of the Serpens Albus.
Natsuki: (There’s the storehouse… ATRI must be in there.)
I pilot the sub inside.
I wave the light across the room, searching for her.
Natsuki: (ATRI… Where are you? ATRI…)
She may be one with these waters now, but if she really does possess a consciousness, that alone should still remain somewhere.
A consciousness cannot simply disappear. It is the ultimate proof that an individual exists.
I’m sure that she’s here somewhere, sleeping in this sea of information.
Natsuki: (ATRI… You’re here, aren’t you?)
There in the dark, I finally see a glimmer of light.
Natsuki: (You’re here…)
There, in that coffinlike capsule.
There, she sleeps.
Natsuki: (I knew you had a consciousness… A soul…)
So this is what it feels like to be inside the singularity itself…
Natsuki: (ATRI… Wake up, ATRI…!)
…
She does not respond.
I thought that if I at least found her consciousness, that could be the key to waking her up.
But it seems like that won’t be enough. There’s one thing missing.
One thing I have.
Natsuki: Remember, ATRI… All those dear moments…
I hold our to her three notebooks, notebooks that I have kept safe all these years… Those three logs that record every moment from her birth to her final sleep.
…
Her eyes open.
She stares at me with those ruby-red pools of light.
ATRI: …
Natsuki: (You’re alive…)
She’s really still here.
She gazes at me quizzically, and tilts her head to the side. It’s just like she always used to do.
ATRI: Who are you…?
Natsuki: (Have you forgotten me?)
A Humanoid always remembers its master…
ATRI: …Natsuki-san.
She reaches out, and opens the capsule.
The soft sound of ocean waves fills my ears.
Before me stretches out that familiar landscape.
Natsuki: This place…
ATRI: It would be a little hard to talk underwater, wouldn’t it?
Natsuki: Oh…
Natsuki: We’re back in that time…
ATRI: Would you have preferred to stay an old man?
Natsuki: No, I like this. It wouldn’t be fair if you were the only one who looked the same as in the past.
ATRI: Don’t blame me for that. I was made to look like this.
She looks up at me with a playful smile, that little tuft of hair on her head bouncing up and down.
ATRI: Welcome back, Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: It’s good to be home.
Finally, I get to hear those words.
The words I’ve been waiting decades for.
ATRI: Did you manage to save the world?
Natsuki: You already know the answer to that. You’ve been watching me, haven’t you?
ATRI: Yes, I’ve been watching from Eden. Watching the world, and you Natsuki-san.
Natsuki: I’ve planted the seeds. It’s up to the next generation to grow them.
Natsuki: My work is done. I’m tired, and I need to rest.
ATRI: Just like me, in fact.
Tomorrow, she’ll be sunk to the bottom of the sea.
Natsuki: I promised that I’d spend one last day with you, didn’t I?
ATRI: That you did. ♪
Natsuki: With our minds connected directly to the internet like this, our perception of the flow to time might be a little different to how it would be in the normal world though.
ATRI: Oh, how much? Enough to make one day last, say, sixty years?
Natsuki: Heh, it’s going to be along day.
Thankfully, we’ve got plenty of lost time to make up for.
ATRI: Hey! What’s with that leg!? Are you cheating on me!?
Natsuki: C-Calm down…
ATRI glares at my prosthetic leg.
It’s the same kind that I’ve been using all my life until today.
I’ve always preferred an older, non-cybernetic type.
My unconscious must have recreated in this realm.
ATRI: Tsk, you’ve had sixty years to upgrade, and you’ re still using a piece of junk like thar?
Natsuki: Well, I couldn’t find a leg that matched up to you.
ATRI: Heh, of course you couldn’t! I’m just that high performance!
She puffs up her chest proudly.
I probably shouldn’t tell her that there’s a lot of things in the world a little more “high performance” than her now, particularly when it comes to cybernetics.
Yet I always wanted to keep using an older, less technologically-advanced leg. It reminds me of my own flaws.
The flaws that I’m always depending on other people to help me with.
Natsuki: I was always so proud and stubborn… But it’s only by knowing your own weaknesses that you can work with others.
There’s another reason I kept using an old leg, too-so that I’d always want to go back to find ATRI again.
Natsuki: You haven’t been bored down here, have you?
ATRI: No, I’ve been sleeping the whole time.
ATRI: I did have a nice dream, though. I dreamt that you married Minamo.
ATRI: You were surrounded by children and grandchildren. You looked so happy.
ATRI: …I was a little jealous.
Natsuki: She left me go to spend my final day with you, though. She says hello.
No one will know what happens here today.
We are all alone on Eden. No one is permitted on a condemned island like this.
I’ve planned for this for so many years. Minamo was the only person I could ever tell about it.
ATRI: Won’t you be in trouble if people find out you’ve done this?
Natsuki: Don’t worry. All of the physical evidence will be sealed away.
ATRI: I’ll make sure there’s no digital evidence on Eden’s network, either.
Natsuki: Thanks.
Natsuki: I’ve spent my whole life working toward this. I want to spend my last day relaxing.
ATRI: That sound lovely. I’ll accompany you.
She holds out her hand.
I entwine my fingers with hers.
“Time is a cruel thief to rob us of our former selves. We lose as much to life as we do to death.”
So much time has passed since that last moment we spent together. It has given me so many wonderful things, and taken just as much.
But maybe, after all we’ve been through, it will let us have one day to ourselves.
ATRI: What are we going to do first, Natsuki-san?
Natsuki: I think… I’d like to sleep with you in my arms.
ATRI: Hehe, you haven’t changed. You’re still the same spoiled little kid.
Our long summer is finally ending.
We have one last day.
One last day for the robot who had a heart, and the boy who loved her.
